== 2000s ==

=== 2000 ===
* On January 10, approximately 100 barrels of jet fuel were discharged from [[Plantation Pipeline]] in [[Newington, Virginia]], some of which entered into [[Accotink Creek]] and its adjoining shorelines. The failure resulted from a failed gasket on an interface detector.<ref name="epa.gov">{{cite web|url=http://www.epa.gov/compliance/resources/decrees/civil/cwa/plantationpipeline-cd.pdf |title=UNITED STATES OF AMERICA, and STATE OF NORTH CAROLINA, Plaintiffs, v. PLANTATION PIPE LINE COMPANY, Civil Action No. 3:08-cv-500 |accessdate=June 14, 2012 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028061446/http://www.epa.gov/compliance/resources/decrees/civil/cwa/plantationpipeline-cd.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 |df= }}</ref>
* On January 21, a [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] pipeline leaked from a welding flaw near [[Corinne, Utah]], spilling about 100 barrels of Diesel fuel. The product spread over 38 acres of salt flat and wetlands used by birds. About 75% to 80% of the spill was intentionally burned to eliminate it.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://ioscproceedings.org/doi/pdf/10.7901/2169-3358-2003-1-109 |title=Use of In Situ Burning at a Diesel Spill in Wetlands and Salt Flats, Northern Utah, U.S.A: Remediation Operations and 1.5 Years of Post-Burn Monitoring |publisher= |date= |accessdate=April 12, 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270220 |title=Jan. 21, 2000 – ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=January 21, 2000 |accessdate=April 12, 2014 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131103090300/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270220 |archivedate=November 3, 2013 }}</ref>
* On January 21, an Equilon Pipeline Co. crude oil line was ruptured off of the [[Louisiana]] coast, by an eight-ton anchor dropped by a ship. About 94,000 gallons of crude oil were spilled, creating a slick 2 miles wide by 7 miles long.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270221 |title=Jan. 21, 2000 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020202700/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270221 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1980&dat=20000123&id=sIQiAAAAIBAJ&sjid=uqkFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4460,5282202|title=The Item – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On January 27, in [[Winchester, Kentucky]], a [[Marathon Oil]] pipeline accident released about {{convert|490,000|USgal|L}} of crude oil. NTSB investigators found a dent on the bottom of the pipe in the rupture area. Marathon spent about $7.1&nbsp;million in response to the accident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAB0102.aspx |title=Pipeline Accident Brief PAB-01-02 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150922142401/http://ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAB0102.aspx |archivedate=September 22, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Letter to Ms. Daragh Porter |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220005011H/220005011H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_10172000.pdf |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028021928/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220005011H/220005011H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_10172000.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 |df= }}</ref>
* On February 5, a pipeline failed and spilled over {{convert|192,000|USgal|L}} of crude oil in the [[John Heinz National Wildlife Refuge]] in Pennsylvania. The source of the spill was a break in a miter bend in the pipe, which was estimated to be at least 50 years old.<ref>{{cite web|author=Ron Rothschadl |url=http://www.fws.gov/northeast/SUNOCO/index.html |title=SUNOCO Oil Spill Settlement |publisher=Fws.gov |date=August 3, 2005 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121111115125/http://www.fws.gov/northeast/SUNOCO/index.html |archivedate=November 11, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|author= |url=http://www.incidentnews.gov/incident/7466 |title=IncidentNews: Sun Oil Pipeline |publisher=Incidentnews.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120314025707/http://www.incidentnews.gov/incident/7466 |archivedate=March 14, 2012 }}</ref>
* On March 9, an Explorer petroleum products pipeline failed in [[Greenville, Texas]]. The 28-inch pipeline ruptured and released {{convert|13436|oilbbl|m3}} of gasoline. The released gasoline eventually reached East Caddo Creek. The banks of the tributary and creek contained the escaping gasoline as it flowed away from the ruptured pipe. The probable cause of the pipeline failure was corrosion-fatigue cracking that initiated at the edge of the longitudinal seam weld at a likely preexisting weld defect. Contributing to the failure was the loss of pipe coating integrity.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB0103.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=March 9, 2000 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB0103.pdf |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 7, a pipeline released fuel oil at Chalk Point near [[Aquasco, Maryland]]. The Piney Point Oil Pipeline system, which was owned by the Potomac Electric Power Company (Pepco), experienced a pipe failure at the [[Chalk Point Generating Station]] in southeastern [[Prince George's County, Maryland]]. The release was not discovered and addressed by the contract operating company, Support Terminal Services, Inc., until the late afternoon. Approximately {{convert|140,400|USgal|L}} of fuel oil were released into the surrounding wetlands and Swanson Creek and, subsequently, the [[Patuxent River]] as a result of the accident. No injuries were caused by the accident, which cost approximately $71&nbsp;million for environmental response and clean-up operations.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR0201.aspx |title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-02-01 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150922142532/http://ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR0201.aspx |archivedate=September 22, 2015 }}</ref>
* On May 19, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] Co. line failed near [[Greensboro, North Carolina]]. At least 714 gallons (17 barrels) of kerosene spilled, some of which entered a pond that flows into a tributary of the East Fork Deep River. The kerosene spill caused a sheen about 40 feet by 40 feet in the pond. As a result of this, and six other previous [[Colonial Pipeline]] accidents, the EPA fined Colonial $34&nbsp;million in 2003.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.epa.gov/compliance/resources/cases/civil/cwa/colonial.html |title=Settlement: Colonial Pipeline Company Clean Water Act Settlement &#124; Civil Enforcement &#124; Compliance and Enforcement &#124; US EPA |publisher=Epa.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028062657/http://www.epa.gov/compliance/resources/cases/civil/cwa/colonial.html |archivedate=October 28, 2013}}</ref>
* On June 7, a stopple fitting weld failed on a Wolverine Pipeline Company line, causing a rupture releasing {{convert|75,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline into the environment, and causing the evacuation of more than 500 houses in [[Blackman Charter Township, Michigan]]. The failure caused the shutdown of 30% of Michigan's gasoline supplies for nine days, contaminated a creek which flows into the Grand River, and a railroad track near the failure site was shut down for a week. Later tests found 715 anomalies in this pipeline. Wolverine later agreed to pay for switching houses in the area from local water wells to a city water source.<ref>{{cite web
 |title=Letter to Mr. Robert C. Luckner, President Wolverine Pipe Line Company 
 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320025001H/320025001H_CAO_02252002.pdf 
 |accessdate=October 30, 2016 
 |deadurl=yes 
 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20100527154052/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320025001H/320025001H_CAO_02252002.pdf 
 |archivedate=May 27, 2010 
 |df= 
}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1988&dat=20000823&id=EIYyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=m6wFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4189,4370256|title=The Argus-Press – Google News Archive Search |accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On July 5, two boats hit a [[Southern Natural Gas]] pipeline off the coast of [[Plaquemines, Louisiana]], causing a gas fire that burned five members of the boat crews. The fire could be seen at 35 miles away from it.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1955&dat=20000706&id=Qg0iAAAAIBAJ&sjid=R6YFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4769,2708179|title=Reading Eagle – Google News Archive Search |accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270349 |title=July 5, 2000 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020202958/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270349 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* On August 19, a 30-inch diameter [[El Paso Natural Gas]] pipeline rupture and fire near [[Carlsbad, New Mexico]] killed 12 members of an extended family camping over {{convert|600|ft|m}} from the rupture point. The force of the escaping gas created a {{convert|51|ft|m|adj=on}}-wide crater about {{convert|113|ft|m}} along the pipe. A {{convert|49|ft|m|adj=on}} section of the pipe was ejected from the crater, in three pieces measuring approximately {{convert|3|ft|m}}, {{convert|20|ft|m}}, and {{convert|26|ft|m}} in length. The largest piece of pipe was found about {{convert|287|ft|m}} northwest of the crater. The cause of the failure was determined to be severe internal corrosion of that pipeline. On July 26, 2007, a USDOJ Consent Decree was later entered into by the pipeline owner to perform pipeline system upgrades to allow better internal pipeline inspections.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR0301.aspx |title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-03-01 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date=August 19, 2000 |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150908011132/http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR0301.aspx |archivedate=September 8, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.justice.gov/enrd/4431.htm |title=USDOJ: Environment and Natural Resources Division : U.S. v. El Paso Natural Gas Co |publisher=Justice.gov |date=July 26, 2007 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130414054257/http://www.justice.gov/enrd/4431.htm |archivedate=April 14, 2013}}</ref>
* On August 20, a gas pipeline exploded and burned in [[Concord, North Carolina]]. A nearby shopping mall was evacuated, but, there were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1314&dat=20000821&id=S9AzAAAAIBAJ&sjid=QvIDAAAAIBAJ&pg=6915,22149|title=The Spokesman-Review – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On August 24, a 6-inch pipeline operated by [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] failed from alleged external corrosion, spilling 126,000 gallons of crude oil into an unnamed creek, near [[Snyder, Texas]]. The creek was dry at the time. Later, a Federal Court ruled that the [[Clean Water Act]] did not apply, since there was no water flowing in the creek at the time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cleanwaterfund.org/feature/when-lake-not-lake-when-river-not-river |title=When is a lake not a lake? When is a river not a river? – Clean Water Fund |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150101171011/http://www.cleanwaterfund.org/feature/when-lake-not-lake-when-river-not-river |archivedate=January 1, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=UNITED STATES OF AMERICA, Plaintiff, v. CHEVRON PIPE LINE COMPANY, Defendant. Civil Action No. 5:05-CV-293-C ECF |url=http://rapanos.typepad.com/chevron.pdf |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20061115133859/http://rapanos.typepad.com/chevron.pdf |archivedate=November 15, 2006}}</ref>
* On September 7, a bulldozer ruptured a 12-inch diameter NGL pipeline on State Route 36 south of [[Abilene, Texas]]. An Abilene police detective, with 21 years of service, was severely burned when the vapors ignited, and he later died. Nearby, a woman saved herself by going underwater in her swimming pool. Her house was destroyed by the explosion and fire. The owner of the pipeline, ExxonMobil, was later fined by the Texas Railroad Commission for the pipeline not being marked.<ref>{{cite web| url=http://www.statesman.com/specialreports/content/specialreports/pipelines/24pipeabilene.html | publisher= The American Statesman| archiveurl=
https://web.archive.org/web/20030707103612/http://www.statesman.com/specialreports/content/specialreports/pipelines/24pipeabilene.html | archivedate= July 7, 2003| title= Digs gone awry: a top cause of tragedy | date= July 24, 2001 | first1=Ralph K.M.|last1= Haurwitz |first2=Jeff| last2= Nesmith| accessdate=April 2, 2013| location= Austin, Texas}} {{dead link|date=April 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|first=Brian |last=Williams |url=http://lubbockonline.com/stories/090800/loc_090800083.shtml |title=Abilene pipeline blast injures two |publisher=Lubbock Avalanche-Journal |date=September 8, 2000 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121003203006/http://lubbockonline.com/stories/090800/loc_090800083.shtml |archivedate=October 3, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|agency=Associated Press |url=http://lubbockonline.com/stories/110701/bus_1107010007.shtml |title=Exxon Mobil ordered to pay for pipeline blast |publisher=Lubbock Avalanche-Journal |date=November 7, 2001 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121004183825/http://lubbockonline.com/stories/110701/bus_1107010007.shtml |archivedate=October 4, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=20000921&id=10JTAAAAIBAJ&sjid=UYUDAAAAIBAJ&pg=5753,5009624|title=The Victoria Advocate – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On November 3, a front end loader punctured an 8-inch pipeline carrying Diesel fuel in [[Lancaster County, Pennsylvania]]. Diesel fuel sprayed {{convert|40|ft|m}} into the air. The fuel flowed for over 2 hours before stopping, and contaminating the area with more than {{convert|40,000|USgal|L}} of Diesel fuel.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.fireengineering.com/index/articles/display/101600/articles/fire-engineering/volume-154/issue-4/features/pipeline-rupture-a-case-study.html |title=Pipeline Rupture: A Case Study |publisher=Fire Engineering |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110718201416/http://www.fireengineering.com/index/articles/display/101600/articles/fire-engineering/volume-154/issue-4/features/pipeline-rupture-a-case-study.html |archivedate=July 18, 2011 }}</ref>

=== 2001 ===
* On January 17 and 18, a series of gas explosion hit downtown [[Hutchinson, Kansas]], resulting in 2 deaths, and 2 buildings being destroyed. Later, it was discovered that gas was leaking from an underground gas storage cavern in the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=20020221&id=5kYyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=FucFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6783,985626|title=Lawrence Journal-World – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1291&dat=20010121&id=tFFUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=jY4DAAAAIBAJ&pg=6595,4592237|title=Boca Raton News – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On April 1, a Dome Pipeline in North Dakota carrying gasoline ruptured and burst into flames a few miles west of [[Bottineau, North Dakota]]. An estimated {{convert|1.1|e6USgal|m3}} of gasoline burned before the pipeline could be shut down. The company attributed the break to damage by an "outside force", which A Bottineau County Sheriff said appeared to be frost that melted at uneven rates, twisting and breaking the pipeline.<ref name="nwf">{{cite web |title=Fuel Oil Incident List |url=http://www.nwf.org/News-and-Magazines/Media-Center/News-by-Topic/Global-Warming/2010/~/media/PDFs/Global%20Warming/Reports/Full-Oil-Incident-List.ashx |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20100803143750/http://www.nwf.org/News-and-Magazines/Media-Center/News-by-Topic/Global-Warming/2010/~/media/PDFs/Global%20Warming/Reports/Full-Oil-Incident-List.ashx |archivedate=August 3, 2010}}</ref>
* On April 14, a 6-inch petroleum productions failed near [[Harwood, North Dakota]], spilling 40 barrels of fuel oil. There were no injuries. The failure was due to an [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam failure, with this particular pipeline having had other ERW seam failures in the past in 1987 and 1993.<ref>{{cite web|title=NOTICE OF PROPOSED CORRECTWE ACTION ORDER |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320015015H/320015015H_CAO_06222001.pdf |website=primis.phmsa.dot.gov |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028014558/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320015015H/320015015H_CAO_06222001.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On May 1, a MAPCO 10-inch propane pipeline exploded and burned, in [[Platte County, Missouri]]. 13,500 barrels of propane were burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270584 |title=May 1, 2001 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140714124934/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270584 |archivedate=July 14, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=KC&p_theme=kc&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0EC04EE4B5FAC828&p_field_direct-0=document_id&p_perpage=10&p_sort=YMD_date:D&s_trackval=GooglePM |title=Big blast, but no injuries Pipeline explodes in Platte County field |accessdate=July 18, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=20010501&id=UYAyAAAAIBAJ&sjid=n-YFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6661,996898|title=Lawrence Journal-World – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On May 24 bulldozer being used in [[Taylor County, Texas]] hit a petroleum pipeline, causing a large petroleum fire. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.texnews.com/1998/2001/local/oil0526.html |title=Local News – Potosi oil pipeline blaze doused, but dispute smolders |publisher=Texnews.com |date=May 26, 2001 |accessdate=February 14, 2014 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028010955/http://www.texnews.com/1998/2001/local/oil0526.html |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On June 13, in [[Pensacola, Florida]], at least ten persons were injured when two natural gas lines ruptured and exploded after a parking lot gave way beneath a cement truck at a car dealership. The blast sent chunks of concrete flying across a four-lane road, and several employees and customers at neighboring businesses were evacuated. About 25 cars at the dealership and ten boats at a neighboring business were damaged or destroyed.
* On July 24, a pipeline ruptured and spread burning gasoline near [[Manheim, Pennsylvania]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.hazmat2-9.com/gas.html |title=Gasoline Pipeline Explosion |publisher=Hazmat2-9.com |date=July 24, 2001 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027233752/http://www.hazmat2-9.com/gas.html |archivedate=October 27, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=KLQvAAAAIBAJ&sjid=FNsFAAAAIBAJ&pg=1336,6127433&dq=mobil+pipeline+leak&hl=en|title=Beaver County Times – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On August 11, at approximately 5:05&nbsp;a.m. MST, an [[El Paso Natural Gas]] 24-inch gas transmission pipeline failed near [[Williams, Arizona]], resulting in the release of natural gas. The natural gas continued to discharge for about an hour before igniting. [[Stress corrosion cracking]] was determined to be the cause of the failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.ebdc7a8a7e39f2e55cf2031050248a0c/?vgnextoid=18d135199448d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=663fc02b8be2d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print |title=PHMSA – Southwest – CPF 4-2001-1005-H |publisher=Phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130317112938/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.ebdc7a8a7e39f2e55cf2031050248a0c/?vgnextoid=18d135199448d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=663fc02b8be2d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print |archivedate=March 17, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420011005H/420011005H.pdf |title=Nov 25, 2003 – RESEARCH AND SPECIAL PROGRAMS ADMINISTRATION |accessdate=November 27, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170209173432/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420011005H/420011005H.pdf |archivedate=February 9, 2017 }}</ref>
* On August 12, a bulldozer hit a 14-inch LP gas pipeline near [[Weatherford, Texas]], causing a massive fire. One person was injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1988&dat=20010814&id=Bk4iAAAAIBAJ&sjid=W6wFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6260,3648661|title=The Argus-Press – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270649 |title=Aug. 12, 2001 – ProPublica |publisher=Projects.propublica.org |date=August 12, 2001 |accessdate=February 14, 2014 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131220095154/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270649 |archivedate=December 20, 2013 }}</ref>
* On August 17, an Oklahoma crude oil pipeline ruptured after being struck by a machine cleaning roadside ditches, sending oil {{convert|30|ft|m}} into the air and damaging nearby cotton crops with up to {{convert|150,000|USgal|L}} spilled.<ref name="ukopa.co.uk">{{cite web |title=WORLDWIDE PIPELINE INCIDENTS – APRIL 2002 |url=http://www.ukopa.co.uk/publications/pdf/020035.pdf |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20080517110500/http://www.ukopa.co.uk/publications/pdf/020035.pdf |archivedate=May 17, 2008}}</ref>
* On September 3, at approximately 1&nbsp;p.m. CST, a rupture occurred near the intersection of the 22-inch T-ML Pipeline and the Black Bayou in Louisiana, resulting in the release of an estimated 8.00&nbsp;mmcf to 13.00&nbsp;mmcf of natural gas. In addition, the liquids loss is estimated to be 15,000 gallons.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.6f23687cf7b00b0f22e4c6962d9c8789/?vgnextoid=694f35199448d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=663fc02b8be2d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print |title=PHMSA – Southwest – CPF 4-2001-1006-H |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022130413/http://phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.6f23687cf7b00b0f22e4c6962d9c8789/?vgnextoid=694f35199448d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=663fc02b8be2d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref>
* On October 4, a drunken man used a rifle to shoot a hole in the Alaskan Pipeline. More than 285,000 gallons of crude oil were spilled, costing more $13&nbsp;million to clean up. The man was later convicted and sentenced to 16 years in prison.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=XEcvAAAAIBAJ&sjid=PE8DAAAAIBAJ&pg=5341,4248853&dq=pipeline+spill&hl=en|title=Ludington Daily News – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|title=Pipeline shooter draws 16-year sentence |work=Peninsula Clarion |date=June 8, 2003 |url=http://peninsulaclarion.com/stories/060803/ala_060803ala011001.shtml#.WIfvv_l95PY |accessdate=25 January 2017 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170202034551/http://peninsulaclarion.com/stories/060803/ala_060803ala011001.shtml |archivedate=February 2, 2017 }}</ref>
* On October 15, a 6-inch [[ConocoPhillips]] LPG pipeline failed near [[Sweeny, Texas]], forcing 2&nbsp;dozen residents to evacuate. About 195,000 gallons of LPG were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=20011017&id=OltTAAAAIBAJ&sjid=X4UDAAAAIBAJ&pg=2359,3951715|title=The Victoria Advocate – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270683 |title=Oct. 15, 2001 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140714182412/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270683 |archivedate=July 14, 2014 }}</ref>
* On or about November 27, approximately 2,575 barrels of Jet A Kerosene (Jet Fuel) discharged from the P-62 pipeline of the TEPPCO Pipeline System into tributaries of the [[Neches River]] and the Neches River itself. The release occurred 4 miles southeast of [[Vidor, Texas]]. This spill was caused by disbonded coating and external corrosion on the pipeline. This incident was later part of a U.S. [[Environmental Protection Agency]] consent decree.<ref name="www2.epa.gov">{{cite web|url=http://www2.epa.gov/sites/production/files/2013-09/documents/teppco-cd.pdf |format=PDF |title=United States v TE Products Pipeline Company |website=Epa.gov |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304095159/http://www.epa.gov/sites/production/files/2013-09/documents/teppco-cd.pdf |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On December 14, an anhydrous ammonia spill near [[Algona, Iowa]] killed nearly 1.3&nbsp;million fish, the largest [[fish kill]] on that state's record-to-date, Iowa state officials said. More than {{convert|58,000|USgal|L}} of anhydrous ammonia over a nine-hour period spilled into Lotts Creek and the [[Des Moines River]], killing minnows, bass and other game fish. [[Koch Industries]] owned the 8-inch pipeline, and was doing maintenance work on a valve on the pipeline. The plume drifted over a six-mile (10&nbsp;km) area causing officials to evacuate residents in its path.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2150&dat=20030925&id=iJ9kAAAAIBAJ&sjid=IYUNAAAAIBAJ&pg=973,2865006|title=The Danish Villages Voice – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>

=== 2002 ===
* On February 8, a trenching machine with a new rock bit being tested hit a 20-inch gas transmission pipeline in [[Noble County, Oklahoma]], causing an explosion that killed the trencher operator.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://dms.ntsb.gov/pubdms/search/document.cfm?docID=292679&docketID=38133&mkey=59739 |title=Document 1 Oklahoma Corporation Commission Pipeline Failure Investigation Report (manually redacted) Filing Date April 17, 2008 13 page(s) of Text (PDF) Photos |publisher=Dms.ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://dms.ntsb.gov/pubdms/search/document.cfm?docID=292679&docketID=38133&mkey=59739 |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 6, an explosion and a massive fire hit a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] natural gas substation near [[Mount Sterling, Kentucky]]. 30 families in the area voluntarily evacuated. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1842&dat=20020305&id=YmoeAAAAIBAJ&sjid=W8kEAAAAIBAJ&pg=1838,896318|title=Times Daily – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270790 |title=March 6, 2002 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020202843/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270790 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* On March 13, a Buckeye Partners pipeline ruptured due to internal corrosion in [[Wren, Ohio]], spilling about 1500 gallons of gasoline.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1350&dat=20020314&id=6VhPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=xwMEAAAAIBAJ&pg=6258,3728992|title=Toledo Blade – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On or about March 13, approximately 20 barrels of oil or [[jet fuel]] were discharged from a portion of the Plantation Pipeline in [[Alexandria, Virginia]], some of which entered into an unnamed tributary of Hooff Run and its adjoining shorelines. The pipeline failure appears to have resulted from a hole in the pipeline caused by high-voltage arcing between the pipeline and a utility pole anchor.<ref name="epa.gov" />
* On March 15, a failure occurred on a 36-inch gas pipeline near [[Crystal Falls, Michigan]]. The failure resulted in a release of gas, which did not ignite, that created a crater {{convert|30|ft|m}} deep, {{convert|30|ft|m}} wide, and {{convert|120|ft|m}} long. There were no deaths or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: Great Lakes Gas Transmission Company CPF No. 3-2002-1003-H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320021003H/320021003H_CAO_03282002.pdf |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120311083955/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320021003H/320021003H_CAO_03282002.pdf |archivedate=March 11, 2012 }}</ref>
* On April 6, a BP-Amoco pipeline ruptured and released about {{convert|100,000|USgal|L}} of oil into a coastal area known as Little Lake in Louisiana.<ref name="ukopa.co.uk" />
* On May 22, an 8-inch petroleum products pipeline failed, spilling about 2,000 barrels of unleaded gasoline on to a wheat field near [[Ottawa, Kansas]]. Booms had to be deployed in nearby creeks. The pipe failed along a seam, possibly due to LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] pipeline failure issues.<ref>{{cite web|title=May 31, 2002 – Re: CPF No. 3-2002-501 I H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320025011H/320025011h_text.pdf |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028014046/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320025011H/320025011h_text.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On June 20, PHMSA ordered [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] Company to do extensive repair to one of their gas transmission pipelines in the states of [[Pennsylvania]] and [[New York (state)|New York]], after finding extensive wall thinning on sections of that pipeline system caused by external corrosion. Approximately 800 anomalies with wall thickness losses of greater than 65 percent were found during a smart pig examination, with 76 of the found anomalies having a wall thickness loss of greater than 80 percent. Many of the affected sections of pipe were older sections lacking coating, which is known to reduce external corrosion on pipelines.<ref>{{cite web|title=June 20, 2002 – RE: CPF No. 1-2002-1004-H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120021004H/120021004H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06202002.pdf |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028024147/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120021004H/120021004H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06202002.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On July 4, there was a rupture of an [[Enbridge]] Pipeline, and release of crude oil near [[Cohasset, Minnesota]]. The pipeline ruptured in a marsh in Itasca County, spilling {{convert|6000|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil. In an attempt to keep the oil from contaminating the [[Mississippi River]], the Minnesota Department of Natural Resources set a controlled burn that lasted for one day and created a smoke plume about 1 mile (1.6&nbsp;km) high and 5 miles (8&nbsp;km) long. The pipe failed due to cracking caused by train shipping induced cracking of the pipe being delivered.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR0401.aspx |title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-04-01 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150922142541/http://ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR0401.aspx |archivedate=September 22, 2015 }}</ref>
* On July 24 a gas explosion leveled a [[Hopkinton, Massachusetts]] house, killing a 4-year-old girl and her 5-year-old sister. A failed sleeve on the gas line in the basement of the house was suspected of being the cause.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.metrowestdailynews.com/news/x1602165196/Family-still-grieves-10-years-after-fatal-Hopkinton-explosion?zc_p=0 |title=Family still grieves ten years after fatal Hopkinton explosion – News – Framingham, MA |publisher=The MetroWest Daily News |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028042824/http://www.metrowestdailynews.com/news/x1602165196/Family-still-grieves-10-years-after-fatal-Hopkinton-explosion?zc_p=0 |archivedate=October 28, 2013}}</ref>
* On August 5, a natural gas pipeline exploded and caught fire west of Rt. 622, on Poca River Road near [[Lanham, West Virginia]]. Emergency workers evacuated three or four families. Kanawha and Putnam Counties in the area were requested to shelter in place. Parts of the pipeline were thrown hundreds of yards away, around, and across Poca River. The fire was not contained for several hours because valves to shut down the line did not exist. The Orange Glow from the fire at 11&nbsp;PM; could be seen for several miles.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.ebdc7a8a7e39f2e55cf2031050248a0c/?vgnextoid=fdd2dfa122a1d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=3430fb649a2dc110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print |title=PHMSA – Data and Statistics – Distribution, Transmission, and Liquid Accident and Incident Data |publisher=Phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130428103024/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/portal/site/PHMSA/menuitem.ebdc7a8a7e39f2e55cf2031050248a0c/?vgnextoid=fdd2dfa122a1d110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextchannel=3430fb649a2dc110VgnVCM1000009ed07898RCRD&vgnextfmt=print |archivedate=April 28, 2013 }}</ref> The explosion and fire caused in $2,735,339 property damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/safety/IncDetSt_st_WV_flt_sig.html?nocache=2986 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028020753/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/safety/IncDetSt_st_WV_flt_sig.html?nocache=2986 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On September 20, at around 22:10 a gasoline leak from an 8-inch pipeline operated by Cenex Pipeline (terminal) was discovered near [[Glendive, Montana]]. The release of bout{{convert|1000|oilbbl|m3}} of unleaded gasoline flowed into Seven Mile Creek, and then downstream to its confluence with the [[Yellowstone River]]. Several trenches were constructed near the ruptured pipe for product collection points. As of September 25, 2002, a vacuum truck had recovered approximately {{convert|21,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline [and water] from the boomed locations and trenches.<ref>{{cite web|title=U.S. EPA On-Scene Coordinator Report |date=November 20, 2002 |work=Docket No. CWA-08-2002-35 |url=http://www.epa.gov/region8/superfund/mt/milltowncfr/cfr/CenexPol1.pdf |publisher=EPA.gov |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121102023429/http://www.epa.gov/region8/superfund/mt/milltowncfr/cfr/CenexPol1.pdf |archivedate=November 2, 2012}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Environmental Protection Agency: CWA0820040033CAFO |url=https://www.scribd.com/doc/2011842/Environmental-Protection-Agency-CWA0820040033CAFO |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121108135255/http://www.scribd.com/doc/2011842/Environmental-Protection-Agency-CWA0820040033CAFO |archivedate=November 8, 2012}}</ref>
* On November 2, a [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] pipeline ruptured near [[Corinne, Utah]], spilling about 450 barrels of petroleum. The cause was from external corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270957 |title=Nov. 2, 2002 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20151228110111/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270957 |archivedate=December 28, 2015 }}</ref>
* On December 10, a farmer plowing a field hit and ruptured a [[Williams Companies]] pipeline, near [[Lawrence, Kansas]]. About 4,700 gallons of gasoline were spilled. Later, it was noted that particular pipeline lacked soil coverage in places, including some exposed spots. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270977 |title=Dec. 10, 2002 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006203659/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/270977 |archivedate=October 6, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=20021218&id=_o4yAAAAIBAJ&sjid=Q-kFAAAAIBAJ&pg=6782,6552336|title=Lawrence Journal-World – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>

=== 2003 ===
* On January 24, an [[Enbridge]] crude oil pipeline ruptured at a terminal in [[Douglas County, Wisconsin]]. Some of the crude oil flowed into the [[Nemadji River]]. Over {{convert|100,000|USgal|L}} were spilled.<ref name="nwf"/>
* On February 2, a natural gas pipeline ruptured near [[Viola, Illinois]], resulting in the release of natural gas which ignited. A l6-foot section of the pipe fractured into three sections, which were ejected to distances of about 300 yards from the failure site.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: CPF No. 3-2003-1002-H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320031002H/320031002H_CAO_02072003.pdf |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120311083600/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320031002H/320031002H_CAO_02072003.pdf |archivedate=March 11, 2012 }}</ref>
* On February 20, a 24-inch gas transmission pipeline started leaking in [[Scott County, Missouri]], underneath the [[Mississippi River]]. A shifted pipeline weight has caused damage to the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No 3-2003-1005-H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320031005H/320031005h_cao_03042003_text.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170224172944/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320031005H/320031005h_cao_03042003_text.pdf |archivedate=February 24, 2017 }}</ref>
* On or about February 22, 2003, approximately 788 barrels of gasoline were discharged from a portion of [[Plantation Pipeline]] in [[Hull, Georgia]], some of which entered into an unnamed tributary of East Sandy Creek and its adjoining shorelines. The spill resulted from a failed gasket on a buried block valve.
* On February 27, dropping temperatures caused an [[Enbridge]] pipeline to fail in [[Samaria, Michigan]]. 130 barrels of crude oil were spilled.
* On March 13, a seam failed on an 8-inch Dixie Pipeline propane line near [[Appling, Georgia]], releasing about 110,000 gallons of propane. There were no injuries. The pipe split due to seam failure.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: CPF No. 2-2003-5002H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220035002H/220035002h_cao_03242003_text.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170215131725/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220035002H/220035002h_cao_03242003_text.pdf |archivedate=February 15, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271056 |title=March 13, 2003 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140714135720/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271056 |archivedate=July 14, 2014 }}</ref>
* On March 23, a 24-inch [[El Paso Natural Gas]] pipeline near [[Eaton, Colorado]] exploded. The explosion sent flames 160 meters in the air, forcing evacuations. No one was injured. The heat from the flames melted the siding of two nearby houses and started many smaller grass fires.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: CPF No, 5-2003-1002H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520031002H/520031002h_corrective%20action%20order_04032003_text.pdf |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028015353/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520031002H/520031002h_corrective%20action%20order_04032003_text.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On April 1, a 12-inch [[ConocoPhillips]] petroleum products pipeline ruptured, spilling about 1,000 barrels of Diesel fuel near [[Ponca City, Oklahoma]], with of the fuel getting into Doga Creek. There were no injuries. Low Frequency ERW pipe seam failure was suspected as the cause.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: CPF No. 4-2003-S009H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420035009H/CPF420035009H.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170207182901/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420035009H/CPF420035009H.pdf |archivedate=February 7, 2017 }}</ref>
* On May 1, a 26-inch [[Williams Companies]] natural gas transmission pipeline failed near [[Lake Tapps, Washington]]. A neighboring elementary school, a supermarket, and 30 to 40 houses in approximately a {{convert|4|mi|km|adj=on}} area were evacuated. There was no fire or injuries. Land movement was suspected at first, but the failure was later determined to be from [[stress corrosion cracking]]. There were four previous failures on this pipeline in the preceding eight years.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: CPF No. 5-2003-1003-8 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520031003H/520031003H.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170209173544/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520031003H/520031003H.pdf |archivedate=February 9, 2017 }}</ref><ref name="primis.phmsa.dot.gov">{{cite web|title=CPF No. 5-2003-1003-8 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520031003H/520031003HA.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170220173528/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520031003H/520031003HA.pdf |archivedate=February 20, 2017 }}</ref>
* On May 8, an 8-inch LPG pipeline failed near [[Lebanon, Ohio]]. About 80 houses and one school in the area were evacuated. There was no fire or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: CPF No. 3-2003-5014H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320035014H/320035014H_CAO_05162003.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211092103/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/Reports/enforce/documents/320035014H/320035014H_CAO_05162003.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On May 20, a 30-inch gas pipeline exploded and burned near [[Nederland, Texas]]. The cause of the failure was internal corrosion, and the damages were estimated to be $6,901,322.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.firehouse.com/topic/rescue-and-special-ops/natural-gas-pipeline-explodes-texas |title=Natural Gas Pipeline Explodes in Texas |publisher=Firehouse |date=May 21, 2003 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271121 |title=May 20, 2003 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020202955/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271121 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* On July 2, excavation damage to a natural gas distribution line resulted in an explosion and fire in [[Wilmington, Delaware]]. A contractor hired by the city of Wilmington to replace sidewalk and curbing, dug into an unmarked natural gas service line with a backhoe. Although the service line did not leak where it was struck, the contact resulted in a break in the line inside the basement of a nearby building, where gas began to accumulate. A manager for the contractor said that he did not smell gas and therefore did not believe there was imminent danger and that he called an employee of the gas company and left a voice mail message. At approximately 1:44&nbsp;p.m., an explosion destroyed two residences and damaged two others to the extent that they had to be demolished. Other nearby residences sustained some damage, and the residents on the block were displaced from their houses for about a week. Three contractor employees sustained serious injuries. Eleven additional people sustained minor injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB0401.pdf |format=PDF |title=National Transportation Safety Board |date=July 2, 2003 |website=Ntsb.gov |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB0401.pdf |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On July 3, a jury found Texas-New Mexico Pipeline (TNMP) Company guilty of fraud, gross negligence and willful misconduct in concealing a 1992 crude oil pipeline leak beneath a [[Midland, Texas]] residential subdivision, before selling the pipeline to EOTT Energy in 1999. Oil was discovered in the water table in late 2000, and in March 2001 a group of Midland residents sued EOTT, TNMP and Equilon. Residents living on affected land also received settlements. The spill was estimated in 2003 to be 9,000–13,000 barrels. 190 boxes full of TNMP documents about the pipeline dating from the late 1980s to early 1990s (prior to EOTT Energy taking over the pipeline) were dug up from a 45-foot-deep hole at a site along the company's pipeline in New Mexico.<ref>{{cite web|author= |url=http://lubbockonline.com/stories/070303/reg_070303068.shtml |title=Texas-New Mexico Pipeline Co. found guilty of negligence in Midland oil leak &#124; Lubbock Online &#124; Lubbock Avalanche-Journal |publisher=Lubbock Online |date=July 3, 2003 |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160130110820/http://lubbockonline.com/stories/070303/reg_070303068.shtml |archivedate=January 30, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.bizjournals.com/houston/stories/2003/06/09/newscolumn1.html?page=all |title=More pipeline documents may be collecting dust near Midland |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141025065451/http://www.bizjournals.com/houston/stories/2003/06/09/newscolumn1.html?page=all |archivedate=October 25, 2014 }}</ref>
* On July 10, a 16-inch [[Citgo]] petroleum products pipeline failed in [[Cook County, Illinois]]. About 25 barrels of gasoline were spilled from the pipeline. A crack in the pipe had developed at a dent. There was no fire or injured reported.<ref>{{cite web|title=RE: CPF No 3-2003-5019H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320035019H/320035019H_CAO_07172003.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170224151255/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320035019H/320035019H_CAO_07172003.pdf |archivedate=February 24, 2017 }}</ref>
* On July 16, a 12&nbsp;3/4-inch pipeline burst in [[Barnes County, North Dakota]], releasing 9,000 barrels of propane, which ignited. There were no casualties. During repairs, mechanical damage was seen on 2 nearby section of this pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: CPF No. 3-2003-5020H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320035020H/320035020H_CAO_07252003.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170208175839/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320035020H/320035020H_CAO_07252003.pdf |archivedate=February 8, 2017 }}</ref>
* On July 30, a [[Kinder Morgan]] pipeline in Tucson, Arizona ruptured, and sprayed 16,548 gallons of gasoline on five houses under construction, and flooding nearby streets with gasoline. The resulting pipeline closure caused major gas shortages and price increases in the state. The failure at first was thought to be from LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] flaws, but tests showed it was due to [[stress corrosion cracking]]. A hydrostatic test that was performed on this pipeline after repairs failed again {{convert|40|ft|m}} from the first failure.<ref>{{cite web|title=Re: CPF No. 4-2003-$0108 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420035010H/420035010H.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170209173530/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420035010H/420035010H.pdf |archivedate=February 9, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.azcentral.com/12news/news/articles/0820gas-main20-ON-CP.html |archive-url=https://archive.is/20120719031704/http://www.azcentral.com/12news/news/articles/0820gas-main20-ON-CP.html |dead-url=yes |archive-date=July 19, 2012 |title=Pipeline fails tests; gas shortage likely to continue |publisher=Azcentral.com |date=August 20, 2003 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://docs.google.com/viewer?a=v&q=cache:t9p8LUOjuhIJ:www.globalsecurity.org/security/library/congress/2003_h/031009-bannigan.doc+kinder+morgan+arizona+pipeline+failure&hl=en&gl=us&pid=bl&srcid=ADGEESg8hYg86MCQY-i1SSpC-LhS3cL279Iin8fPjcY0Hhd_iPnaHrkKkURTBaX62d8mArqYe8Qlz_pMKohUdKElB1OSBK-K_84Q2AJWNaup8w3YQXxN6VdBnpo3UAbLvGUMMjdCzpVr&sig=AHIEtbQ4teiQyeIt8vRqcO3Zlsh3wScSeQ |title=Google Drive Viewer |publisher=Docs.google.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.azleg.state.az.us/Alispdfs/46leg/1r/House/ArizonaFuelSupplyReport111303.pdf |title=Microsoft Word – ArizonaFuelSupplyReport11_13_03.doc |format=PDF |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028121307/http://www.azleg.state.az.us/Alispdfs/46leg/1r/House/ArizonaFuelSupplyReport111303.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271171 |title=July 30, 2003 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140714134204/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271171 |archivedate=July 14, 2014 }}</ref>
* On August 8, a 26-inch [[Kinder Morgan]] and Myria Holdings [[Natural Gas Pipeline Company of America]] transmission pipeline ruptured in [[Caddo County, Oklahoma]], releasing about 84,000 MCF of natural gas. A 54-foot long section of 26" diameter pipe had blown out and landed 30 feet from the ditch. Evacuations took place within 3/4 of a mile from the release, but there was no fire or casualties. [[Stress corrosion cracking]] was identified as the pipe failure's cause.<ref>{{cite web|title=PHMSA Corrective Action Order, CPF No.4-2003-1008H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420031008H/420031008H.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170209173459/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420031008H/420031008H.pdf |archivedate=February 9, 2017 }}</ref>
* On September 26, a propane pipeline at the Phillips Petroleum storage facility in [[Cahokia, Illinois]] ruptured, sending flames high into the air and sparking small grass fires in the area.
* On October 6, a 12-inch petroleum products pipeline ruptured in [[Johnson County, Kansas]], spilling about 100 to 200 barrels of Diesel fuel. Some of the Diesel contaminated a nearby waterway. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No.3-2003-5023 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320035023H/320035023H_CAO_10242003.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211093037/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/reports/enforce/documents/320035023H/320035023H_CAO_10242003.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On October 13, a failure on an [[Enbridge]] pipeline near [[Bay City, Michigan]] spilled 500 barrels of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271227 |title=Oct. 13, 2003 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020203108/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271227 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref><ref name="addictinginfo.org">{{cite web|url=http://www.addictinginfo.org/2013/07/17/fighting-fossil-fuel-in-michigan-inside-the-pipeline-chris-wahmhoff-story-part-2/#ixzz2ZIsftiAy |title=Addicting Info |work=Addicting Info |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141103192408/http://www.addictinginfo.org/2013/07/17/fighting-fossil-fuel-in-michigan-inside-the-pipeline-chris-wahmhoff-story-part-2/ |archivedate=November 3, 2014 }}</ref>
* On October 14, a leak on what was originally the [[Big Inch]] 24-inch of natural gas occurred in [[Orange County, Indiana]]. There were no injuries or evacuations. The pipeline had been installed in 1943.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2003-1010H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320031010H/320031010H_CAO_10242003.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170208175830/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320031010H/320031010H_CAO_10242003.pdf |archivedate=February 8, 2017 }}</ref>
* On November 2, a Texas Eastern Transmission natural gas pipeline exploded in [[Bath County, Kentucky]], about 1.5&nbsp;km south of a Duke Energy pumping station. A fire burned for about an hour before firefighters extinguished it. No one was injured and no property damage was reported.<ref name="nwf"/>
* On November 9, an 8-inch [[Buckeye Partners]] pipeline failed near [[Mazon, Illinois]]. While repairs were being tested on this pipeline on November 14, another section of this pipeline failed about 1500 feet from the first leak. About ten barrels of gasoline and Diesel fuel were spilled by the two leaks, requiring soil removal. External corrosion caused both failures. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2003-5026H|accessdate=27 November 2016}}</ref>
* On December 13, another section of the same [[Williams Companies]] gas transmission pipeline that failed on May 1, 2003, failed in [[Lewis County, Washington]]. There was no fire this time. Gas flowed for three hours before being shut off. Gas pressure had already been reduced 20% on this pipeline after the May 1 explosion. External corrosion and [[stress corrosion cracking]] were seen in this failed area of pipe.<ref name="primis.phmsa.dot.gov" />

=== 2004 ===
* On January 25, a TEPPCO 8-inch propane pipeline failed, near [[Davenport, New York]]. The propane ignited, destroying a trailer house, and forcing evacuations. About 5,000 barrels of propane were burned. There were no injuries. The incident resulted from a through-wall failure of the pipe material at a fitting that was attached to the top of the pipe.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No.- 1-2004-5002-H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120045002H/120045002H.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170206191748/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120045002H/120045002H.pdf |archivedate=February 6, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 1-2010-5008H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120105008H/120105008H_CAO_09022010_text.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170208200819/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120105008H/120105008H_CAO_09022010_text.pdf |archivedate=February 8, 2017 }}</ref>
* On March 12, a TEPPCO pipeline spilled about 500 barrels of unleaded gasoline spilled into the [[Moro Creek]], which flows into the [[Sabine River (Texas–Louisiana)|Sabine River]] near [[Kingsland, Arkansas]]. The cause was corrosion of a 1/2-inch bleeder line, that was part of a 20-inch pipeline block valve used to equalize pressure across the valve.<ref name="www2.epa.gov" />
* On April 28, a petroleum pipeline of [[Kinder Morgan Energy Partners]] ruptured, and spilled an estimated 103,000 gallons of Diesel fuel into marshes, adjacent to [[Suisun Bay]], in Northern California. The line failed from external cossorosion. The company failed to notify California authorities about the spill for 18 hours, a failure for which it was later cited.<ref name="nwf"/><ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?file=/c/a/2004/04/30/MNGQ46DALP47.DTL |work=The San Francisco Chronicle |first1=Demian |last1=Bulwa |first2=Kelly |last2=St. John |first3=Peter |last3=Fimrite |title=Pipeline spills {{convert|60,000|USgal|L}} of fuel into Suisun Marsh / Operators noticed problem Tuesday but waited to report it |date=June 24, 2011 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20090315191702/http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?file=%2Fc%2Fa%2F2004%2F04%2F30%2FMNGQ46DALP47.DTL |archivedate=March 15, 2009 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271379 |title=April 27, 2004 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141206063357/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271379 |archivedate=December 6, 2014 }}</ref>
* On May 23, a leak in a sampling tube on a pipeline in [[Renton, Washington]] spilled several thousand gallons of gasoline, which ignited.<ref>{{cite news|author1=Gordy Holt|author2= Robert Mcclur |url=http://www.seattlepi.com/local/174862_olympic25.html |title=Wear caused gas leak in Olympic pipeline |publisher=Seattlepi.com |date=May 24, 2004 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref>
* On August 19, a series of explosions starting hit an underground natural gas storage cavern in [[Moss Bluff, Texas]], resulting in evacuations for a 3-mile radius. The first blast, about 4&nbsp;a.m., sent flames 150 to 200 feet into the air. The second explosion was seen as far as 20 miles away. Some type of equipment failure was suspected. The cavern had just been expanded using the SMUG (solution mining under gas) process, which permits salt cavern expansion without interrupting gas storage operations. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://usatoday30.usatoday.com/news/nation/2004-08-20-gas-explosion_x.htm?csp=36 |work=USA Today |title=Second explosion rocks gas storage facility in Texas |date=August 20, 2004 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130412204116/http://usatoday30.usatoday.com/news/nation/2004-08-20-gas-explosion_x.htm?csp=36 |archivedate=April 12, 2013 }}</ref>
* On August 21, a natural gas explosion destroyed a residence in [[DuBois, Pennsylvania]]. Two residents were killed in this accident. The NTSB determined that the probable cause of the leak, explosion, and fire was the fracture of a defective butt-fusion joint.<ref>{{cite web|title=DCA-04-MP-006 |url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB0601.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170201221613/https://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB0601.pdf |archivedate=February 1, 2017 }}</ref>
* On September 26, a vandal started up a trackhoe at a construction site in [[New Caney, Texas]], and dug into a propylene pipeline. The escaping propylene ignited, causing nearby residents to evacuate. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.chron.com/news/houston-texas/article/Trespassers-blamed-for-pipeline-explosion-1955274.php |title=Trespassers blamed for pipeline explosion – Houston Chronicle |publisher=Chron.com |date=September 27, 2004 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028013412/http://www.chron.com/news/houston-texas/article/Trespassers-blamed-for-pipeline-explosion-1955274.php |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On September 27, 2004, near [[Blair, Nebraska]], an ammonia pipeline failed, releasing 193,213 pounds of ammonia, resulting in the hospitalization of one individual and emergency responders evacuated houses within a one-mile circumference of the break. An estimated 1,000 fish were killed along North Creek and in a golf course pond.<ref name="justice">{{cite web|url=http://www.justice.gov/opa/pr/2009/August/09-enrd-807.html |title=Pipeline Firms to Pay $3.65 Million to Settle Claims Related to 2004 Ammonia Spills in Nebraska and Kansas – OPA – Department of Justice |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140713040002/http://www.justice.gov/opa/pr/2009/August/09-enrd-807.html |archivedate=July 13, 2014 }}</ref>
* On September 28, a pipeline failed in [[Hughes County, Oklahoma]], spilling an estimated {{convert|1500|oilbbl|m3}} of Diesel fuel.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2004-5028H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420045028H/420045028H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_10012004.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211183428/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/Reports/enforce/documents/420045028H/420045028H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_10012004.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* In October, crews from [[Shell Oil Company]] recovered 100,000 of an oil seawater mix. [[Hurricane Ivan]] had damaged a crude oil pipeline off of the [[Louisiana]] Coast.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1454&dat=20041007&id=7wRPAAAAIBAJ&sjid=vR8EAAAAIBAJ&pg=6896,1841841|title=Star-News – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On October 27, an anhydrous ammonia pipeline ruptured near [[Kingman, Kansas]], and released approximately {{convert|4858|oilbbl|m3}} of anhydrous ammonia. Nobody was killed or injured due to the release. The anhydrous ammonia leak killed more than 20,000 fish along a 12.5-mile section of [[Smoots Creek]], including some from threatened species. The pipeline had previous damage to it. The pipeline controller had misinterpreted the leak as other problems with the system operation, causing the leak to go on longer. As a result of this, and another ammonia pipeline leak the month before, the pipeline owner and its two operating companies were later fined $3.65&nbsp;million.<ref name="justice"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ens-newswire.com/ens/aug2009/2009-08-14-093.asp |title=Ammonia Spills in Nebraska, Kansas Cost Pipeline Firms $3.65M |publisher=ENS-Newswire.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028103937/http://www.ens-newswire.com/ens/aug2009/2009-08-14-093.asp |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On November 1, construction crew ruptured a high-pressure gas line in [[Little Rock, Arkansas]], near one of the state's busiest intersections Monday, triggering a fire that melted traffic lights that hung overhead. No one was injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.firehouse.com/news/news/gas-line-explodes-west-little-rock-arkansas |title=Gas Line Explodes In West Little Rock, Arkansas |publisher=Firehouse |date=November 1, 2004 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref>
* On November 8, a NGL pipeline failed in a housing division in [[Ivel, Kentucky]]. The vapor cloud from the leak ignited, seriously burning a Kentucky State Trooper evacuating those living in the area. Eight others were injured and five houses were destroyed. The pipeline, only {{convert|65|mi|km}} long, had 11 previous corrosion failures.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 2-2004-5017H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220045017H/CPF2_2004_5017H_CAO.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170208110720/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220045017H/CPF2_2004_5017H_CAO.pdf |archivedate=February 8, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=266&dat=20041111&id=ONkrAAAAIBAJ&sjid=GQUGAAAAIBAJ&pg=1534,3752372|title=Kentucky New Era – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On November 9, in [[Walnut Creek, California]], a petroleum pipeline carrying gasoline to [[San Jose, California]], owned and operated by [[Kinder Morgan Energy Partners]] (KMEP) was struck by a backhoe used by Mountain Cascade, Inc., a contractor operating in the construction of a water pipeline for the East Bay Municipal Utility District (EBMUD). A large gasoline spill was subsequently ignited, resulting in an explosive fireball that caused the deaths, by burns, of four workers and one supervisor and the severe injury of five others. A Kinder Morgan worker had misread an as-built map, and had incorrectly marked the pipeline's route before the accident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://osfm.fire.ca.gov/pipeline/pdf/WCFinalReport/KMWCInvRep.pdf |title=Pipeline System |format=PDF |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130406122502/http://osfm.fire.ca.gov/pipeline/pdf/WCFinalReport/KMWCInvRep.pdf |archivedate=April 6, 2013 }}</ref>
* On November 21, a 14-inch petroleum products pipeline sprung a leak while it was shipping gasoline in the [[Mojave Desert]]. The [[Calnev Pipeline]], owned and operated by the California-Nevada Pipeline Company, a subsidiary of [[Kinder-Morgan Energy Partners]], is the main source of petroleum fuel products for the [[Las Vegas Valley]], [[Nevada]]. An {{convert|80|ft|m|adj=on}} geyser of gasoline was discovered on the next morning, after numerous complaints of a strong gasoline odor along Interstate 15 in northern San Bernardino County, CA.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.epa.gov/oem/docs/oil/fss/fss06/key_2.pdf |title=Mojave River Pipeline Spill, San Bernardino County, CA |format=PDF |work=Part 2 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121025183639/http://www.epa.gov/oem/docs/oil/fss/fss06/key_2.pdf |archivedate=October 25, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.epa.gov/oem/docs/oil/fss/fss06/key_1.pdf |title=Mojave River Pipeline Spill, San Bernardino County, CA |format=PDF |work=Part 1 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028062923/http://www.epa.gov/oem/docs/oil/fss/fss06/key_1.pdf |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On December 15, employees were performing maintenance on a propane pipeline near [[Mantador, North Dakota]], when a gasket on the pipeline's valve failed, causing a leak. Nearby resident were evacuated, and a rail line was shut down temporarily. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.firehouse.com/news/news/propane-pipeline-leaks-richland-county-north-dakota |title=Propane Pipeline Leaks In Richland County, North Dakota |publisher= Firehouse.com |date=December 16, 2004 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref>
* On December 24, as much as 5,000 gallons of crude oil spilled from a [[ConocoPhillips]] pipeline south of [[Laurel, Montana]] near the Yellowstone River. Hydrogen sulfide gas from the oil could have posed a major danger, but "the wind helped immensely" to dissipate the gas.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.firehouse.com/news/news/5000-gallons-crude-oil-spilled-montana-pipeline |title=Up To 5,000 Gallons Of Crude Oil Spilled From Montana Pipeline |publisher=Firehouse.com |date=December 27, 2004 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref>

=== 2005 ===
* In January, a Mid-Valley owned and Sunoco operated pipeline ruptured, spilling {{convert|260,000|USgal|L}} of oil into the Kentucky and Ohio rivers. The U.S. Environmental Protection Agency fined the companies $2.5&nbsp;million for the spill.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.justice.gov/opa/pr/2006/August/06_enrd_534.html |title=Federal Government Reaches Settlement with Pipeline Companies Regarding Crude Oil Spills |publisher=Justice.gov |date=August 15, 2006 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130713232646/http://www.justice.gov/opa/pr/2006/August/06_enrd_534.html |archivedate=July 13, 2013 }}</ref>
* On January 18, an [[Enbridge]] pipeline failed from temperature problems, causing a spill of 100 barrels of crude oil in [[Bay City, Michigan]]. The pipe was just two years old at the time.<ref name="addictinginfo.org" /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271629 |title=Jan. 18, 2005 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020210642/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271629 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* On January 26, a Mid Valley 22-inch pipeline ruptured in [[Carrollton, Kentucky]], spilling about 290,000 gallons of crude oil. Some of the crude entered the [[Ohio River]]. The pipe failure was caused by earth movement.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271636 |title=Jan. 26, 2005 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140809050248/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271636 |archivedate=August 9, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=266&dat=20050201&id=-_grAAAAIBAJ&sjid=EW0FAAAAIBAJ&pg=1201,2550921|title=Kentucky New Era – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On February 1, an ExxonMobil gasoline pipeline fire forced 43 families from their houses near [[Allentown, Pennsylvania]]. The fire burned for over 72 hours. There were no reported injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.firehouse.com/news/news/pennsylvania-pile-line-fire-finally-dies-out |title=Pennsylvania Pile Line Fire Finally Dies Out |publisher=Firehouse |date=February 5, 2005 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 1-2005-5002H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120055002H/120055002h_amendment%20to%20corrective%20action%20order_02102005_text.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170225104849/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120055002H/120055002h_amendment%20to%20corrective%20action%20order_02102005_text.pdf |archivedate=February 25, 2017 }}</ref>
* On or about February 28, 2005, approximately 2,497 barrels of Jet A Kerosene discharged from a 14-inch TEPPCO pipeline, reaching the [[Big Cow Creek]], flowing into the [[Sabine River (Texas–Louisiana)|Sabine River]], near [[Newton, Texas]]. The discharge was caused by the over-tightening of a coupling at a 3/8-inch cooling line at the top of a 14-inch mainline pump.<ref name="www2.epa.gov" />
* On March 16, a crew installing a communications cable nicked a gas distribution pipeline in [[Moon Township, Pennsylvania]]. The crew then notified the local One Call center, but, failed to alert first responders. two hours after the nick, gas exploded in a house, burning two teenagers there.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=20050616&id=7L8iAAAAIBAJ&sjid=E7YFAAAAIBAJ&pg=4236,4341778|title=Beaver County Times – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On April 1, a [[Kinder Morgan Energy Partners]] petroleum products pipeline was found to be leaking gasoline, near [[Truckee, California]]. Gasoline spread into Summit Creek, then, into [[Donner Lake]]. About 300 gallons spilled.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 5-2005-5020H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520055020H/520055020H_corrective%20action%20order_04212005.pdf?nocache=4253 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304054322/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520055020H/520055020H_corrective%20action%20order_04212005.pdf?nocache=4253 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.law360.com/articles/25295/kinder-morgan-pays-5-3m-for-california-oil-spills |title=Kinder Morgan Pays $5.3M For California Oil Spills |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141205010432/http://www.law360.com/articles/25295/kinder-morgan-pays-5-3m-for-california-oil-spills |archivedate=December 5, 2014 }}</ref>
* On May 4, a petroleum products pipeline failed near [[El Dorado, Kansas]], spilling about 78,000 gallons of diesel fuel, of which about 46,000 gallons was lost. The pipeline failed from external corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://ksn.com/2015/05/04/diesel-fuel-leaks-into-creek-near-el-dorado/ |title=Diesel fuel leaks into creek near El Dorado |author= |date= |work=KSN-TV |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160610042143/http://ksn.com/2015/05/04/diesel-fuel-leaks-into-creek-near-el-dorado/ |archivedate=June 10, 2016 }}</ref><ref name="dot2">{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_22610.html?nocache=4343#_Incidents_tab_4 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160602230725/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_22610.html?nocache=4343 |archivedate=June 2, 2016 }}</ref>
* On May 13, an underground natural gas pipeline exploded near [[Marshall, Texas]], sending a giant fireball into the sky and hurling a {{convert|160|ft|m|adj=on}} section of pipe onto the grounds of a nearby electric power generating plant. Two people were hurt. The OPS concluded that stress corrosion cracking was the culprit.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No.4-2005-1011 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420051011H/cpf_420051011H.pdf?nocache=8618 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304071502/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420051011H/cpf_420051011H.pdf?nocache=8618 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On May 13, the 30-inch [[Seaway Pipeline]], operated by TEPPCO at the time, failed in [[Bryan County, Oklahoma]], spilling approximately 898 barrels of crude oil. Oil reached Eastman Creek. The discharge was caused by a 6-inch longitudinal seam split on the pipeline that resulted from a stress crack that may have been induced by conditions occurring during rail transport of the pipe, and enlarged by pressure-cycle-induced stresses over years of operation of the pipeline.<ref name="www2.epa.gov" /><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-200S-S02OH |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420055020H/cpf_420055020H.pdf?nocache=6120 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304070107/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420055020H/cpf_420055020H.pdf?nocache=6120 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On May 23, a Magellan Pipeline petroleum products pipeline broke near [[Kansas City, Kansas]], spilling gasoline into the nearby [[Missouri River]]. About 2,936 barrels of gasoline were spilled, with about 2,400 barrels being lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=20050524&id=qa9TAAAAIBAJ&sjid=pTgNAAAAIBAJ&pg=6812,1883891|title=Lawrence Journal-World – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/safety/IncDetSt_st_KS_flt_sig.html?nocache=3916 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022132703/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/safety/IncDetSt_st_KS_flt_sig.html?nocache=3916 |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref>
* On May 28, a {{convert|12|in|mm|adj=on}} [[Kinder Morgan Energy Partners]] pipeline ruptured in [[El Paso, Texas]], releasing gasoline.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-200S-S021H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420055021H/cpf_420055021H.pdf?nocache=6836 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304070221/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420055021H/cpf_420055021H.pdf?nocache=6836 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On August 11, a bulldozer hit a crude oil pipeline north of [[Lufkin, Texas]]. The escaping crude ignited, injuring the bulldozer operator. About 18,500 gallons of crude oil were lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=20050812&id=9wFaAAAAIBAJ&sjid=DksNAAAAIBAJ&pg=3062,2400235|title=The Victoria Advocate – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271786 |title=Aug. 11, 2005 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140914134301/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/271786 |archivedate=September 14, 2014 }}</ref>
* On August 18, a leak was detected in an insulating flange along the [[BP Amoco]] Whiting to River Rouge pipeline at a monitoring well in [[Granger, Indiana]]. Initially, the bolts and nuts were replaced around the flange to mitigate any leaks; on August 25, when supply concerns diminished, the insulating flange was cut out and replaced with a straight section of pipe. Approximately 21 gallons of gasoline were removed from the ground, with no injuries or fatalities. Metallurgical analysis revealed that the fiber ring joint gasket had evidence of a prior leak.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://phmsa.dot.gov/pv_obj_cache/pv_obj_id_57120F071D73FB61A361DB56996AD13B62882100/filename/AmocoBPflange_red_app_d.pdf |title=US Department of Transportation Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety Administration, Office of Pipeline Safety – Failure Investigation Report |accessdate=July 13, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://phmsa.dot.gov/pv_obj_cache/pv_obj_id_57120F071D73FB61A361DB56996AD13B62882100/filename/AmocoBPflange_red_app_d.pdf |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On August 29 [[Hurricane Katrina]] caused a protective levee to fail near [[Nairn, Louisiana|Nairn]] in [[Plaquemines Parish, Louisiana]], causing a Shell 20-inch pipeline to rupture.
