About 13,400 gallons were spilled, with about 10,500 gallons of this spill reaching the shoreline, and coastal marshes.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.tos.org/oceanography/archive/19-2_pine.pdf |title=19.2_text.indd |format=PDF |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027234229/http://www.tos.org/oceanography/archive/19-2_pine.pdf |archivedate=October 27, 2013}}</ref>
* In August, [[Hurricane Katrina]] damaged numerous offshore pipelines, in [[Gulf of Mexico]] region.<ref>https://www.cbsnews.com/news/not-one-drop-of-oil-spilled-not-quite/</ref>
* On September 18, a pipeline pumping station employee was killed in [[Monroe, Ohio]], when leaking propane was ignited and exploded by an arcing pump on September 18. Flames reached {{convert|300|ft|m}} high in the following fire.<ref>{{cite web |title=US Department of Transportation: PHMSA Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety Administration: OPS Office of Pipeline Safety: Central Region |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/pv_obj_cache/pv_obj_id_62FA151109EF7E5E68067AE644C9CCD599530600/filename/TEPPCO%20HL%20OH%202005-09-18%20508.pdf |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160126152710/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/pv_obj_cache/pv_obj_id_62FA151109EF7E5E68067AE644C9CCD599530600/filename/TEPPCO%20HL%20OH%202005-09-18%20508.pdf |archivedate=January 26, 2016}}</ref>
* On December 6, a natural gas compressor station exploded near [[Rifle, Colorado]], about 200 yards from Interstate 70. There was only one minor injury to a nearby truck driver.<ref>{{cite web|first=Heidi |last=Rice |url=http://www.summitdaily.com/article/20051207/NEWS/112070033 |title=Natural gas explosion shakes up Colo. between Rifle and Rulison |publisher=SummitDaily.com |date=December 7, 2005 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027232304/http://www.summitdaily.com/article/20051207/NEWS/112070033 |archivedate=October 27, 2013 }}</ref>
* On December 13, workers removing an underground oil tank in [[Bergenfield, New Jersey]] undermined a 1&nbsp;1/4-inch steel gas pipeline. The gas line later failed, causing an explosion. Three residents of a nearby apartment building were killed. Four other residents and a tank removal worker were injured. Failure to evacuate the apartment building after the gas line ruptured was listed as a contributing factor.<ref>{{cite web|title=Accident No.: DCA-06-MP-001 |url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB0701.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161128050131/http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Reports/PAB0701.pdf |archivedate=November 28, 2016 }}</ref>

=== 2006 ===
* On January 13, a pipeline leak near [[Independence, Kansas]] spill about 135,000 gallons of petroleum product, of which about 93,000 gallons was lost. The pipeline failed from external corrosion.<ref name="dot4">{{cite web|title=UNITED STATES SECURITIES AND EXCHANGE COMMISSION Washington, D.C. 20549 FORM 10-Q |url=https://www.magellanlp.com/uploadedFiles/Investors/Financials/2006/MMP%20-%203q06%2010q%20-%20Final%20Donnelley%20Draft.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20101216093213/http://magellanlp.com/uploadedFiles/Investors/Financials/2006/MMP%20-%203q06%2010q%20-%20Final%20Donnelley%20Draft.pdf |archivedate=December 16, 2010 }}</ref>
* On February 28, a gas compressor station explosion severely burned a worker, and set off a raging fire near [[De Beque, Colorado]]. A second explosion at that site soon after caused no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nbc11news.com/home/headlines/2385406.html |title=Man Injured In Natural Gas Explosion |publisher=NBC11news.com |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028044309/http://www.nbc11news.com/home/headlines/2385406.html |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* The [[Prudhoe Bay oil spill]]: On March 2, a surveillance crew discovered a crude oil spill from a [[BP]] crude pipeline near [[North Slope Borough, Alaska]]. The pipeline failure resulted in a release currently estimated at {{convert|5000|oilbbl|m3}} of processed crude oil, impacting the arctic tundra and covering approximately {{convert|2|acre|m2}} of permafrost. The pipeline's leak detection system was not effective in recognizing and identifying the failure. Failure to run [[pigging|cleaning pigs]] to remove internal corrosive build up. The failure caused crude oil price to spike throughout the World.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 5-2006-501 5H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520065015H/BP%205-2006-5015H%20-%20Final.pdf?nocache=9340 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304065542/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520065015H/BP%205-2006-5015H%20-%20Final.pdf?nocache=9340 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.chron.com/business/energy/article/Pipe-corrosion-in-Alaska-takes-the-issue-off-back-1899295.php |title=Pipe corrosion in Alaska takes the issue off back burner – Houston Chronicle |publisher=Chron.com |date=August 13, 2006 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121010133036/http://www.chron.com/business/energy/article/Pipe-corrosion-in-Alaska-takes-the-issue-off-back-1899295.php |archivedate=October 10, 2012 }}</ref>
* On March 23, a pipeline failed west of [[Toledo, Ohio]], spilling about {{convert|200 |oilbbl|m3}} of unleaded gasoline. During the repair work, another smaller nearby leak was also found.<ref>{{cite web|title=Corrective Action Order_03292006 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320065033H/320065033H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_03292006.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170217225824/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/reports/enforce/documents/320065033H/320065033H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_03292006.pdf |archivedate=February 17, 2017 }}</ref>
* On April 17, a [[Plantation Pipeline]] line experienced a failure in Henrico County, near [[Richmond, Virginia]]. The failure resulted in the release of 23,226 gallons of jet fuel in a residential area. The jet fuel sprayed for approximately 14 minutes and the spray traveled the distance of approximately {{convert|200|ft|m}}. The jet fuel did not ignite.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF NO. 1-2006-5003-H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120065003H/120065003H_CAO_04202006.pdf?nocache=4592 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304065757/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120065003H/120065003H_CAO_04202006.pdf?nocache=4592 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272047 |title=April 17, 2006 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020210550/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272047 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* On June 27, a [[Koch Industries]] pipeline carrying crude oil failed near the town of [[Little Falls, Minnesota]]. The pipeline estimated that approximately {{convert|3200 |oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil were released. The pipeline failed from previous mechanical damage to the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2006-5037H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320065037H/CPF_NO_3-2006-5037H.pdf?nocache=1341 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304064126/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320065037H/CPF_NO_3-2006-5037H.pdf?nocache=1341 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272108 |title=June 27, 2006 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020210552/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272108 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* On July 22, a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] Company gas transmission pipeline ruptured, resulting in an estimated release of {{convert|42946000|cuft|m3|abbr=on}} of natural gas near Clay City in [[Clark County, Kentucky]]. The gas ignited, but there were no injuries, and just minor property damage. External corrosion was suspected.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 2-2006-3 007 H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220061007H/220061007H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_07272006.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211183405/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/Reports/enforce/documents/220061007H/220061007H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_07272006.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lex18.com/news/gas-explosion-was-kentucky-s-fourth-in-last-decade#!prettyPhoto/0/ |title=Gas Explosion Was Kentucky's Fourth In Last Decade |location=Lexington, Kentucky |publisher=LEX18.com |date=January 3, 2012 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027221607/http://www.lex18.com/news/gas-explosion-was-kentucky-s-fourth-in-last-decade |archivedate=October 27, 2013}}</ref>
* On August 7, a leak from a pump, on a pipeline, released about 241,000 gallons of HVL's, in [[Jennings, Louisiana]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272137|title=Aug. 7, 2006 – ProPublica|author=|date=|work=propublica.org|accessdate=May 23, 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31554.html?nocache=7376#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160308063412/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31554.html?nocache=7376 |archivedate=March 8, 2016 }}</ref>
* On August 12, a Kinder Morgan petroleum pipeline failed in [[Romeoville, Illinois]]. About {{convert|59,000|USgal|L}} of butane were lost. External corrosion was the cause, but there were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_4472.html?nocache=4162#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |publisher=DOT.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028022217/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_4472.html?nocache=4162 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref name=autogenerated2>{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/liquid0102.zip |publisher=phmsa.dot.gov |title=liquid0102.zip |accessdate=September 28, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161213203558/http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/liquid0102.zip |archivedate=December 13, 2016 }}</ref>
* On September 8, a leak on a pump on an LPG pipeline in [[Apex, North Carolina]] spilled about 12,000 gallons of propane, forcing evacuations.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_3445.html?nocache=2146#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307104148/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_3445.html?nocache=2146 |archivedate=March 7, 2016 }}</ref>
* On September 29, a crew replacing an old pipeline hit a high pressure gas pipeline in [[Labette County, Kansas]], killing a crewman. Resident with a milre of the incident were evacuated for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2199&dat=20060930&id=sXNUAAAAIBAJ&sjid=PzsNAAAAIBAJ&pg=1944,7850067|title=Lawrence Journal-World – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On October 12, a pipeline exploded when a tugboat pushing two barges hit that pipeline Thursday in West Cote Blanche Bay, about two miles (3&nbsp;km) from shore and {{convert|100|mi|km}} southwest of [[New Orleans, Louisiana]]. Four crew members were killed, and two were missing and later presumed dead.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.foxnews.com/story/0,2933,220505,00.html |work=Fox News |title=Searchers Find Body of Fourth Victim of Deadly Louisiana Gas Pipeline Explosion |date=October 13, 2006}}{{dead link|date=May 2016|bot=medic}}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|first=Dwayne |last=Clark |url=http://lawboat.blogspot.com/2006_10_01_archive.html |title=Jacksonville Florida Maritime Lawyers |publisher=Lawboat.blogspot.com |date=October 5, 2006 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131107005754/http://lawboat.blogspot.com/2006_10_01_archive.html |archivedate=November 7, 2013 }}</ref>
* On October 25, an ammonia pipeline failed from corrosion near [[Clay Center, Kansas]], releasing about 4500 barrels of ammonia. two people were injured by the fumes.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31618.html |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |publisher=DOT.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121008190226/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31618.html |archivedate=October 8, 2012 }}</ref>
* On November 11, a jet-black, {{convert|300|acre|km2|adj=on}} burn site surrounded the skeletal hulk of a bulldozer that struck a natural-gas pipeline during construction of another pipeline, and produced a powerful explosion near [[Cheyenne, Wyoming]]. The bulldozer operator was killed. The company building the new pipeline was fined $2.3&nbsp;million for failing to obtain a locate on the other pipeline.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.foxnews.com/story/0,2933,228843,00.html |title=1 Dead After Wyoming Gas Pipeline Explodes |publisher=Fox News |date=November 11, 2006 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20071208135236/http://www.foxnews.com/story/0%2C2933%2C228843%2C00.html |archivedate=December 8, 2007 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2009/12/01/el-paso-corp-fined-23-mil_n_375774.html |work=Huffington Post |title=El Paso Corp. Fined $2.3 million For Wyoming Pipeline Explosion |date=December 1, 2009 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131031054223/http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2009/12/01/el-paso-corp-fined-23-mil_n_375774.html |archivedate=October 31, 2013}}</ref>
* On or about November 27, 2006, approximately 97 barrels of gasoline were discharged from a portion of [[Plantation Pipeline]] in [[Mecklenburg County, North Carolina]], into Paw Creek and its adjoining shorelines. The leak resulted from a failed gasket on an above-ground block valve.<ref name="epa.gov" />
* '''[[2006 Falk Corporation explosion]]''': Leaks in a [[Milwaukee|Milwaukee, Wisconsin]] propane pipe running below an apartment building caused an explosion. Three people were killed and forty-seven others injured.
* On December 19, a lineman for Midwest Energy hit a natural gas transmission pipeline near [[Mason, Michigan]]. The lineman was killed in the following explosion and fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://news.msn.com/us/pipeline-explosions-from-around-the-united-states#image=7|title=News|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/safety/IncDetSt_st_MI_flt_sig.html?nocache=2203 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022132814/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/safety/IncDetSt_st_MI_flt_sig.html?nocache=2203 |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref>
* On December 24, a [[Plains All American Pipeline]] ruptured, spilling about 23,856 gallons of crude oil in the [[Gulf of Mexico]], about 30 miles southeast of [[Galveston, Texas]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=861&dat=20061227&id=NKE_AAAAIBAJ&sjid=alYMAAAAIBAJ&pg=1187,1165867|title=The Victoria Advocate – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272243 |title=Dec. 24, 2006 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020210647/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272243 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>

=== 2007 ===
* On January 1, an [[Enbridge]] pipeline that runs from [[Superior, Wisconsin]] to near [[Whitewater, Wisconsin]] failed, resulting in a spill of 1,500 barrels of crude oil onto farmland and into a drainage ditch. Incomplete fusion of a longitudinal weld at the pipe maker that failed as pressure cycle was established as the cause.<ref>{{cite web|last=Content |first=Thomas |url=http://www.jsonline.com/business/29254864.html |title=Milwaukee Journal Sentinel: "Oil group cleans spill in Clark County" |publisher=Jsonline.com |date=January 4, 2007 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130520082146/http://www.jsonline.com/business/29254864.html |archivedate=May 20, 2013 }}</ref><ref name="phmsa.dot.gov">{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2012-5017H |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Corrective_Action_Order_073012.pdf |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130222200918/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Corrective_Action_Order_073012.pdf |archivedate=February 22, 2013 }}</ref>
* On February 2, a construction crew struck an [[Enbridge]] pipeline in [[Rusk County, Wisconsin]] with equipment, spilling {{convert|4800|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil, of which only 2,066 barrels were recovered.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_11169.html?nocache=8539#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |publisher=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028021252/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_11169.html?nocache=8539 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref> Some of the oil filled a hole more than {{convert|20|ft|m}} deep and was reported to have contaminated the local water table.<ref>{{cite web|last=Bergquist |first=Lee |url=http://www.jsonline.com/news/wisconsin/29343664.html |title=Milwaukee Journal Sentinel: "Oil spill tainted water table" |publisher=Jsonline.com |date=February 16, 2007 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130520084215/http://www.jsonline.com/news/wisconsin/29343664.html |archivedate=May 20, 2013 }}</ref>
* On February 17, in a rural area of [[Harris County, Texas]], a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] transmission pipeline was damaged, and later exploded and burned. Grass fires spread across a three-square mile rural area.<ref name="YouTube">{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aiWC5FMjHv8 |title=Pipeline Fire |website=[[YouTube]] |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140705194810/http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aiWC5FMjHv8 |archivedate=July 5, 2014 }}</ref> The 31-inch natural gas pipeline leaked after a bulldozer hit it. Residents reported a loud explosion that shook houses enough to set off car alarms, as well as a rumbling sound and a bright orange fireball in the sky. Firefighters "backfilled" the break with nitrogen.<ref>{{cite web|title=Gas explosion rocks northwest Harris County |url=http://www.chron.com/news/houston-texas/article/Gas-explosion-rocks-northwest-Harris-County-1583763.php |website=Houston Chronicle |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=bot: unknown |archiveurl=https://archive.is/20161128012005/http://www.chron.com/news/houston-texas/article/Gas-explosion-rocks-northwest-Harris-County-1583763.php |archivedate=November 28, 2016 |df= }}</ref> PHMSA reported 1 person injured.<ref>TGP, Pipeline & Hazardous Materials Safety Administration, http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141030030518/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/ |date=October 30, 2014 }}.</ref>
* On March 29, near [[Yutan, Nebraska]], a pipeline was hit by construction equipment. About 1,697 barrels of natural gasoline were lost.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.1011now.com/news/headlines/64223167.html |title=Pipeline Firm Sues Excavator over 2007 Leak |agency=Associated Press |work=1011now.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115901/http://www.1011now.com/news/headlines/64223167.html |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref><ref name="ens-newswire.com">{{cite web|url=http://ens-newswire.com/2012/06/04/pipeline-companies-fined-1-million-for-spills-in-three-states/ |title=– Pipeline Companies Fined $1 Million for Spills in Three States – ENS |work=ens-newswire.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://ens-newswire.com/2012/06/04/pipeline-companies-fined-1-million-for-spills-in-three-states/ |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 27, a 22-inch gas transmission pipeline failed near [[Pawnee, Illinois]]. The failure ejected a 109 inch long section of pipe, and, releasing 38&nbsp;mmcf of natural gas that ignited. The rupture and resulting fire required the evacuation of a residence and the death of farm animals. The failure was due to external corrosion.<ref name="dot3">{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2014-10088 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320141008S/320141008S_Notice%20of%20Proposed%20Safety%20Order_12242014.pdf |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150115105300/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320141008S/320141008S_Notice%20of%20Proposed%20Safety%20Order_12242014.pdf |archivedate=January 15, 2015 }}</ref>
* On May 4, a backhoe helping to lay a gas pipeline hit another gas pipeline in [[Weatherford, Texas]]. The gas ignited, sending flames hundreds of feet into the air. Vehicles, equipment, and power lines in the area were destroyed, but, there were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2457&dat=20070313&id=PME8AAAAIBAJ&sjid=JC4MAAAAIBAJ&pg=1435,3195635|title=Bangor Daily News – Google News Archive Search|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On May 16, about {{convert|63,000|USgal|L}} of gasoline spilled into an old stripping pit that covers a three-acre area in [[Coal Township, Pennsylvania]]. The Kerris and Helfrick company owns the property where the gas leak occurred, and the excavator, was working for the company when he accidentally ruptured the Sunoco Logistics 14-inch petroleum pipeline. The gasoline was mostly absorbed into areas of soil, fill and coal strippings at the site.<ref>{{cite web|title=Leak in Jackson Township, Tioga County in the NCRO weekly report |url=http://dothemountain.wordpress.com/2009/10/16/spill-in-jackson-township-tioga-county-in-the-ncro-weekly-report/ |website=How Should We Do the Mountain? |accessdate=27 November 2016 |date=16 October 2009 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161019064755/https://dothemountain.wordpress.com/2009/10/16/spill-in-jackson-township-tioga-county-in-the-ncro-weekly-report/ |archivedate=October 19, 2016 }}</ref> Several residents made U.S. Rep. Christopher P. Carney aware of complaints about gasoline odors in residential basements. "Moreover, many residents are legitimately concerned about groundwater contamination as well as a host of future problems associated with the spill", Carney wrote to Department of Environmental Protection Secretary Kathleen McGinty.{{citation needed|date=November 2016}} The pipeline was installed in 1964 by the Atlantic Richfield Co.(ARCO) and purchased in 1990 by Sunoco. On September 29, the PADEP Environmental Cleanup program finalized a consent order and agreement with Mallard Contracting, which included a $45,000 civil penalty covering both DEP's response costs and a fine for violations of the Pa. Solid Waste Management Act.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://newsitem.com/news/small-gas-leak-on-little-mountain-posed-no-danger-1.1604903 |title=Small gas leak on Little Mountain posed no danger |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020064607/http://newsitem.com/news/small-gas-leak-on-little-mountain-posed-no-danger-1.1604903 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* In August, a gas compressor turbine caught fire inside BP's Gathering Center 1 in [[Alaska]], after an oil hose ruptured and spewed flammable liquid across the motor. A mechanic on patrol in the facility — seeing smoke — fled the room as the turbine burst into flames. Automatic fire and gas alarms were never triggered. A subsequent investigation by Alaska state authorities found that a ruptured hydraulic oil hose was Jerry-rigged in a position that chaffed against the turbine's hot engine. The investigation also found that the facility's fire and gas detectors were not powered on at the time.<ref>{{cite web|author= |url=http://www.alaskadispatch.com/article/bp-alaska-facilities-still-risk?page=0,1 |title=BP Alaska facilities still at risk |publisher=Alaska Dispatch |date=November 7, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028011305/http://www.alaskadispatch.com/article/bp-alaska-facilities-still-risk?page=0%2C1 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On October 8, a gas pipeline at a gas storage facility in [[Salem, Michigan]] ruptured and caught fire. Siding was melted on nearby houses.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wzzm13.com/news/article/82016/14/Investigation-begins-into-what-caused-natural-gas-explosion|archive-url=https://archive.is/20131218230754/http://www.wzzm13.com/news/article/82016/14/Investigation-begins-into-what-caused-natural-gas-explosion|dead-url=yes|archive-date=December 18, 2013|title=Investigation begins into what caused natural gas explosion|work=wzzm13.com|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On October 18, an ethylene pipeline explosion early, was heard for miles around [[Port Arthur, Texas]], waking residents. The following fire spread to a nearby butadiene pipeline, causing it to rupture and burn. Later, over 300 residents sued the pipeline's owners for health issues claimed to be caused from the chemicals released by the accident. External corrosion of the ethylene pipeline caused the first pipeline failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.liveleak.com/view?i=84c_1192763205 |title=Dow Chemical Ethylene Pipe Explodes in Port Arthur, Texas |publisher=LiveLeak.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130426074056/http://www.liveleak.com/view?i=84c_1192763205 |archivedate=April 26, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|author=Ryan Myers |url=http://www.beaumontenterprise.com/news/article/Pipeline-explosion-spurs-lawsuit-770820.php |title=Pipeline explosion spurs lawsuit |publisher=Beaumont Enterprise |date=October 2, 2008 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027214641/http://www.beaumontenterprise.com/news/article/Pipeline-explosion-spurs-lawsuit-770820.php |archivedate=October 27, 2013 }}</ref>
* On November 1, a 12-inch propane pipeline exploded, killing two people, and injuring five others, near [[Carmichael, Mississippi|Carmichael]] in the southeast portion of [[Clarke County, Mississippi]]. The NTSB determined the probable cause was an LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam failure. During hydrostatic testing of the pipeline after repair, another LF-ERW seam failed nearby. Inadequate education of residents near the pipeline about the existence of this pipeline, and how to respond to a pipeline accident, were also cited as a factors in the deaths.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR0901.aspx |title=Pipeline Accident Report PAR-09-01 |work=ntsb.gov |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150922142551/http://ntsb.gov/investigations/AccidentReports/Pages/PAR0901.aspx |archivedate=September 22, 2015 }}</ref>
* On November 12, three teenaged boys drilled into an ammonia pipeline, in [[Tampa Bay, Florida]], causing a major ammonia leak. They later claimed they did it due to stories of money being hidden inside that pipeline. The leak took two days to be capped. One of the teens had serious chemical burns from the ammonia. Residents within a half miles from the leak were evacuated. PHMSA later noted the pipeline company failed to adequately plan for emergencies with the local Fire Agency, as required by CFR 195.402(c)(12).<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 2-2008-6002 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220086002/220086002_FinalOrder_04262010.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211114341/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220086002/220086002_FinalOrder_04262010.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On November 13, [[Enbridge]] discovered a leak on their 34-inch Line 3, at Mile Post 912, near [[Clearbrook, Minnesota]]. Later, the pipeline exploded during repairs, on November 27, causing the deaths of two employees. DOT officials said that two Enbridge workers died in a crude oil explosion as they worked to make repairs on the former Lakehead system pipeline. Enbridge was cited for failing to safely and adequately perform maintenance and repair activities, clear the designated work area from possible sources of ignition, and hire properly trained and qualified workers.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.chron.com/business/article/Enbridge-fined-in-fatal-Minnesota-accident-1705992.php |title=Enbridge fined in fatal Minnesota accident – Houston Chronicle |publisher=Chron.com |date=August 18, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028012942/http://www.chron.com/business/article/Enbridge-fined-in-fatal-Minnesota-accident-1705992.php |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last=Griese |first=Noel |url=http://energypipelinenews.blogspot.com/2009/05/enbridge-will-appeal-24-million-fine.html |title=Energy Pipeline News: Enbridge will appeal $2.4 million fine levied for fatal Minnesota accident |publisher=Energypipelinenews.blogspot.com |date=May 8, 2009 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131107012920/http://energypipelinenews.blogspot.com/2009/05/enbridge-will-appeal-24-million-fine.html |archivedate=November 7, 2013 }}</ref>
* On November 21, a 30-inch gas transmission pipeline failed, near [[Haven, Kansas]]. The gas ignited, resulting in road closures.<ref name="dot3"/>
* On December 14, two men were driving east in a pickup truck, on Interstate 20, Near [[Delhi, Louisiana]], when a 30-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded. One of the men were killed, and the other injured. External corrosion was later identified as the cause of the failure.<ref>{{cite web |title=Attorney Matt Minner leads Hare Wynn team in achieving $3 million dollar settlement in explosion case |url=http://www.hwnn.com/news/76-attorney-matt-minner-leads-hare-wynn-team-in-achieving-3-million-dollar-settlement-in-explosion-case |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20100201024847/http://www.hwnn.com/news/76-attorney-matt-minner-leads-hare-wynn-team-in-achieving-3-million-dollar-settlement-in-explosion-case |archivedate=February 1, 2010}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.tuscaloosanews.com/article/20071215/NEWS/71215003 |title=Fayetteville man hurt in deadly Louisiana interstate blast |publisher=TuscaloosaNews.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131121033928/http://www.tuscaloosanews.com/article/20071215/NEWS/71215003 |archivedate=November 21, 2013 }}</ref>

=== 2008 ===
* On January 5, 2008, a pipeline ruptured at a filet weld, leaking natural gasoline in [[Oologah, Oklahoma]]. About 45,000 gallons of the gasoline was spill, with about 29,000 gallons being lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.federalregister.gov/articles/2010/02/22/2010-3318/notice-of-lodging-of-consent-decree-pursuant-to-the-clean-water-act#p-2 |title=Federal Register &#124; Notice of Lodging of Consent Decree Pursuant to the Clean Water Act |publisher=Federalregister.gov |date=February 22, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131101020153/https://www.federalregister.gov/articles/2010/02/22/2010-3318/notice-of-lodging-of-consent-decree-pursuant-to-the-clean-water-act |archivedate=November 1, 2013 }}</ref>
* On January 7, a pipeline split open, near [[Denver City, Texas]], spilling {{convert|1.3|e6USgal|m3}} of crude oil. The pipeline company failed to detect and stop the leak for more than 24 hours. [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam failure appears to be the cause.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272540 |title=Jan. 7, 2008 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272540 |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.chron.com/disp/story.mpl/front/7294570.html |title=Old pipelines are a hidden menace &#124; Energy &#124; Chron.com – Houston Chronicle |publisher=Chron.com |date=November 15, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref>
* On January 11, a Belle Fourche maintenance crew damaged its own pipeline, spill about 11,100 gallons of crude in [[Alexander, North Dakota]].<ref name=autogenerated1>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_1248.html?nocache=1673#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307110237/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_1248.html?nocache=1673 |archivedate=March 7, 2016 }}</ref>
* On February 5, a natural gas pipeline compressor station exploded and caught fire, near [[Hartsville, Tennessee]], and was believed to have been caused by a tornado hitting the facility.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.newschannel5.com/story/7833882/no-fatalities-from-gas-plant-explosion |title=No Fatalities From Gas Plant Explosion – NewsChannel5.com &#124; Nashville News, Weather and Sports |publisher=NewsChannel5.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131029040951/http://www.newschannel5.com/story/7833882/no-fatalities-from-gas-plant-explosion |archivedate=October 29, 2013}}</ref>
* On February 15, a 20-inch distillate pipeline exploded and burned in [[Hidalgo County, Texas]], closing road FM490.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.foxnews.com/story/2008/02/15/explosion-reported-at-south-texas-oil-pipeline.html |title=Explosion Reported at South Texas Oil Pipeline |work=Fox News |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://www.foxnews.com/story/2008/02/15/explosion-reported-at-south-texas-oil-pipeline.html |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 14, a house in a [[Columbia, Missouri]] neighborhood exploded in an explosion that could be felt for miles, causing fatal injuries to the elderly couple living there. Problems with the gas distribution line there were blamed for the explosion. Another house nearby also suffered damage.<ref>{{cite web|last=Michler |first=Caroline |url= http://www.columbiamissourian.com/stories/2012/09/09/sneed-trial-set-being-tuesday/ |title=Ameren Missouri wrongful death trial set to begin Tuesday |publisher=Columbia Missourian |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref>
* On May 16, a crew boring to install a new gas main hit an existing 4-inch gas line in [[McKinney, Texas]]. Escaping gas caused two houses to explode, and one other house to catch fire. Three people were burned from this incident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://dms.ntsb.gov/pubdms/search/document.cfm?docID=302926&docketID=46589&mkey=68687 |title=Document 1 DOT Incident Report (manually redacted) Filing Date November 06, 2008 3 page(s) of Text (PDF) Photos |publisher=Dms.ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://dms.ntsb.gov/pubdms/search/document.cfm?docID=302926&docketID=46589&mkey=68687 |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On July 28, the U.S. District Court for the Southern District of Illinois ordered Apex Oil Company Inc., to clean up ground water and soil contamination, at an expected cost of at least $150&nbsp;million. During the period 1967 through 1988, Apex Oil's legal predecessor, Clark Oil and Refining Corp., released gasoline from leaking pipelines and other spills, that commingled with other responsible parties' releases and resulted in the large plume of refined petroleum substances beneath [[Hartford, Illinois]]. Vapors from the underground plume of millions of gallons of leaked and spilled petroleum products have migrated into houses in the village, causing years of fires, explosions, and evacuations.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ens-newswire.com/ens/jul2008/2008-07-29-091.html |title=Apex Oil Ordered to Clean Soil, Water Under Illinois Village |publisher=ENS-Newswire.com |date=July 29, 2008 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028104405/http://www.ens-newswire.com/ens/jul2008/2008-07-29-091.html |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On August 10, a 20-inch crude oil pipeline ruptured near [[Golden Gate, Illinois]]. About 243,000 gallons of crude were spilled, with about 33,000 gallons being lost. The cause was listed as a pipe seam failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_32147.html?nocache=8922#_Incidents_tab_4 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |publisher=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028025105/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_32147.html?nocache=8922 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2008/08/11/refinery-operations-marathon-catlettsbur-idUKN1148743220080811 |agency=Reuters |first=Rebekah |last=Kebede |title=Marathon KY refinery cuts rates after pipe leak |date=August 11, 2008 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028004604/http://uk.reuters.com/article/2008/08/11/refinery-operations-marathon-catlettsbur-idUKN1148743220080811 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.courierpress.com/news/2008/aug/12/workers-cleaning-up-illinois-oil-spill-crude/ |title=Workers cleaning up Illinois oil spill; crude valued around $525,000 " Evansville Courier and Press |publisher=Courierpress.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027214501/http://www.courierpress.com/news/2008/aug/12/workers-cleaning-up-illinois-oil-spill-crude/ |archivedate=October 27, 2013}}</ref>
* On August 25, a 24-inch gas transmission pipeline failed in a rural area west of [[Pilot Grove, Missouri]]. The longitudinal rupture in the pipe body created a 50 foot by 33-foot by 7-foot deep crater in the ground. The cause of the rupture was external corrosion.<ref name="dot3"/>
* On August 28, a 36-inch gas pipeline failed near [[Stairtown, Texas]], causing a fire with flames {{convert|400|ft|m}} tall. The failure was caused by external corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_32099.html?nocache=5038#_SignificantIncidents_tab_5 |title=PHMSA Stakeholder Communications: Operator Information – Incident and Mileage Data |publisher=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028025239/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_32099.html?nocache=5038 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Gas pipeline fire burns out in Caldwell County |url=http://www.texas-fire.com/2008/08/28/gas-pipeline-fire-burns-out-in-caldwell-county/ |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20081005101051/http://www.texas-fire.com/2008/08/28/gas-pipeline-fire-burns-out-in-caldwell-county/ |archivedate=October 5, 2008}}</ref>
* On August 29, a 24-inch gas transmission pipeline ruptured in [[Cooper County, Missouri]]. Corrosion had caused the pipeline to lose 75% of its wall thickness in the failure area.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Panhandle_Eastern_GT_MO_508_2008-08-25.pdf |title=Pipeline Failure Investigation Report |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161031030013/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Panhandle_Eastern_GT_MO_508_2008-08-25.pdf |archivedate=October 31, 2016 }}</ref>
* On September 9, workers constructing a new pipeline hit an existing natural gas pipeline in [[Wheeler County, Texas]]. Two workers were burned by this accident.<ref>{{cite web|author=Janelle Stecklein |url=http://amarillo.com/stories/091008/new_news4.shtml |title=Gas explosion burns 2 |publisher=Amarillo Globe-News |date=September 10, 2008 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028043834/http://amarillo.com/stories/091008/new_news4.shtml |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On September 14, a 30-inch [[Williams Companies]] gas pipeline ruptured and gas ignited near [[Appomattox, Virginia]]. Two houses were destroyed by the fire. External corrosion was the cause of the failure.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 1-2008-1004H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120081004H/120081004H_CAO_09252008.pdf?nocache=8422 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304074321/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120081004H/120081004H_CAO_09252008.pdf?nocache=8422 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wset.com/story/15465084/anniversary-of-gas-pipeline-explosion-in-appomattox |title=Three Years Later, Residents Moved on After Gas Pipeline Explosi – WSET.com – ABC13 |publisher=WSET.com |date=September 14, 2011 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028043822/http://www.wset.com/story/15465084/anniversary-of-gas-pipeline-explosion-in-appomattox |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On September 23, a ruptured pipeline causes a fire at a Pipeline Terminal in [[Pasadena, Texas]]. One worker was killed, and another injured, with about {{convert|190,000|USgal|L}} of product being lost. The failure was caused by internal corrosion.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2008/09/24/kindermorgan-fire-longhornpipeline-idUSN2444404820080924 |agency=Reuters |first=Janet |last=McGurty |title=Longhorn Pipeline stops fuel flow due to fire |date=September 24, 2008 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028003314/https://www.reuters.com/article/2008/09/24/kindermorgan-fire-longhornpipeline-idUSN2444404820080924 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_26041.html?nocache=5118#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |publisher=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028022658/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_26041.html?nocache=5118 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On October 3, a crew working on a Turnpike expansion drill into a [[Colonial Pipeline]] petroleum products pipeline, in [[Hamilton Township, Mercer County, New Jersey|Hamilton, New Jersey]]. About 35,000 gallons of Diesel fuel were spilled, with 100 gallons not recovered.<ref>{{cite web|author=JEFF TRENTLY |url=http://www.nj.com/news/times/regional/index.ssf?/base/news-14/122317953084150.xml&coll=5 |title=Cleanup of oil spill continues |publisher=NJ.com |date=October 5, 2008 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121014022220/http://www.nj.com/news/times/regional/index.ssf?%2Fbase%2Fnews-14%2F122317953084150.xml&coll=5 |archivedate=October 14, 2012 }}</ref><ref name="dot5">{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_2552.html?nocache=7343#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307113746/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_2552.html?nocache=7343 |archivedate=March 7, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 3, construction equipment hit a Mid Valley Pipeline Company pipeline in [[Florence, Kentucky]], spilling 3,650 barrels of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272783 |title=Oct. 3, 2008 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140407074451/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272783 |archivedate=April 7, 2014 }}</ref>
* On the night of November 15, a gas compressor for a pipeline at an entry exploded and burned near [[Godley, Texas]]. The fire spread to another company's gas compressor station next to it. A 24-inch gas pipeline had to be shut down to stop the fire. There were no injuries, and damages were estimated at $2&nbsp;million.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cleburnetimesreview.com/godley/x489007782/Compressor-station-blows-up |archive-url=https://archive.is/20120730225554/http://www.cleburnetimesreview.com/godley/x489007782/Compressor-station-blows-up |archive-date=July 30, 2012 |title=Compressor station blows up |deadurl=no |accessdate=July 18, 2013}}</ref>
* On November 25, a gasoline release from a [[Sunoco]] petroleum pipeline occurred, near a retail mall in [[Murrysville, Pennsylvania]]. Officials said the release occurred from the 6-inch line at about 9:30&nbsp;a.m. while a Sunoco Logistics crew was working on a ball valve. It was suspected the ball valve was improperly installed. The failure resulted in the evacuation of numerous stores, restaurants and roads in the immediate vicinity due to the dousing of gasoline and subsequent vapors emitting from the {{convert|11,760|USgal|L}} of spilled product.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://triblive.com/news/adminpage/5709670-74/sunoco-dep-board#axzz3GD7wewpI |title=Sunoco faces $2.3 million DEP fine for Murrysville pipeline leak |work=TribLIVE.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://triblive.com/news/adminpage/5709670-74/sunoco-dep-board |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On December 5, a driver of a vehicle went off of a road, and struck a valve on an [[AMOCO]] gasoline pipeline in [[Colon, Michigan]]. The driver was killed, and, the fire burned for several days. About 14,000 gallons of gasoline were burned, or lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mlive.com/news/kalamazoo/index.ssf/2008/12/driver_killed_as_vehicle_hits.html |title=Driver killed as vehicle hits Colon gas pipeline; fire expected to burn all weekend |author= |date= |work=MLive.com |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307181932/http://www.mlive.com/news/kalamazoo/index.ssf/2008/12/driver_killed_as_vehicle_hits.html |archivedate=March 7, 2016 }}</ref><ref name="dot6">{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_395.html?nocache=1547#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307180912/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_395.html?nocache=1547 |archivedate=March 7, 2016 }}</ref>

=== 2009 ===
* On January 4, 2009, a 6.625-inch storage well line operated by [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] Company in Elk View (near Charleston), Kanawha County, West Virginia, ruptured due to internal corrosion pitting complicated by low impact toughness of the pipe material, causing $29,011 in damage.<ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report – Columbia Gas Transmission Well Line Rupture Failure Date: 01/04/2009 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/CGT_GT_WV_20090104.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161127220640/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/CGT_GT_WV_20090104.pdf |archivedate=November 27, 2016 }}</ref>
* On January 15, an accidental massive gas release at Pump Station 1 of the trans-Alaskan pipeline by [[Alyeska Pipeline Service Company]] threatened the site at the time. The company that runs the pipeline acknowledges a fire or explosion, had the gas ignited, could have imperiled the station's 60-plus workers and caused "an extended shutdown" of oil fields. There was no ignition or explosion. The incident occurred as BP workers used a cleaning device called a pig to swab oil out of an old pipeline the company was preparing to decommission. The 34-inch pipe was among major Prudhoe trunk lines found in 2006 to be ravaged with corrosion, due to BP's admitted lack of proper maintenance. A large volume of gas then bypassed the pig somehow, and rushed to Pump Station 1, a key asset through which every drop of oil coming off the North Slope must pass.<ref>{{cite web|first=Wesley |last=Loy |url=http://www.adn.com/2009/02/06/682090/inquiry-launched-after-pump-station.html |title=Inquiry launched after pump station accident |publisher=ADN.com |date=February 6, 2009 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130927144559/http://www.adn.com/2009/02/06/682090/inquiry-launched-after-pump-station.html |archivedate=September 27, 2013}}</ref>
* On February 11, a gas pipeline exploded and burned near a natural gas treatment plant, near [[Carthage, Texas]]. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2009/02/11/explosion-dcp-texas-idUKN1135208520090211 |agency=Reuters |title=UPDATE 1-Explosion near DCP Midstream's Texas natgas plant |date=February 11, 2009 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028005229/http://uk.reuters.com/article/2009/02/11/explosion-dcp-texas-idUKN1135208520090211 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On February 19, leaking gas was detected near homes, in [[Somerset, Massachusetts]]. Evacuations followed, but one resident who did not respond to knocking on doors was killed, when the gas exploded. Prior excavation damage to a gas main was the cause.<ref>http://archive.boston.com/news/local/massachusetts/articles/2009/02/21/before_explosion_gas_crew_waved_off_help/</ref>
* At approximately 5&nbsp;p.m. on February 18, a rupture of pipeline near the pump station and terminal located in [[Cygnet, Ohio]], owned by Philadelphia-based [[Sunoco]], resulted in one of the largest oil spills in Wood County history.<ref>{{cite web|title=Press release by Sunoco Logistics |url=http://www.wtol.com/story/9873737/press-release-by-sunoco-logistics |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170219083344/http://www.wtol.com/story/9873737/press-release-by-sunoco-logistics |archivedate=February 19, 2017 }}</ref> Upon learning of the release, the company immediately shut down the pipeline, stopped operations at the pump station and terminal, notified the appropriate authorities, and began an emergency response. As of 11:05&nbsp;a.m. ET on February 19, the release had been stopped from the pipe. The damaged pipeline, which was operating at the time, released {{convert|1250|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil into a farm field. Eventually, 782 of the {{convert|1250|oilbbl|m3}} released were recovered. Some of the crude oil, approximately {{convert|200|oilbbl|m3}}, did contaminate a local creek. There were no fatalities, or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.toledoblade.com/article/20100730/NEWS16/7290358 |title=Ohio, Michigan score among highest for states with oil spills |publisher=Toledoblade.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Pipeline Failure Investigation Report – 2-18-2009 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Mid_Valley_HL_OH_2009-02-18_508.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170201174551/http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Mid_Valley_HL_OH_2009-02-18_508.pdf |archivedate=February 1, 2017 }}</ref>
* On May 4, [[Kinder Morgan]]'s Florida Gas Transmission pipeline burst near Palm City and [[Hobe City, Florida|Hobe City]] (near [[Port Salerno, Florida]]). The explosion ejected 106 feet of buried pipe weighing about 5,000 pounds out of the ground and onto the right-of-way between Interstate 95 and the Florida Turnpike (SR-91). The rupture was near a high school that was within the 366-foot potential impact radius. Two people were injured when their car ran off the road, and a Sheriff's deputy walked through a dense cloud and inhaled natural gas. The escaping gas did not ignite. The leak caused $596,218 in property damage. FGT was cited for safety violations: failing to identify a high-consequence area, failing to test operators for alcohol and drugs, and failing to have prompt emergency response; PHMSA assessed a $95,000 fine.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 2-2009-1002H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220091002H/220091002H_CAO_05072009.pdf?nocache=4283 |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304080826/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220091002H/220091002H_CAO_05072009.pdf?nocache=4283 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On May 5, a natural gas pipeline exploded and caught on fire, near [[Rockville, Indiana]] in Parke County, about {{convert|24|mi|km}} north of [[Terre Haute, Indiana]]. The cause of this failure was determined to be external corrosion. Additional work performed as a result of this order provided significant indications of external corrosion in various sections of this line. Pictures have been released around the area showing the damage caused. 52 people were evacuated in a one-mile (1.6&nbsp;km) area of the explosion. No injuries reported.<ref name="dot3"/><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2009-1009H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320091009H/320091009H_CAO_05132009.pdf?nocache=6515 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304070206/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320091009H/320091009H_CAO_05132009.pdf?nocache=6515 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On May 21, an [[Enbridge]] pipeline pig sending trap in [[Superior, Wisconsin]] leaked from operator error, spilling about 6500 gallons of crude oil. 700 cubic yards of contaminated soil had to be removed.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF 3-2012-5018 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320125018/320125018_NOPV%20PCP_08272012.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161224081623/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320125018/320125018_NOPV%20PCP_08272012.pdf |archivedate=December 24, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272967 |title=May 21, 2009 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/272967 |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On July 15, an explosion occurred at Kinder Morgan's Midcontinent Express pipeline natural gas metering station that was under construction, while it was being pressure tested with nitrogen, in [[Smith County, Mississippi]]. One worker was killed, and two others injured. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kltv.com/Global/story.asp?s=10741392&clienttype=printable |title=Pipeline accident investigation could take months – KLTV.com-Tyler, Longview, Jacksonville, Texas &#124; ETX News |publisher=Kltv.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027225750/http://www.kltv.com/Global/story.asp?s=10741392&clienttype=printable |archivedate=October 27, 2013 }}</ref> The workers were "literally right on top" of the explosion; their injuries were caused by pressure, not heat. One worker was injured when part of the pipe fell on him. The explosion snapped and bent a pipeline connected to a massive separator unit which was slung several yards.<ref>{{cite web|title=Pipeline explodes,killed 1 injured 3 |url=https://www.industrialprojectsreport.com/forum/showthread.php?8590-Pipeline-explodes-killed-1-injured-3 |website=www.industrialprojectsreport.com |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304024817/https://www.industrialprojectsreport.com/forum/showthread.php?8590-Pipeline-explodes-killed-1-injured-3 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On August 10, operators of a Belle Fourche pipeline incorrectly operated the line, causing it to fail, near [[Edgerton, Wyoming]]. About 30,000 gallons of crude oil were spill, with about 1,200 gallons being lost.<ref name="dot4"/>
* On August 17, a pipeline was found leaking by an aerial patrol in Atoka County, Oklahoma. {{convert|50|oilbbl|m3}} of diesel fuel were estimated to have been released as a result of this accident, and none of it was recovered.<ref>{{cite web|title=Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety Administration – November 2, 2010 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Explorer_HL_OK_2009-08-17_508.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161127220057/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Explorer_HL_OK_2009-08-17_508.pdf |archivedate=November 27, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 7, a leaking pipeline carrying jet fuel was accidentally ignited by a pipeline repair crew in [[Upton County, Texas]].<ref>{{cite web |title=Upton County Gas Line Fire Caused by Leak |url=http://www.texas-fire.com/2009/10/08/upton-county-gas-line-fire-caused-by-leak/ |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120315222201/http://www.texas-fire.com/2009/10/upton-county-gas-line-fire-caused-by-leak/ |archivedate=March 15, 2012}}</ref>
* On October 28, [[Kinder Morgan]]'s Natural Gas Pipeline Company of America above-ground storage tank north of St. Elmo, [[Illinois]] caught fire, injuring two workers. Welding caused the tank to ignite resulting in several explosions. Two workers were taken to the hospital.<ref>{{cite web|title=Fire rocks plant north of St. Elmo|url=http://www.effinghamdailynews.com/news/local_news/fire-rocks-plant-north-of-st-elmo/article_944c2536-0733-5549-ba26-baacb0e805a2.html|website=Effingham Daily News|accessdate=28 November 2016}}</ref>
* On November 5, two people were hurt when an [[El Paso Natural Gas]] pipeline exploded in the Texas Panhandle near [[Bushland, Texas]]. The explosion left a hole about 30 yards by 20 yards and close to {{convert|15|ft|m}} deep. The orange inferno rose about 700 feet in the air; the blast incinerated the home of the Jose Torres family, injuring his wife Agnieszka and daughter Franczeska. About 200 residents in the area were evacuated. Bushland is in Potter County, about {{convert|15|mi|km}} west of Amarillo. The failure was in an abandoned tap, but the exact failure reason remains unknown. The explosion cause $436,136 in property damage.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2009-1021H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420091021H/420091021H_CAO_11102009.pdf?nocache=4008 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304070338/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420091021H/420091021H_CAO_11102009.pdf?nocache=4008 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|author= |url=http://www.firefightingnews.com/articlePSO-US.cfm?articleID=72461 |title=Home Destroyed In Texas Gas Line Blast |publisher=Firefightingnews.com |date=November 5, 2009 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027202708/http://www.firefightingnews.com/articlePSO-US.cfm?articleID=72461 |archivedate=October 27, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|author1=Kevin Welch |author2=JC Cortez |title=Bushland gas release reminds residents of 2009 explosion |publisher=Amarillo Globe-News |url=http://amarillo.com/news/local-news/2014-06-25/bushland-neighborhood-evacuated-after-gas-pipeline-rupture |accessdate=January 19, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160128012018/http://amarillo.com/news/local-news/2014-06-25/bushland-neighborhood-evacuated-after-gas-pipeline-rupture |archivedate=January 28, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2009-1021H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420091021H/420091021H_Closure_04132011.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170301004014/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420091021H/420091021H_Closure_04132011.pdf |archivedate=March 1, 2017 }}</ref>
* On November 14, a fire at a gas compressor station near [[Cameron, West Virginia]] slightly burned one employee, and causes $5.6&nbsp;million of damage to the facility.<ref>{{cite web|title=Columbia Gas Transmission – Adaline Compressor Station Fire Failure Date 11/14/2009 |url=http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Pipeline/Columbia_GasTrans_GT_WV_2009-11-14.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161002040127/http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Pipeline/Columbia_GasTrans_GT_WV_2009-11-14.pdf |archivedate=October 2, 2016 }}</ref>
* Also on November 14, 2009, a newly built 42-inch gas transmission pipeline near [[Philo, Ohio]] failed on the second day of operation. There was no fire, but evacuations resulted. Several indications of pipe deformation were found.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2009-1024H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320091024H/320091024H_CAO_02172010.pdf?nocache=1083 |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304070254/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320091024H/320091024H_CAO_02172010.pdf?nocache=1083 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2009-1024H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320091024H/320091024H_Notice%20of%20Proposed%20CAO_12212009.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211184749/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/reports/enforce/documents/320091024H/320091024H_Notice%20of%20Proposed%20CAO_12212009.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* From December 3 to 4, a [[Minnesota Pipeline]] carrying crude oil leaked in [[Todd County, Minnesota]], spilling about 5,000 barrels of crude. Pipeline workers on December 3 had been repairing sections of the 16-inch pipe in a rural area, left on the afternoon of December 3, and the spill occurred during the evening hours of December 3–4.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://energypipelinenews.blogspot.com/2009/12/kochs-mpc-line-spills-210000-gallons-of.html |title=Energy Pipeline News |author=Noel Griese |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141218170946/http://energypipelinenews.blogspot.com/2009/12/kochs-mpc-line-spills-210000-gallons-of.html |archivedate=December 18, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/273107 |title=Dec. 4, 2009 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20151031141013/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/273107 |archivedate=October 31, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.staplesworld.com/news/2009-12-10/front_page/001.html |title=Pipeline leaks 210,000 gallons of oil – www.staplesworld.com – Staples World |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141016232028/http://www.staplesworld.com/news/2009-12-10/front_page/001.html |archivedate=October 16, 2014}}</ref>
* On December 23, a crude oil pipeline started leaking in [[Galveston, Texas]]. There was no fire or explosion as a result of the accident, and an estimated {{convert|120|oilbbl|m3}} of crude oil were released to the environment.<ref>{{cite web|title=Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety Administration  – September 29, 2010 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Enterprise%20HL%20TX%202009-12-23.pdf |accessdate=27 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161127215948/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Enterprise%20HL%20TX%202009-12-23.pdf |archivedate=November 27, 2016 }}</ref>
== 2010s ==

=== 2010 ===
* On January 2, [[Enbridge]]'s Line 2 ruptured near [[Neche, North Dakota]], releasing about 3,784 barrels of crude oil, of which 2,237 barrels of were recovered. The cause was a material defect.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_11169.html?nocache=5280#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |publisher=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130602185558/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_11169.html?nocache=5280 |archivedate=June 2, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2010-5001H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320105001H/320105001H_CAO_01192010.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170215110410/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320105001H/320105001H_CAO_01192010.pdf |archivedate=February 15, 2017 }}</ref>
* On January 7, a gas pipeline exploded near [[Barksdale Air Force Base]], Louisiana, in January, killing a pipeline employee.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.airforcetimes.com/news/2010/01/ap_airforce_barksdale_explosion_010710/ |archive-url=https://archive.is/20120720212631/http://www.airforcetimes.com/news/2010/01/ap_airforce_barksdale_explosion_010710/ |dead-url=yes |archive-date=July 20, 2012 |title=Pipeline explosion at Barksdale kills civilian – Air Force News &#124; News from Afghanistan & Iraq |publisher=Air Force Times|agency=Associated Press|date= January 7, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref>
* On February 1, a plumber trying to unclog a sewer line in [[St. Paul, Minnesota]] ruptured a gas service line that has been "cross bored" through the house's sewer line. The plumber and resident escape the house moments before as an explosion and following fire destroyed the house. The Minnesota Office of Pipeline Safety ordered that gas utility, Xcel, to check for more cross bored gas lines. In the following year, 25,000 sewer lines inspected showed 57 other cross bored gas lines. In [[Louisville, Kentucky]], 430 gas line cross bores were found in {{convert|200|mi|km}} of a sewer project, including some near schools and a hospital. The NTSB had cited such cross bore incidents as a known hazard since 1976.<ref>{{cite web |title=A year later, gas line checks continue |publisher=StarTribune.com |url=http://www.startribune.com/local/115153164.html |archive-url=https://archive.is/20130203061257/http://www.startribune.com/local/115153164.html |dead-url=yes |archive-date=February 3, 2013 |accessdate=May 14, 2012}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.crossboresafety.org/history.htm |title=History |publisher=CrossboreSafety.org |date=February 9, 1999 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130417114346/http://www.crossboresafety.org/history.htm |archivedate=April 17, 2013 }}</ref>
* On February 7,  a power plant explosion occurred at the Kleen Energy Systems, killing 5 and injuring a dozen.  [[2010 Connecticut power plant explosion]]
* On February 25, a natural gas liquids (NGL) pipeline ruptured near [[Pond Creek, Oklahoma]], releasing over {{convert|575,000|USgal|L}} of NGL's, and forcing road closures. There was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://enidnews.com/localnews/x1004926657/Highway-closed-for-gas-leak |title=Highway closed for gas leak " Local news " The Enid News and Eagle, Enid, OK |publisher=Enidnews.com |date=February 25, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_32109.html?nocache=3139#_OuterPanel_tab_2 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |publisher=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028010325/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_32109.html?nocache=3139 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* On March 1, at about 8:10&nbsp;am, Mid-Valley Pipeline identified a release of crude oil in the manifold area of the Mid-Valley tank farm in [[Longview, Texas]]. Crude oil was observed "gushing" from the soil in the manifold area. About 198 barrels of crude oil were estimated to have been released and 196 barrels were recovered from the secondary containment area within Mid-Valley's site.<ref>[http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/Mid-Valley%20Pipeline%20HL%20TX%202010-03-01%20508.pdf Failure Investigation Report – Mid-Valley Pipeline Internal Corrosion] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120402093120/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/Mid-Valley%20Pipeline%20HL%20TX%202010-03-01%20508.pdf |date=April 2, 2012 }} Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety Administration, November 7, 2011, accessed September 5, 2015, 31 pages</ref>

The area was under the control of the Operator in a fenced off area that is off-limits to the public.<ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report – Sunoco R&M Flange Gasket 03/25/2010 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/Sunoco%20RM%20HL%20PA%202010-03-25.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170203111219/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/Sunoco%20RM%20HL%20PA%202010-03-25.pdf |archivedate=February 3, 2017 }}</ref>

* On June 7, a 36-inch gas pipeline explosion and fire in [[Johnson County, Texas]], was caused by workers installing poles for electrical lines. One worker killed, and six were injured. Confusion over the location and status of the construction work lead to the pipeline not being marked beforehand.<ref name="texasobserver.org">{{cite web|last=Wilder |first=Forrest |url=http://www.texasobserver.org/cover-story/the-fire-down-below |title=The Fire Down Below |publisher=The Texas Observer |date=November 26, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120925193438/http://www.texasobserver.org///cover-story/the-fire-down-below |archivedate=September 25, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.platts.com/RSSFeedDetailedNews/RSSFeed/HeadlineNews/NaturalGas/6158630|archiveurl=https://archive.is/20120907022650/http://www.platts.com/RSSFeedDetailedNews/RSSFeed/HeadlineNews/NaturalGas/6158630|deadurl=yes|title=Platts: RSS Feed Detailed News|date=September 7, 2012|archivedate=September 7, 2012|publisher=}}</ref>

* On July 26, the [[Kalamazoo River oil spill]]: Enbridge Energy Partners LLP ([[Enbridge]]), reported that a {{convert|30|in|adj=on}} pipeline belonging to Enbridge burst in [[Marshall, Michigan]]. Enbridge had numerous alarms from the affected Line 6B, but controllers thought the alarms were from phase separation, and the leak was not reported to Enbridge for 17 hours. Enbridge estimates over {{convert|800,000|USgal|L}} of crude oil leaked into Talmadge Creek, a waterway that feeds the [[Kalamazoo River]],<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.epa.gov/enbridgespill/index.html |title=U.S. EPA "EPA Response to Enbridge Spill in Michigan" |publisher=Epa.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130413130556/http://www.epa.gov/enbridgespill/index.html |archivedate=April 13, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://issuu.com/toledoblade/docs/07302010_the_blade |title=Archived copy |accessdate=May 14, 2012 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121007172122/http://issuu.com/toledoblade/docs/07302010_the_blade |archivedate=October 7, 2012}}</ref> whereas EPA reports over 1,139,569 gallons of oil have been recovered as of November 2011.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://epa.gov/enbridgespill/ |title=EPA Response to Enbridge Spill in Michigan &#124; US EPA |publisher=Epa.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130327022924/http://www.epa.gov/enbridgespill/ |archivedate=March 27, 2013 }}</ref> On July 27, 2010, an Administrative Order was issued by U.S. EPA requiring the performance of removal actions in connection with the facility. The Order requires Enbridge to immediately conduct removal of a discharge or to mitigate or prevent a substantial threat of a discharge of oil and to submit a Work Plan for the cleanup activities that was to include a Health and Safety Plan,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.battlecreekenquirer.com/assets/pdf/A5162632817.PDF |title=U.S. EPA REMOVAL ADMINISTRATIVE ORDER UNDER SECTION 311(c) OF THE CLEAN WATER ACT, REGION 5 |format=PDF |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013}}{{dead link|date=May 2016}}</ref> as required by 29 CFR 1910.120 ([[HAZWOPER]]). In 2012, the NTSB later cited known but unrepaired cracks and external corrosion as the cause.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ntsb.gov/news/2012/120710.html |title=Press Release July 10, 2012 |publisher=Ntsb.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130403031649/http://www.ntsb.gov/news/2012/120710.html |archivedate=April 3, 2013}}</ref>
* On August 10, the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) and the Justice Department announced that Plains All American Pipeline and several of its operating subsidiaries have agreed to spend approximately $41&nbsp;million to upgrade {{convert|10,420|mi|km}} of crude oil pipeline operated in the United States. The settlement resolves Plains' Clean Water Act violations for ten crude oil spills in Texas, Louisiana, Oklahoma, and Kansas, and requires the company to pay a $3.25&nbsp;million civil penalty.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.epa.gov/compliance/resources/cases/civil/cwa/plainspipeline.html |title=Plains All American Pipeline Settlement &#124; Compliance and Enforcement &#124; US EPA |publisher=Epa.gov |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130413233436/http://www.epa.gov/compliance/resources/cases/civil/cwa/plainspipeline.html |archivedate=April 13, 2013}}</ref>
