* On September 9, 2010 [[San Bruno pipeline explosion|a high pressure gas pipeline exploded]] in [[San Bruno, California]], a suburb of San Francisco. The blast destroyed 38 houses and damaged 120 houses. Eight people died and many were injured. Ten acres of brush also burned. Later, PG&E was unable to supply the California Public Utilities Commission with documents on how PG&E established pressure limits on some of its gas transmission pipelines. It was also revealed that this pipeline had 26 leaks between Milpitas and San Francisco during the time of 1951 to 2009, with some of the leak causes listed in records as "unknown". Later hydrostatic testing of the same pipeline that failed found a pinhole leak, and a previously damaged section blew out.<ref>{{cite news|last=Wittenstein |first=Jeran |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/2010-09-10/san-francisco-neighborhood-engulfed-by-fire-after-gas-pipeline-explosion.html |title=Gas Explosion Engulfs Houses in San Francisco suburb of San Bruno |publisher=Bloomberg.com |date=September 10, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121103145956/http://www.bloomberg.com/news/2010-09-10/san-francisco-neighborhood-engulfed-by-fire-after-gas-pipeline-explosion.html |archivedate=November 3, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mercurynews.com/news/ci_16041191 |title=San Bruno explosion and fire kills 4, destroys 38 homes |publisher=Mercurynews.com |date=September 12, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121002215053/http://www.mercurynews.com/news/ci_16041191 |archivedate=October 2, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last=Worth |first=Katie |url=http://www.sfexaminer.com/local/bay-area/2011/03/pge-threatened-fines-1-million-pipeline-data |title=PG&E threatened with fines of $1 million for pipeline data &#124; Katie Worth &#124; Bay Area &#124; San Francisco Examiner |publisher=Sfexaminer.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130515150525/http://www.sfexaminer.com/local/bay-area/2011/03/pge-threatened-fines-1-million-pipeline-data |archivedate=May 15, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?f=/c/a/2011/10/22/MNU41LFO41.DTL |work=The San Francisco Chronicle |first=Jaxon |last=Van Derbeken |title=PG&E knew of many leaks in San Bruno pipeline |date=October 24, 2011 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20111231043835/http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?f=%2Fc%2Fa%2F2011%2F10%2F22%2FMNU41LFO41.DTL |archivedate=December 31, 2011 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2011/11/07/pacific-gas-electric-pipeline-bursts_n_1080280.html |work=Huffington Post |title=Pacific Gas & Electric Pipeline Bursts During Test, Closing Freeway |date=November 7, 2011 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20111108052340/http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2011/11/07/pacific-gas-electric-pipeline-bursts_n_1080280.html |archivedate=November 8, 2011}}</ref>
* On September 9, a 20-inch diameter [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] Company pipeline failed in [[Lawrence County, Kentucky]]. While there was no fire or evacuations, the condition of this uncoated, non-cathodic protected, unknown grade pipeline caused PHMSA to enter into a Consent Order to eventually replace this pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF 2-2010-1010S |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220101010S/220101010S_Notice%20of%20Proposed%20Safety%20Order_09302010.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211200004/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220101010S/220101010S_Notice%20of%20Proposed%20Safety%20Order_09302010.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On September 28, a repair crew was working on a corroded gas pipe in [[Cairo, Georgia]], when the line exploded. One crew member was killed, and three others burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wctv.tv/home/headlines/Investigation_Report_Released_for_Cairo_Gasline_Explosion_112962719.html |title=Investigation Report Released for Cairo Gasline Explosion |publisher=Wctv.tv |date=January 5, 2011 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130907133014/http://www.wctv.tv/home/headlines/Investigation_Report_Released_for_Cairo_Gasline_Explosion_112962719.html |archivedate=September 7, 2013 }}</ref>
* On October 15, a gas pipeline under construction in [[Grand Prairie, Texas]] was running a [[pigging|cleaning pig]] without a pig "trap" at the end of the pipe. The 150 pound pig was expelled from the pipeline with enough force to fly {{convert|500|ft|m}}, and crash through the side of a house. No one was injured.<ref>{{cite web|last=Shipp |first=Brett |url=http://www.wfaa.com/news/local/Pipeline-Flying-Pig-crashes-through-Grand-Prairie-home-105387413.html |title=Pipeline 'pig' crashes through Grand Prairie home &#124; wfaa.com &#124; Dallas – Fort Worth Local News |publisher=wfaa.com |date=October 20, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130126024404/http://www.wfaa.com/news/local/Pipeline-Flying-Pig-crashes-through-Grand-Prairie-home-105387413.html |archivedate=January 26, 2013}}</ref>

* On November 30, a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] 30-inch gas pipeline failed at [[Natchitoches, Louisiana]]. There was no fire, but the pipeline had a Magnetic Flux smart pig test earlier in the year that indicated no flaws in the pipeline. The failure was at a crack in a wrinkle bend. The deadly 1965 gas pipeline accident had occurred on a different pipeline owned by the same company nearby.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2010-1007H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420101007H/420101007H_CAO_12032010.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161226084530/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420101007H/420101007H_CAO_12032010.pdf |archivedate=December 26, 2016 }}</ref>

This failure was only 100 yards from a June 2010 failure on the same pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|author= |url=http://www.sltrib.com/sltrib/home/50804000-76/chevron-pipeline-leak-lake.html.csp |title=Was Chevron's response too slow? &#124; The Salt Lake Tribune |publisher=Sltrib.com |date=December 3, 2010 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121009050613/http://www.sltrib.com/sltrib/home/50804000-76/chevron-pipeline-leak-lake.html.csp |archivedate=October 9, 2012 }}</ref>

* On December 8, at East Bernard, Texas, a 24” diameter [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] exploded, blasting a 12-foot section of ruptured pipe 295 feet and caused $715,000 in property damage. It took 6 hours for the pipe system to blow down. The cause of the leak was a full guillotine failure of the pipe caused by internal corrosion micro-biologically induced due to moisture in the pipe.<ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report – Tennessee Gas Pipeline Co. ‐ Internal Corrosion   Failure Date 12/08/2010 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/TGP_GT_TX_20101208.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170130190444/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/TGP_GT_TX_20101208.pdf |archivedate=January 30, 2017 }}</ref>

=== 2011 ===
* On January 11, personnel from [[Millennium Pipeline]] noticed that a gas transmission pipeline was leaking in [[Tioga County, New York]]. This 30-inch diameter pipeline was built in 2008. A pinhole in a rejected girth weld was found to be the cause of the failure. It appears that during the course of the construction project for the line, the subject pipe section was inadvertently picked up and subsequently installed in the pipeline. PHMSA ordered testing of this pipeline for similar flaws.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF 1-2011-1013S |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120111013S/120111013S_NOPSO_07062011.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161225071520/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/120111013S/120111013S_NOPSO_07062011.pdf |archivedate=December 25, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report – Columbia Gas Transmission, Millennium Pipeline Weld Anomaly Failure Date 01/11/2011 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/CGT_2616_Millennium_West_NY_09132012_[Redacted_for_Internet].pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170127033252/http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/CGT_2616_Millennium_West_NY_09132012_%5BRedacted_for_Internet%5D.pdf |archivedate=January 27, 2017 }}</ref>
* A 12-inch cast iron gas main leaking in [[Philadelphia]] explodes, killing a repair crew member and injuring six others on January 18.<ref>{{cite web |title=2nd UPDATE: Philadelphia Gas-Line Blast Kills One, Hurts Six |url=https://online.wsj.com/article/BT-CO-20110119-716460.html |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110123003654/http://online.wsj.com/article/BT-CO-20110119-716460.html |archivedate=January 23, 2011}}</ref><ref name="opsweb.phmsa.dot.gov">{{cite web|url=http://opsweb.phmsa.dot.gov/cast_iron/ |title=Page has moved |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150310100120/http://opsweb.phmsa.dot.gov/cast_iron/ |archivedate=March 10, 2015 }}</ref>
* Multiple gas pressure regulators failed, and caused a gas pressure surge in [[Fairport Harbor, Ohio]], on January 24, causing gas fires in 11 houses, and one apartment. 150 gas appliances were damaged or destroyed, but there were no injuries. Gas company Dominion East Ohio says it found fluids and debris in a failed regulator. A year after the explosion, the Public Utilities Commission of Ohio recommended a $500,000 fine for Dominion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://news-herald.com/articles/2011/02/02/news/nh3594036.txt?viewmode=fullstory |title=Fairport Harbor blasts probed |publisher=news-herald.com |date=February 2, 2011 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120313003640/http://news-herald.com/articles/2011/02/02/news/nh3594036.txt?viewmode=fullstory |archivedate=March 13, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|agency=Associated Press |url=http://www.newsnet5.com/dpp/news/local_news/lawsuit-filed-over-natural-gas-fires-in-fairport-harbor |title=Lawsuit filed over natural gas fires in Fairport Harbor |publisher=Newsnet5.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120309144633/http://www.newsnet5.com/dpp/news/local_news/lawsuit-filed-over-natural-gas-fires-in-fairport-harbor |archivedate=March 9, 2012}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://news-herald.com/articles/2011/10/19/news/nh4642830.txt |title=Dominion officials respond to Fairport residents |publisher=news-herald.com |date=October 19, 2011 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120529082946/http://news-herald.com/articles/2011/10/19/news/nh4642830.txt |archivedate=May 29, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Puco Staff Report Fire Investigation |url=http://www.fox8.com/news/wjw-news-puco-staff-report-fire-investigation,0,910014.story |accessdate=May 14, 2012}}{{dead link|date=May 2016|bot=medic}}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref>
* Five people were killed, and eight houses were destroyed, in a gas explosion and fire in [[Allentown, Pennsylvania]] on February 9. The NTSB had warned UGI about cast iron gas mains needing replacement after the 1990 gas explosion in that city. Between 1976 and the date of the letter, July 10, 1992, two more gas explosions occurred. Three people were killed, 23 injured and 11 houses were destroyed or damaged in those explosions. UGI was cited in 2012 for several safety violations, including a lack of valves on their gas system.<ref>{{cite web |title=Five Killed in Pennsylvania Gas Explosion |url=http://www.firehouse.com/news/top-headlines/five-killed-massive-pennsylvania-gas-explosion |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110221080733/http://www.firehouse.com/news/top-headlines/five-killed-massive-pennsylvania-gas-explosion |archivedate=February 21, 2011}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=UGI told years ago to remove old pipes |url=http://www.mcall.com/news/local/allentown/mc-allentown-ntsb-blast-20110301,0,3589679.story |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121002151407/http://www.mcall.com/news/local/allentown/mc-allentown-ntsb-blast-20110301%2C0%2C3589679.story |archivedate=October 2, 2012 |df= }}</ref><ref>{{cite av media|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=uG8m7V0KXbs&feature=player_embedded |title=Allentown Explosion |date=February 10, 2011 |publisher= |accessdate=January 19, 2016 |via=YouTube |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=uG8m7V0KXbs&feature=player_embedded |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wfmz.com/news/news-regional-lehighvalley/UGI-cited-for-multiple-safety-violations-leading-to-Allentown-gas-explosion/-/132502/14773532/-/t2eat7/-/index.html |title=UGI cited for multiple safety violations leading to Allentown gas explosion &#124; Regional: Lehigh Valley – Home |publisher=Wfmz.com |date=June 11, 2012 |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130320172323/http://www.wfmz.com/news/news-regional-lehighvalley/UGI-cited-for-multiple-safety-violations-leading-to-Allentown-gas-explosion/-/132502/14773532/-/t2eat7/-/index.html |archivedate=March 20, 2013 }}</ref>
* Late on February 10, a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] 36-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned near [[Lisbon, Ohio]]. No injuries resulted. The cause was from stress on a girth weld on the pipeline. A failure on another girth weld on the pipeline system led to a PHMSA Consent Agreement.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wytv.com/mostpopular/story/Huge-Natural-Gas-Explosion-Near-Lisbon/P5r50OZ9VkOqkl_ZuNTL0A.cspx |title=Huge Natural Gas Explosion Near Lisbon – 33 News – We Believe in This Valley |publisher=Wytv.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120325055104/http://www.wytv.com/mostpopular/story/Huge-Natural-Gas-Explosion-Near-Lisbon/P5r50OZ9VkOqkl_ZuNTL0A.cspx |archivedate=March 25, 2012}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wfmj.com/story/15677053/cause-of-explosion-in-hanover-township-determined |title=Cause of explosion in Hanover Township determined – 21 News Now, More Local News for Youngstown, Ohio |publisher=Wfmj.com |date= |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028060153/http://www.wfmj.com/story/15677053/cause-of-explosion-in-hanover-township-determined |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2011-1001S |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320111001S/320111001S_Consent%20Agreement_03312011.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170209065759/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320111001S/320111001S_Consent%20Agreement_03312011.pdf |archivedate=February 9, 2017 }}</ref>

* Early on March 17, a 20-inch steel [[CenterPoint Energy]] natural gas line running through a [[Minneapolis, Minnesota]] neighborhood ruptured, and gas from it ignited, caused evacuations to buildings nearby, and Interstate 35W was closed from downtown Minneapolis to Highway 62. There were no injuries. The Minnesota Office of Pipeline Safety later found the pipe there was not designed to handle the load of soil and passing cars, and efforts to shore up the pipeline were incorrectly carried out.<ref name="dot7">{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_12350.html?nocache=5865#_Incidents_tab_3 |publisher=primis.phmsa.dot.gov |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |accessdate=October 5, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161005110154/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_12350.html?nocache=5865 |archivedate=October 5, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|author=David Joles |url=http://www.startribune.com/local/118164804.html |title=Light 'like the sun' rose above Mpls. blast crater |publisher=StarTribune.com |accessdate=April 2, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130825235202/http://www.startribune.com/local/118164804.html |archivedate=August 25, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://southwestminneapolis.patch.com/articles/report-id-s-cause-of-windom-pipeline-explosion |title=Report ID's Cause of Windom Pipeline Explosion |work=Southwest Minneapolis, Minnesota Patch |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130429075734/http://southwestminneapolis.patch.com/articles/report-id-s-cause-of-windom-pipeline-explosion |archivedate=April 29, 2013 }}</ref>

* An 8-inch NGL pipeline failed in [[Romeoville, Illinois]] on May 14, leaking about 4200 gallons of butane. Corrosion inside a casing under a road was the cause of the failure. Corrosion only 2.5 feet from the failure had been seen by a smart pig run in 2007, but was not within action limits at the time.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2011-5008S |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320115008S/320115008S_Notice%20of%20Proposed%20Safety%20Order_06152011_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170216044534/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320115008S/320115008S_Notice%20of%20Proposed%20Safety%20Order_06152011_text.pdf |archivedate=February 16, 2017 }}</ref>

* Late on July 1, a 12-inch Exxon Mobil crude oil pipeline. also known as the Silvertip Pipeline, ruptured, and spilled about 63,000 gallons of oil into the [[Yellowstone River]] in south-central Montana. There was confusion in the pipeline control room, causing a delayed pipeline shutdown. Some residents of [[Laurel, Montana]] had to be evacuated.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2011/07/03/us/03oilspill.html |work=The New York Times |first=Anahad |last=O'Connor |work=KTVQ.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141026211809/http://www.ktvq.com/news/laurel-residents-evacuate-after-oil-pipeline-break/ |archivedate=October 26, 2014}}</ref> The break near Billings fouled the riverbank and forced municipalities and irrigation districts to close intakes.<ref>{{cite archive-date=November 12, 2012 | work=The Washington Post |date=July 3, 2011 |title=Exxon oil spill prompts evacuations}}</ref> Exxon later increased the spill size estimate to 1500 barrels in January 2012 after seeing the damage to the pipeline.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://latimesblogs.latimes.com/greenspace/2011/07/exxon-pipeline-spill-on-yellowstone-river.html |work=Los Angeles Times 140 people were evacuated starting about 12:15&nbsp;a.m. Saturday due to concerns about possible explosions and the overpowering fumes. All were allowed to return after instruments showed petroleum odors had decreased,<ref name="msnbc.msn.com">{{cite web|url=http://www.msnbc.msn.com/id/43619388/ns/us_news-environment/ |title=ExxonMobil pipe spills oil into Yellowstone River |work=msnbc.com |accessdate=January 19, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121105123050/http://www.msnbc.msn.com/id/43619388/ns/us_news-environment/ |archivedate=November 5, 2012 }}</ref> although no information was available regarding the concentrations of benzene in air. Speculation involves high water flow in the Yellowstone River may have scoured the river bed and exposed the pipe. Consequently, with three oil refineries are located in the Billings area, the fire chief for the city of Laurel said he asked all three to turn off the flow of oil in their pipelines under the river after the leak was reported. Exxon Mobil and Cenex Harvest Refinery did so, and that Conoco Phillips said its pipe was already shutdown.<ref name="msnbc.msn.com" /> Cenex had a release into the Yellowstone River in September 2002. Exxon Mobil later announced the cleanup would cost $135&nbsp;million. In 2015, Exxon Mobil was fined $1&nbsp;million by PHMSA for this incident.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.foxnews.com/us/2012/01/19/exxon-yellowstone-spill-1500-barrels-not-1000/ |work=Fox News |title=Exxon: Yellowstone spill 1,500 barrels, not 1,000 |date=January 19, 2012 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120208091909/http://www.foxnews.com/us/2012/01/19/exxon-yellowstone-spill-1500-barrels-not-1000/ |archivedate=February 8, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dallasnews.com/business/energy/20130914-lawsuits-against-exxon-mobil-mount-over-big-oil-pipeline-spills.ece |title=Lawsuits against Exxon Mobil mount over big oil pipeline spills |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141021015804/http://www.dallasnews.com/business/energy/20130914-lawsuits-against-exxon-mobil-mount-over-big-oil-pipeline-spills.ece |archivedate=October 21, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.deq.mt.gov/statesuperfund/silvertipoilspill/default.mcpx |title=Montana DEQ – Page Not Found |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150128163142/http://deq.mt.gov/StateSuperfund/silvertipoilspill/default.mcpx |archivedate=January 28, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dailyinterlake.com/news/state_news/exxon-mobil-gets-million-penalty-for-pipeline-spill/article_199baf3c-a380-11e4-9674-d3ebafa41c24.html |title=Exxon Mobil gets $1 million penalty for pipeline spill |work=Daily Inter Lake |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150128004826/http://www.dailyinterlake.com/news/state_news/exxon-mobil-gets-million-penalty-for-pipeline-spill/article_199baf3c-a380-11e4-9674-d3ebafa41c24.html |archivedate=January 28, 2015 }}</ref>

* On August 17, [[Kinder Morgan]]'s [[Natural Gas Pipeline Company of America]] had a flash fire and explosion at a plant south of [[Herscher, Illinois]]. Five employees went to the hospital. Kinder Morgan was later cited for pipeline and workplace safety violations.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.naturalgaswatch.org/?p=817 |title=Kinder Morgan, Owner of Illinois Natural Gas Pipeline Co. Where Explosion Occurred, Has Lengthy Record of Pipeline, Workplace Safety Violations – Natural Gas Watch.org |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141008080039/http://www.naturalgaswatch.org/?p=817 |archivedate=October 8, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.hazardexonthenet.net/article/44270/Gas-plant-explosion-injures-five.aspx?AreaID=2 |title=HazardEx – Gas plant explosion injures five |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006124557/http://www.hazardexonthenet.net/article/44270/Gas-plant-explosion-injures-five.aspx?AreaID=2 |archivedate=October 6, 2014 }}</ref>
* A pipeline carrying heating oil was hit by construction workers in [[East Providence, Rhode Island]] on August 31, spraying oil on roofs, trees, and pavement, and flowed into storm drains. At least {{convert|56,000|USgal|L}} of oil were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.projo.com/news/environment/content/OIL_SPILL_UPDATE_09-03-11_SKQ4BP2_v15.64660.html |title=Providence Journal – Rhode Island news, sports, weather and more |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20111016024958/http://www.projo.com/news/environment/content/OIL_SPILL_UPDATE_09-03-11_SKQ4BP2_v15.64660.html |archivedate=October 16, 2011}}</ref>
* A [[Cupertino, California]] condominium was gutted August 31, after a plastic pipeline fitting cracked, filling the garage with natural gas that exploded just minutes after the owner left for lunch. PG&E later found six other plastic pipe failures near the blast site. The line was an especially problematic type of pipe manufactured by DuPont called Aldyl-A. PG&E has {{convert|1,231|mi|km}} of the early-1970s-vintage pipe in its system. Federal regulators singled out pre-1973 Aldyl-A starting in 2002 as being at risk of failing because of premature cracking. Explosions caused by failed Aldyl-A and other types of plastic pipe have killed more than 50 people in the United States since 1971, the federal government says.<ref>{{cite news| url=http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?file=/c/a/2011/09/26/MNAH1L8QMB.DTL | work=The San Francisco Chronicle | first=Jaxon | last=Van Derbeken | title=Plastic natural gas pipe failure data kept secret | date=October 17, 2011}}</ref>
* A 10-inch LPG pipeline failed on September 8 in [[Mitchell County, Texas]]. The escaping gas ignited, starting a small brush fire. The cause of the failure was a crack in the weld of a repair sleeve from bending and heat hardening. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report – Chevron Coahoma LPG Loop Failure Date 9/8/2011 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Chevron%20HL%20TX%202011-09-08%20508.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161128140609/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Chevron%20HL%20TX%202011-09-08%20508.pdf |archivedate=November 28, 2016 }}</ref>
* On September 20, a farmer digging to lay drainage tile hit a 10-inch gasoline pipeline near [[Aurelius, New York]], spilling about {{convert|3,300|USgal|m3}} of gasoline. There was no fire or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.syracuse.com/news/index.ssf/2011/09/ruptured_gasoline_pipeline_fix.html |title=Ruptured gasoline pipeline fixed in Aurelius; testing of nearby private wells continues |work=syracuse.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141220181631/http://www.syracuse.com/news/index.ssf/2011/09/ruptured_gasoline_pipeline_fix.html |archivedate=December 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* A 2-inch crude oil gathering pipeline failed in Oklahoma on October 12, spilling about 120 barrels of oil. There were no injuries or fire from the failure.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2011/10/24/pipeline-operations-blueknight-idUKN1E79N0V720111024 |agency=Reuters |first=Janet |last=McGurty |title=Blueknight reopens Oklahoma crude line after leak |date=October 24, 2011 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028001425/http://uk.reuters.com/article/2011/10/24/pipeline-operations-blueknight-idUKN1E79N0V720111024 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* Early on November 3, an explosion and fire hit a gas [[Columbia Gas Transmission]] pipeline compressor station at [[Artemas, Pennsylvania|Artemas]] in [[Mann Township, Bedford County, Pennsylvania]]. There were no injuries. The cause was internal corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://times-news.com/latest_news/x459213779/Artemas-gas-explosion-forces-temporary-evacuation|archive-url=https://archive.is/20120716132352/http://times-news.com/latest_news/x459213779/Artemas-gas-explosion-forces-temporary-evacuation|dead-url=yes|archive-date=July 16, 2012|title=Link to video of Artemas gas explosion at bottom of page|work=The Cumberland Times-News|accessdate=January 18, 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_2616.html?nocache=7677#_Incidents_tab_4 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022132553/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_2616.html?nocache=7677 |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref>
* On November 8, a contractor for Vectren Corp. working on a bare gas main replacement project broke a "short stub" on the main, then failed to notify [[New Albany, Indiana]] authorities about the leak. Gas migrated through the soil, and built up in a nearby house, then exploded. Five people had to be hospitalized.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://newsandtribune.com/local/x1241962523/Vectren-agrees-to-75-000-settlement-in-2011-gas-explosion|title=Vectren agrees to $75,000 settlement in 2011 gas explosion|work=News and Tribune|accessdate=January 18, 2016}}</ref>
* A crew working on a waterline hit a gas distribution pipeline in [[Fairborn, Ohio]] on November 12, leading to a gas explosion that killed one man, and injured five others, including children.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.foxnews.com/us/2011/11/12/ohio-house-explosion-injures-6-1-missing-officials-say/?test=latestnews |work=Fox News |title=Missing Man Found Dead After Deadly Ohio House Explosion |date=November 13, 2011 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120104202747/http://www.foxnews.com/us/2011/11/12/ohio-house-explosion-injures-6-1-missing-officials-say/?test=latestnews |archivedate=January 4, 2012 }}</ref>
* On the evening of November 13, 2011, a release of nearly 1798,000 gallons of diesel fuel occurred at the Belle Fourche Pipeline Company’s Davis Station in a remote area of [[Wyoming]]. The cause was from pumping against a closed valve on the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Belle_Fourche_Wright_WY_2011_11_13_Redacted.pdf |title=Archived copy |accessdate=2017-05-08 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170430084057/https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Belle_Fourche_Wright_WY_2011_11_13_Redacted.pdf |archivedate=April 30, 2017 }}</ref> 
* On November 16, a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] 36-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned near [[Glouster, Ohio]]. Two people were injured, with three houses and a barn destroyed, and a barn damaged. The pipeline failed at a girth weld, with landsliding causing more stress on the weld.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2011-lOlSH |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/320111018H_CAO_11172011%20-%20Tennessee%20Gas.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170216152806/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/320111018H_CAO_11172011%20-%20Tennessee%20Gas.pdf |archivedate=February 16, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mariettatimes.com/page/content.detail/id/545475/Nov--pipeline-blast-leaves-lasting-impact-on-lives.html?nav=5002 |title=Nov. pipeline blast leaves lasting impact on lives |work=The Marietta Times |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160624211305/http://www.mariettatimes.com/page/content.detail/id/545475/Nov--pipeline-blast-leaves-lasting-impact-on-lives.html?nav=5002 |archivedate=June 24, 2016 }}</ref>
* Late on November 21, a [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] 24-inch gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned near [[Batesville, Mississippi]]. Twenty houses were evacuated for a time, but there were no injuries or major property damage. The pipeline failed at a sleeve over a wrinkle bend installed in 1946.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 2-2011-lOlOH |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220111010H/220111010H_CAO_11282011.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211092950/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/reports/enforce/documents/220111010H/220111010H_CAO_11282011.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On December 3, a [[Williams Companies]] gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned in [[Marengo County, Alabama]]. A 47-foot section of the pipe was hurled more than 200 feet from the failure area. The gas burned for several hours, and a nearby pipeline was damaged. There were no injuries, or serious property damage. External corrosion was the cause of the failure, due to issues with the pipeline coating, the cathodic protection level, and the local soil corrosiveness.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wsfa.com/story/16181245/pipeline-explodes-in-marengo-county-causes-massive-fire |title=Pipeline explodes in Marengo County, causes massive fire |date=December 3, 2011 |work=wsfa.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.wsfa.com/story/16181245/pipeline-explodes-in-marengo-county-causes-massive-fire |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 2-2011-lOllH |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220111011H/220111011H_CAO_12062011.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211092016/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/Reports/enforce/documents/220111011H/220111011H_CAO_12062011.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.demopolistimes.com/2012/02/21/corrosion-cited-in-pipeline-explosion/ |title=Corrosion cited in pipeline explosion – The Demopolis Times |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.demopolistimes.com/2012/02/21/corrosion-cited-in-pipeline-explosion/ |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On December 6, explosions and fire erupted at a natural gas pipeline compressor station in [[Sublette County, Wyoming]]. Two workers were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://trib.com/news/state-and-regional/two-injured-in-fire-explosions-at-wyoming-natural-gas-site/article_1e7e73ac-e3a0-563a-bff1-0b6a716457da.html |title=Two suffer injuries due to fire at Wyoming natural gas site |author=JEREMY FUGLEBERG |work=Casper Star-Tribune Online |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120118005859/http://trib.com/news/state-and-regional/two-injured-in-fire-explosions-at-wyoming-natural-gas-site/article_1e7e73ac-e3a0-563a-bff1-0b6a716457da.html |archivedate=January 18, 2012 }}</ref>
* On December 10, a landowner using a bulldozer hit an 8-inch and a 12-inch petroleum pipelines near [[Nemaha, Nebraska]], rupturing both lines. The spill size was estimated to be 119,000 gallons of gasoline, jet fuel, and Diesel fuel. Some of the fuels flowed into a creek leading into Jasper Creek. There were questions about the depth of soil coverage for this pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://journalstar.com/business/local/magellan-pipeline-fixed-near-nemaha-fuel-pumping-to-resume/article_a9db6a3a-2ddb-5d7c-af11-3b329c4576b0.html|title=Magellan: Pipeline fixed near Nemaha, fuel pumping resumes|author=|work=JournalStar.com|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://journalstar.com/news/local/clean-up-begins-on-pipeline-spill-in-nemaha-county/article_97ce305c-051f-5e9f-a93a-34f7ab9e00c2.html |title=Pipeline fixed near Nemaha; fuel pumping resumes |author=ALGIS J. LAUKAITIS / Lincoln Journal Star |work=JournalStar.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120502230044/http://journalstar.com/news/local/clean-up-begins-on-pipeline-spill-in-nemaha-county/article_97ce305c-051f-5e9f-a93a-34f7ab9e00c2.html |archivedate=May 2, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.businessweek.com/news/2011-12-13/magellan-reduces-nebraska-line-spill-estimate-to-2-834-barrels.html |title=Magellan Reduces Nebraska Line Spill Estimate to 2,834 Barrels |author=Paul Burkhardt |work=Businessweek.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028144724/http://www.businessweek.com/news/2011-12-13/magellan-reduces-nebraska-line-spill-estimate-to-2-834-barrels.html |archivedate=October 28, 2013}}</ref>
* A 42-inch natural gas transmission pipeline failed and ignited at a valve on December 10 in [[Cache County, Utah]].<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.denverpost.com/breakingnews/ci_19530048 |work=Denver Post |title=El Paso says no estimate for Return of Ruby gas line in Utah |date=December 12, 2011 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20111215060417/http://www.denverpost.com/breakingnews/ci_19530048 |archivedate=December 15, 2011 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://ebb.cigco.com/ebbmasterpage/Notices/NoticesAutoTable.aspx?code=RUBY&status=Notice&name=Critical%20Notices&sParam1=0495&sParam3=77&sParam14=D&details=Y |title=Ruby Pipeline LLC :: Informational Postings |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141024025514/http://ebb.cigco.com/ebbmasterpage/Notices/NoticesAutoTable.aspx?code=RUBY&status=Notice&name=Critical%20Notices&sParam1=0495&sParam3=77&sParam14=D&details=Y |archivedate=October 24, 2014 }}</ref>
* On December 27, controllers for Enterprise Pipeline received an alarm, for a leak on an LPG pipeline. The leak location was found in [[Loving County, Texas]]. Repair crew excavated the area, and found a full girth weld failure. During the pipeline repair, a flash fire involving residual pipeline product in the soil occurred, injuring 3 employees, one of whom required in-patient hospitalization. The rupture was attributed to the complete circumferential separation of an acetylene girth weld dating to 1928, and the flash fire was attributed to operator error.<ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report – Enterprise Products Operating LLC – Girth Weld Failure 12/27/2011 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/Failure_Investigation_Report_Enterprise_Rio_Grande_Final.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170210055827/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/Failure_Investigation_Report_Enterprise_Rio_Grande_Final.pdf |archivedate=February 10, 2017 }}</ref>

=== 2012 ===
* A 30-inch gas pipeline exploded and burned, in [[Estill County, Kentucky]], on the evening of January 2. The rupture created a crater approximately 86 feet long by 22 feet wide, and expelled a number of pieces of pipe as far as 800 feet from the rupture center. Flames were reported reaching over 1,000 feet high. Residents up to a mile away from the failure were evacuated. There were no injuries. The cause was overstress from land movement.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wkyt.com/wymtnews/headlines/136548983.html |title=Archived copy |accessdate=May 14, 2012 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120106210254/http://www.wkyt.com/wymtnews/headlines/136548983.html |archivedate=January 6, 2012}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report – Columbia Gulf Transmission, Line 200 Rupture in Estill County, Kentucky Failure Date – January 2, 2012 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/CGT_Estill_Co_KY_[Redacted_for_Internet].pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170131220027/http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/CGT_Estill_Co_KY_%5BRedacted_for_Internet%5D.pdf |archivedate=January 31, 2017 }}</ref>
* A forest fire caused a gas pipeline to explode and burn in [[Floyd County, Kentucky]] on January 7. There were no injuries from this incident.<ref>[http://www.therepublic.com/view/story/4d82f196216f484dacfd7657510abcaa/KY--Explosion-Fire/]{{dead link|date=May 2016}}</ref>
* On January 9, a man was killed, and another person injured, in a fiery house explosion from a leaking 4-inch cast iron gas main installed in 1950 in [[Austin, Texas]]. Gas had been smelled in the area for several weeks prior to this. Gas company crews had looked along the affected property for a leak, but were unable to find it.<ref name="opsweb.phmsa.dot.gov" /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.statesman.com/news/local/man-feared-dead-in-home-explosion-had-hoped-2094583.html |title=Man feared dead in home explosion had hoped to move near son |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120129091720/http://www.statesman.com/news/local/man-feared-dead-in-home-explosion-had-hoped-2094583.html |archivedate=January 29, 2012 }}</ref>
* A [[Sunoco]] pipeline ruptured and spilled about 117,000 gallons of gasoline, in [[Wellington, Ohio]], late on January 12. Some residents were evacuated for a week.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wkyc.com/news/state/article/224794/23/Wellington-Families-still-evacuated-after-massive-pipeline-spill|archive-url=https://archive.is/20120919182535/http://www.wkyc.com/news/state/article/224794/23/Wellington-Families-still-evacuated-after-massive-pipeline-spill|dead-url=yes|archive-date=September 19, 2012|title=Wellington: Families still evacuated after massive pipeline spill|author=|date=January 13, 2012|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.newsnet5.com/dpp/news/local_news/oh_lorain/wellington-may-have-answers-in-the-coming-weeks |title=Wellington may have answers in the coming weeks |work=newsnet5 |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131027232258/http://www.newsnet5.com/dpp/news/local_news/oh_lorain/wellington-may-have-answers-in-the-coming-weeks |archivedate=October 27, 2013}}</ref>
* On January 13, an 8-inch gas pipeline exploded and burned, in a vacant agricultural field, in [[Rio Vista, California]]. There were no injuries or evacuations.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mercurynews.com/breaking-news/ci_19739515 |title=No injuries, damage after gas line explodes in Rio Vista |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140714124305/http://www.mercurynews.com/breaking-news/ci_19739515 |archivedate=July 14, 2014 }}</ref>
* A [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] gas compressor had a major leak "that sounded like a rocket" in [[Powell County, Kentucky]], forcing evacuations of nearby residents on January 14. There was no fire or injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lex18.com/news/gas-leak-in-powell-county |title=Archived copy |accessdate=May 14, 2012 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120119085823/http://www.lex18.com/news/gas-leak-in-powell-county |archivedate=January 19, 2012}}</ref>
* A contractor excavating for a communications company caused a massive gas explosion and fire at a condominium complex on January 16 in [[West Haverstraw, New York]], injuring two firefighters and two utility workers. Afterwards, it was found that the excavator's insurance will be insufficient to cover all of the property damage of the incident.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lohud.com/article/20120121/NEWS03/301200069/Cortlandt-contractor-gas-explosion-may-lack-enough-insurance-lawyer-homeowners-says |title=Cortlandt contractor in gas explosion may lack enough insurance, lawyer for homeowners says |work=The Journal News – lohud.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150223060211/http://www.lohud.com/article/20120121/NEWS03/301200069/Cortlandt-contractor-gas-explosion-may-lack-enough-insurance-lawyer-homeowners-says |archivedate=February 23, 2015}}</ref>
* On January 18, the original [[Colonial Pipeline]] mainline failed in [[Belton, South Carolina]], spilling about 13,500 gallons of petroleum product. The failure was caused by internal corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/273705 |title=Jan. 18, 2012 – ProPublica |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140714145123/http://projects.propublica.org/pipelines/incidents/273705 |archivedate=July 14, 2014 }}</ref>
* Workers in [[Topeka, Kansas]] were installing a yard sprinkler system on January 30, hit a gas line. Gas from the leak later on exploded in a nearby house, burning a 73-year-old woman, who died several weeks later.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wibw.com/home/headlines/Building_Explosion_138335069.html |title=Details About Victim Of Home Explosion Released |author1=Giang Nguyen |author2=Marques White |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020085806/http://www.wibw.com/home/headlines/Building_Explosion_138335069.html |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wibw.com/community/headlines//Home_explosion_Victim_Dies_138718084.html |title=Home Explosion Victim Dies |author=Stephanie Ramos-Tomeoni |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020085804/http://www.wibw.com/community/headlines//Home_explosion_Victim_Dies_138718084.html |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* On January 31, a [[Shell Oil Company]] fuel pipeline to the [[Milwaukee, Wisconsin]] Mitchell International Airport was found to be leaking. Jet fuel had been smelled for about two weeks in the area, and was found in runoff water in the area. The cause was from external corrosion. About 9,000 gallons of fuel were spilled. In 2014, a Shell employee was scheduled to plead guilty to charges of falsifying records of the pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wisn.com/news/30345282/detail.html|title=Jet Fuel Leaks For 2 Weeks Into Sewer|work=WISN|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.jsonline.com/news/milwaukee/ex-shell-pipeline-monitor-to-plead-guilty-in-airport-leak-b99392450z1-282987621.html |title=Former Shell Pipeline monitor to plead guilty in airport leak |author=Bruce Vielmetti |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150121055823/http://www.jsonline.com/news/milwaukee/ex-shell-pipeline-monitor-to-plead-guilty-in-airport-leak-b99392450z1-282987621.html |archivedate=January 21, 2015 }}</ref>
* A Florida Gas Transmission Company 30-inch gas transmission pipeline burst near [[Baton Rouge, Louisiana]] on February 13. Residents in the area were evacuated for a time, but there was no fire.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2013-1014H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420131014H/420131014H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06242013.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211183434/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/Reports/enforce/documents/420131014H/420131014H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06242013.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31174.html?nocache=2826#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160126141644/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31174.html?nocache=2826 |archivedate=January 26, 2016 }}</ref>
* On February 15, 2012, in [[Arenac County, Michigan]], oil was discovered in the soil around a 30-inch [[Enbridge]] crude oil pipeline. About 800 gallons of crude oil was spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_11169.html?nocache=3470#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141129063140/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_11169.html?nocache=3470 |archivedate=November 29, 2014 }}</ref>
* Two cars that were drag racing went off the road they were on, and crash through a fence and into a crude oil pipeline in [[New Lenox, Illinois]] on March 3. The pipeline was ruptured, and the crude oil ignited. Two men from the vehicles were killed, and three others seriously burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.firerescue1.com/fire-attack/articles/1247826-2-killed-by-Ill-oil-pipeline-explosion/ |title=2 killed by Ill. oil pipeline explosion |work=FireRescue1.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141102095710/http://www.firerescue1.com/fire-attack/articles/1247826-2-killed-by-Ill-oil-pipeline-explosion/ |archivedate=November 2, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://af.reuters.com/article/energyOilNews/idAFL2E8E7FYA20120307?sp=true |agency=Reuters |title=Late-night car race that caused pipeline fire rare, not unique |date=March 7, 2012 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022072101/https://af.reuters.com/article/energyOilNews/idAFL2E8E7FYA20120307?sp=true |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref>
* On March 5, a leak at an [[Enid, Oklahoma]] pipeline storage facility spread propane fumes in the area, forcing evacuations. There was no fire or explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.tulsaworld.com/business/article.aspx?subjectid=49&articleid=20120306_49_0_ENIDCr320893|title=Tulsa World|first1=Tulsa World: Tulsa|last1=news|first2=|last2=sports|first3=|last3=business|first4=|last4=entertainment|first5=|last5=weather|work=tulsaworld.com|accessdate=September 16, 2016}}</ref>
* A crude oil pipeline leaked near [[Grand Isle, Louisiana]] on March 17, spilling as much as 8,400 gallons of crude oil. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nola.com/environment/index.ssf/2012/03/officials_finish_cleaning_crud.html |title=Officials finish cleaning crude from leaky pipeline in Barataria Bay |work=NOLA.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022105725/http://www.nola.com/environment/index.ssf/2012/03/officials_finish_cleaning_crud.html |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref>
* On March 29, an employee accidentally left a valve open during maintenance work on a [[Williams Companies]] gas compressor station near [[Springville Township, Pennsylvania]]. Later, gas leaked through the valve, causing alarms to evacuate workers in the compressor building. Later, the gas exploded and burned. There were no injuries. It was also found there are no agencies enforcing rules on rural gas facilities in that state.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.philly.com/philly/news/20120408_Northern_Pennsylvania_gas_explosion_was_out_of_regulatory_reach.html?viewAll=y|title=Northern Pennsylvania gas explosion was out of regulatory reach|work=Philly.com|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://thetimes-tribune.com/news/explosion-at-natural-gas-compressor-station-1.1292502#axzz1qWyVU1UF|title=Explosion rocks natural gas compressor station|author=Laura Legere|publisher=|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On April 2, Transcontinental Gas Pipeline Company, reported a leak on their 72nd Street Interstate Transmission Lateral located in [[North Bergen, New Jersey]]. Workers discovered a rock in contact with the bottom of the pipe. Upon removing the rock, the pipeline began to leak. There was no fire or injuries reported as a result of this incident.<ref>{{cite web|title=Williams Gas Pipeline-Transco; North Bergen, NJ, 72nd Street Interstate Trans Lateral Leak Failure Date: 4/2/2012 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/139107_Williams_Gas_Pipeline_North_Bergen_NJ_2012[Redacted_for_Internet].pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170210152455/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/139107_Williams_Gas_Pipeline_North_Bergen_NJ_2012%5BRedacted_for_Internet%5D.pdf |archivedate=February 10, 2017 }}</ref>
* A 12-inch gas pipeline exploded and burned for five hours near [[Gary, Texas]] on April 4. There were no injuries, but the rupture site was only 200 feet from that pipeline's compressor station.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kcentv.com/story/17337012/pipeline-explodes-near-carthage |title=Pipeline explodes near Carthage |author=Amy Tatum |date=April 4, 2012 |work=kcentv.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.kcentv.com/story/17337012/pipeline-explodes-near-carthage |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 6, two gas company workers were mildly burned when attempting to fix a leak on a 4-inch gas pipeline in [[DeSoto County, Mississippi]]. The pipeline exploded and burned during the repairs.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.commercialappeal.com/news/2012/apr/07/in-brief/ |title=In brief: Repairs continue on leaking line |work=MCA |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028000524/http://www.commercialappeal.com/news/2012/apr/07/in-brief/ |archivedate=October 28, 2013}}</ref>
* A gas pipeline exploded and burned in [[Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana]], on April 9. The accident was reported first by a satellite monitoring the area to the NRC. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nola.com/business/index.ssf/2012/04/natural_gas_pipeline_ruptures.html |title=Natural gas pipeline ruptures, sending flames soaring in Terrebonne Parish marshes |work=NOLA.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022105637/http://www.nola.com/business/index.ssf/2012/04/natural_gas_pipeline_ruptures.html |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref>
* Two men escaped with only minor burns after a bulldozer they were using hit a 24-inch gas pipeline near [[Hinton, Iowa]] on April 25. Authorities later announced the men did not call 811 for an underground utility locate.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ktiv.com/story/17797831/northern-natural-gas-men-did-not-check-for-line |title=Northern Natural Gas: Men did not check for pipeline |date=April 26, 2012 |work=ktiv.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.ktiv.com/story/17797831/northern-natural-gas-men-did-not-check-for-line |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 28, an [[ExxonMobil]] 20/22-inch-diameter pipeline ruptured near [[Torbert, Louisiana|Torbert]] in [[Pointe Coupee Parish, Louisiana]], about 20 miles west of Baton Rouge, and crude oil spilled into the surrounding area, and flowed into an unnamed tributary connected to [[Bayou Cholpe]]. About 117,000 gallons of crude were spilled, with about 37,000 gallons being lost. The pipeline failed due to a manufacturing defect.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_4906.html?nocache=4538#_Incidents_tab_4 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022132728/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_4906.html?nocache=4538 |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2012-5019H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420125019H/420125019H_CAO_05082012.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211092454/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/Reports/enforce/documents/420125019H/420125019H_CAO_05082012.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wateronline.com/doc/exxonmobil-pipeline-company-resolves-clean-water-act-violation-stemming-spill-0001 |title=ExxonMobil Pipeline Company To Pay Civil Penalty Under Proposed Settlement For Torbert Louisiana Oil Spill Settlement Resolves Clean Water Act Violation Stemming From 2012 Spill |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020124747/http://www.wateronline.com/doc/exxonmobil-pipeline-company-resolves-clean-water-act-violation-stemming-spill-0001 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* A 26-inch gas transmission pipeline ruptured on June 6 in a compressor station near [[Laketon, Texas|Laketon]] in northeastern [[Gray County, Texas]]. Gas escaped from the 50-foot-long rupture, igniting, leaving a crater 30 feet in diameter, burning two acres of agricultural area and telephone poles. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2012-1011H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420121011H/420121011H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06122012.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211183721/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/reports/enforce/documents/420121011H/420121011H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06122012.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On June 8, near [[Canadian, Texas]], a trackhoe operator suffered burns, after a fire from leaking 4-inch gas-gathering pipeline that was undergoing maintenance. Fumes entered the engine of the trackhoe and ignited.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kristv.com/news/pipeline-worker-hurt-in-texas-panhandle-explosion/|archiveurl=https://archive.is/20130127051818/http://www.kristv.com/news/pipeline-worker-hurt-in-texas-panhandle-explosion/|deadurl=yes|title=Pipeline Worker Hurt in Texas Panhandle Explosion - Corpus Christi, T…|date=January 27, 2013|archivedate=January 27, 2013|publisher=}}</ref>
* A contractor was killed and two others injured after an explosion at a [[BP]] gas compressor station in [[Durango, Colorado]] on June 25. [[BP]], [[Halliburton]], and the other contractors were fined $7,000 each for safety violations in that work.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.hazardexonthenet.net/article/51303/BP-gas-compressor-station-explosion-in-Colorado-kills-one.aspx |title=HazardEx – BP gas compressor station explosion in Colorado kills one |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141108231846/http://www.hazardexonthenet.net/article/51303/BP-gas-compressor-station-explosion-in-Colorado-kills-one.aspx |archivedate=November 8, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.krqe.com/dpp/news/colorado/ap_colorado/BP-Halliburton-fined-in-fatal-pipeline-explosion_54659132 |title=Archived copy |accessdate=January 24, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130201232344/http://www.krqe.com/dpp/news/colorado/ap_colorado/BP-Halliburton-fined-in-fatal-pipeline-explosion_54659132 |archivedate=February 1, 2013}}</ref>
* A West Shore Pipe Line petroleum products pipeline burst near [[Jackson, Washington County, Wisconsin|Jackson, Wisconsin]] on July 17, releasing about 54,000 gallons of gasoline. At least one family self evacuated due to the leak. At least 44 water wells nearby were contaminated from benzine in the gasoline, including a municipal well. A LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam failure was suspected as the cause. Further testing revealed that at least 26 other areas on this pipeline needed repairs, with 22 within the Jackson Marsh Wildlife Area.<ref>{{cite * On July 23, a compressor station operated by [[Williams Companies]] in [[Windsor, New York]] was venting gas in a "routine procedure" — during a lightning storm — when the vent was ignited by lightning, causing a fireball "hundreds of feet into the air"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.naturalgaswatch.org/?p=1459 |title=This Week In Natural Gas Leaks and Explosions – July 30, 2012 – Natural Gas Watch.org |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150620021255/http://www.naturalgaswatch.org/?p=1459 |archivedate=June 20, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wbng.com/news/local/Lightning-Causes-Compressor-Explosion-163497506.html |title=Lightning Causes Compressor Explosion |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141227105411/http://www.wbng.com/news/local/Lightning-Causes-Compressor-Explosion-163497506.html |archivedate=December 27, 2014 }}</ref>
* An [[Enbridge]] crude oil pipeline ruptured in [[Grand Marsh, Wisconsin]], releasing an estimated 1,200 barrels of crude oil. The pipeline had been installed in 1998. Flaws in the longitudinal welds had been seen during X-ray checks of girth welds.<ref name="phmsa.dot.gov" /><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2012/07/29/enbridge-pipeline-idUSL2E8IT1AL20120729 |agency=Reuters |title=UPDATE 4-Enbridge to replace leaky Wisconsin oil pipeline Monday |date=July 29, 2012 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120730091407/https://www.reuters.com/article/2012/07/29/enbridge-pipeline-idUSL2E8IT1AL20120729 |archivedate=July 30, 2012 }}</ref>

* A jet fuel pipeline near [[Chicago]] began leaking on August 27. The burst pipeline spilled an estimated 42,000 gallons of jet fuel into a ditch that empties into the Calumet Sag Channel in Palos Heights, Illinois. External corrosion was the cause of the pipeline failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://ens-newswire.com/2012/08/28/jet-fuel-spill-near-chicago-closes-canal-highway/ |title=Jet Fuel Spill Near Chicago Closes Canal, Highway |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140708231445/http://ens-newswire.com/2012/08/28/jet-fuel-spill-near-chicago-closes-canal-highway/ |archivedate=July 8, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2012-5019H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320125019H/320125019H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_08302012.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211183702/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/reports/enforce/documents/320125019H/320125019H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_08302012.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://palos.patch.com/groups/politics-and-elections/p/pipeline-in-palos-park-was-corroded-company-rep |title=Pipeline in Palos Park Was Corroded: Company Rep |work=Palos, Illinois Patch |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028074633/http://palos.patch.com/groups/politics-and-elections/p/pipeline-in-palos-park-was-corroded-company-rep |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>

* The operator of an excavator machine narrowly escaped serious injury in [[Lewiston, Idaho]] on November 19, when his machine hit a gas pipeline during road work. The resulting fire destroyed a railroad signal, along with several telephone poles, and road construction equipment. The depth of the pipeline has been misjudged at that location.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.idahopress.com/news/state/gas-explosion-lights-the-sky-in-downtown-lewiston/article_64ad1772-32d5-11e2-9ddc-0019bb2963f4.html |title=Gas explosion lights the sky in downtown Lewiston |work=Idaho Press-Tribune |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150222123936/http://www.idahopress.com/news/state/gas-explosion-lights-the-sky-in-downtown-lewiston/article_64ad1772-32d5-11e2-9ddc-0019bb2963f4.html |archivedate=February 22, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.claimsjournal.com/news/west/2013/06/06/230308.htm |title=OSHA Fines Company Over Natural Gas Explosion |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141023190650/http://www.claimsjournal.com/news/west/2013/06/06/230308.htm |archivedate=October 23, 2014 }}</ref>
* On November 20, about 38,000 gallons of crude oil spilled from an [[Enbridge]] pipeline at a tank farm in [[Mokena, Illinois]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.businessweek.com/news/2012-11-21/bp-chicap-pipe-spilled-oil-at-illinois-tank-farm-filing-shows |title=BP Chicap Pipe Spilled Oil at Illinois Tank Farm, Filing Shows |author=Aaron Clark |work=Businessweek.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028143734/http://www.businessweek.com/news/2012-11-21/bp-chicap-pipe-spilled-oil-at-illinois-tank-farm-filing-shows |archivedate=October 28, 2013}}</ref>
* Two men were injured in an explosion and fire at a natural gas production facility east of [[Price, Utah]] on November 20.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://newsok.com/2-workers-hurt-in-natural-gas-explosion-near-price/article/feed/465555 |title=2 workers hurt in natural gas explosion near Price |work=NewsOK.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141021040712/http://newsok.com/2-workers-hurt-in-natural-gas-explosion-near-price/article/feed/465555 |archivedate=October 21, 2014 }}</ref>
* On November 23, a gas company worker looking for the source of a reported gas leak in a [[Springfield, Massachusetts]] strip club pierce a gas line. The gas later exploded, injuring 21, devastating the strip club, and damaging numerous nearby buildings.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.masslive.com/news/index.ssf/2012/11/claims_for_losses_continue_to.html |title=Claims for losses in Springfield explosion continue to mount |work=masslive.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.masslive.com/news/index.ssf/2012/11/claims_for_losses_continue_to.html |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On November 30, a heavy equipment operator punctured a 12-inch gas transmission pipeline, near the city of [[Madera, California]]. The adjacent highway, along with several rural roads, was shut down for hours, while houses and businesses in the area were evacuated.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://abclocal.go.com/kfsn/story?id=8904603|title=Hwy 99 reopens after a Madera County gas leak|work=ABC30 Fresno|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* A malfunction in a gas compressor caused a fire on December 4, north of [[Fort Worth, Texas]]. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=Pipeline Safety and Injuries {{!}} Explosion Burn Death Lawyers Hill Law Firm |url=http://www.rhlawgroup.com/blog/pipeline-safety-and-injuries-death/ |accessdate=28 November 2016 |date=22 January 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161128134248/http://www.rhlawgroup.com/blog/pipeline-safety-and-injuries-death/ |archivedate=November 28, 2016 }}</ref>
* On December 5, a 16-inch gas pipeline at 500&nbsp;psi of pressure exploded and burned near a natural gas plant in [[Goldsmith, Texas]]. A fireball 250 feet high was created after the explosion, destroying 12 to 15 utility poles, and caliche and rocks the size of bowling balls damaged a road. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.oaoa.com/news/fire_and_rescue/article_834541cc-3f60-11e2-9c44-001a4bcf6878.html|title=Pipe explodes near Goldsmith plant|work=Odessa American|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On December 11, at approximately 12:40pm, a 20-inch gas pipeline owned by [[NiSource Inc.]], parent of [[Columbia Gas Transmission|Columbia Gas]], exploded along I-77 between [[Sissonville, West Virginia|Sissonville]] and Pocatalico, West Virginia. Several people suffered minor injuries, four houses were destroyed, and other buildings were damaged. Early reports announced the NTSB was investigating as to why alarms in the control room for this pipeline did not sound for this failure.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.statejournal.com/story/20328434/explosion-highlights-pipeline-safety |title=WV explosion highlights pipeline safety |date=December 12, 2012 |work=statejournal.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://www.statejournal.com/story/20328434/explosion-highlights-pipeline-safety |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/12/11/sissonville-west-virginia-explosion_n_2279577.html?ir=Green |work=Huffington Post |title=PHOTOS: West Virginia Gas Line Explodes, Sends Flames Up To 75 Feet In The Air |date=December 11, 2012 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20121212045355/http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/12/11/sissonville-west-virginia-explosion_n_2279577.html?ir=Green |archivedate=December 12, 2012}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.register-herald.com/breakingnews/x1332354233/Gas-line-explodes-burns-homes-and-roads-near-Sissonville|archive-url=https://archive.is/20130201135453/http://www.register-herald.com/breakingnews/x1332354233/Gas-line-explodes-burns-homes-and-roads-near-Sissonville|dead-url=yes|archive-date=February 1, 2013|title=UPDATED: Gas line explodes, burns homes and roads|work=Beckley Register-Herald|accessdate=January 18, 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dailymail.com/News/201212120281|archiveurl=https://archive.is/20130121061246/http://www.dailymail.com/News/201212120281|deadurl=yes|title=No alarm in Columbia control room as fire raged&nbsp; - News - Charleston …|date=January 21, 2013|archivedate=January 21, 2013|publisher=}}</ref>
* On December 26, a 20-inch Florida Gas Transmission Company pipeline ruptured near [[Melbourne, Florida]], ejecting a 20-foot section of the pipeline. There was no fire or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 2-2012-1005H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220121005H/220121005H_CAO_12282012.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170215110210/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220121005H/220121005H_CAO_12282012.pdf |archivedate=February 15, 2017 }}</ref>

=== 2013 ===
* On January 1, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] line was overpressured by improper operation, causing a spill of about 5,500 gallons of petroleum product in [[Greensboro, North Carolina]]. About 1,000 gallons of product was not recovered.<ref name="dot5"/>
* On January 15, a utility crew struck and ruptured a 4-inch gas pipeline in [[Lewisville, Texas]], causing a nearby house to explode later on. The explosion killed a man.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dallasnews.com/news/community-news/lewisville-flower-mound/headlines/20130115-investigation-of-deadly-lewisville-explosion-continues.ece |title=Investigation of deadly Lewisville explosion continues |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141021015808/http://www.dallasnews.com/news/community-news/lewisville-flower-mound/headlines/20130115-investigation-of-deadly-lewisville-explosion-continues.ece |archivedate=October 21, 2014 }}</ref>
* An independent contractor installing fiber-optic cable for a cable company in [[Kansas City, Missouri]] inadvertently struck an underground gas line on February 19. Gas later caught fire, and created an explosion that destroyed a popular local restaurant, killing one of the workers there, and injuring about 15 others near the scene.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.multichannel.com/cable-operators/cable-contractor-involved-kc-gas-explosion/141835 |title=Cable Contractor Involved in KC Gas Explosion |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028112645/http://www.multichannel.com/cable-operators/cable-contractor-involved-kc-gas-explosion/141835 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kansascity.com/2013/08/15/4412750/osha-cites-drilling-company-restaurant.html |title=OSHA cites drilling company in fatal explosion at JJ's restaurant |work=kansascity |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131203080901/http://www.kansascity.com/2013/08/15/4412750/osha-cites-drilling-company-restaurant.html |archivedate=December 3, 2013 }}</ref>
* A tug towing a barge struck and ruptured a [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] LPG pipeline at [[Bayou Perot]], a marshy area on the borders of [[Jefferson Parish, Louisiana|Jefferson Parish]] and [[Lafourche Parish, Louisiana]] on March 12. The tug Captain was severely burned when the escaping gas ignited, and died several weeks later from those injuries.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2013/03/13/us-coastguard-idUSBRE92C0YB20130313 |agency=Reuters |title=Fire erupts after tug hits Chevron LPG pipeline: Coast Guard |date=March 13, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130326114349/https://www.reuters.com/article/2013/03/13/us-coastguard-idUSBRE92C0YB20130313 |archivedate=March 26, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.upi.com/Top_News/US/2013/04/11/Tug-captain-dies-of-burns-sustained-in-Louisiana-gas-explosion/UPI-68731365703619/ |title=Tug captain Chad Breaux dies of burns after Louisiana gas explosion |work=UPI |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.upi.com/Top_News/US/2013/04/11/Tug-captain-dies-of-burns-sustained-in-Louisiana-gas-explosion/UPI-68731365703619/ |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 8, pipeline equipment failure resulted in a spill of 6,000 barrels of crude oil, in eastern [[Columbia County, Arkansas]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.magnoliareporter.com/news_and_business/local_business/article_7203fa0e-1ae8-11e6-bcb6-dbbaed627cc2.html |title=Settlement reached in 2013 Columbia County case of 6,000-barrel oil spill from pipeline |author= |date= |work=Magnolia Reporter – Magnolia, Arkansas News |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160521041650/http://www.magnoliareporter.com/news_and_business/local_business/article_7203fa0e-1ae8-11e6-bcb6-dbbaed627cc2.html |archivedate=May 21, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 18, a [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] 8-inch petroleum products pipeline ruptured along a seam, spilling Diesel fuel into [[Willard Bay]] State Park near [[Ogden, Utah]]. Wildlife was coated with Diesel, but, the fuel was prevented from entering into water supply intakes. About 25,000 gallons of Diesel were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.sltrib.com/sltrib/news/56068519-78/state-pipeline-willard-diesel.html.csp |title=Utah Local News – Salt Lake City News, Sports, Archive – The Salt Lake Tribune |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020114840/http://www.sltrib.com/sltrib/news/56068519-78/state-pipeline-willard-diesel.html.csp |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 5-2013-5006H |url=http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/520135006H_cao_03222013.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170125195210/http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/520135006H_cao_03222013.pdf |archivedate=January 25, 2017 }}</ref>
* A [[Williams Companies]] 24-inch gas gathering pipeline failed in [[Marshall County, West Virginia]] on March 22. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2013/03/22/gas-pipeline-explosion-idUKL1N0CE9MO20130322 |agency=Reuters |title=UPDATE 1-Williams natgas line ruptures in West Virginia |date=March 22, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028000715/http://uk.reuters.com/article/2013/03/22/gas-pipeline-explosion-idUKL1N0CE9MO20130322 |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* The [[2013 Mayflower oil spill]] occurred when [[ExxonMobil]]'s 20-inch Pegasus crude oil pipeline spilled near [[Mayflower, Arkansas]] on March 29, causing crude to flow through yards and gutters, and towards [[Lake Conway]]. Wildlife was coated in some places. Twenty-two houses were evacuated, due to the fumes and fire hazard. Some estimates say the total amount spilled could reach upwards of 300,000 gallons of [[diluted bitumen]] were spilled. Hook cracks and extremely low impact toughness in the LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam of the pipe were identified as causes of the failure.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2013/04/09/rachel-maddow-mayflower-oil-spill-exxon_n_3047331.html?ir=Green |work=Huffington Post |first=Nick |last=Visser |title=Maddow Slams Exxon's 'Paper Towel' Cleanup Efforts |date=April 9, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130412104754/http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2013/04/09/rachel-maddow-mayflower-oil-spill-exxon_n_3047331.html?ir=Green |archivedate=April 12, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://arkansasmatters.com/fulltext?nxd_id=649812 |title=Web Extra: Background on Pipeline that Ruptured Near Mayflower |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=bot: unknown |archiveurl=https://archive.is/20130410125438/http://arkansasmatters.com/fulltext?nxd_id=649812 |archivedate=April 10, 2013 |df= }}</ref><ref>[http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/File/4%202013%205006H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_4%2002%2013.pdf]{{dead link|date=May 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.thv11.com/news/article/271392/2/Exxon-Cause-of-pipeline-failure--manufacturing-defects |title=Exxon: Cause of pipeline failure 'manufacturing defects' |author= |date=July 10, 2013 |website=Thv11.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028010051/http://www.thv11.com/news/article/271392/2/Exxon-Cause-of-pipeline-failure--manufacturing-defects |archivedate=October 28, 2013}}</ref>
* On April 4, an explosion and fire occurred at a gas compressor station near [[Guthrie, Oklahoma]]. Nearby houses were evacuated. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.koco.com/news/oklahomanews/okc/Employee-ran-1-mile-to-escape-Guthrie-natural-gas-explosion/-/11777584/19629714/-/ols82jz/-/index.html |title=Employee ran 1 mile to escape Guthrie natural gas explosion |work=koco |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131028110217/http://www.koco.com/news/oklahomanews/okc/Employee-ran-1-mile-to-escape-Guthrie-natural-gas-explosion/-/11777584/19629714/-/ols82jz/-/index.html |archivedate=October 28, 2013 }}</ref>
* A flash fire at a pipeline gas compressor station broke out when natural gas liquids ignited in [[Tyler County, West Virginia]] on April 11, seriously burning three workers, two of whom later died. The workers were performing pipeline pigging operations.<ref>[http://www.therepublic.com/view/story/af39190844784b7eac485e85c9b9522d/WV--Gas-Explosion]{{dead link|date=May 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wtov9.com/news/news/2nd-worker-dies-result-tyler-co-pipeline-explosion/nXNHz/ |title=Archived copy |accessdate=April 16, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130714111743/http://www.wtov9.com/news/news/2nd-worker-dies-result-tyler-co-pipeline-explosion/nXNHz/ |archivedate=July 14, 2013}}</ref>
* On April 30, the Pegasus oil pipeline spilled a small amount of crude into a residential yard in Ripley County, Missouri, a month after the same pipe spewed thousands of barrels of crude in Arkansas. The Pegasus pipeline was out of service from the [[Mayflower, Arkansas]] spill, accounting for the minimal amount of oil spilled in Missouri.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2013/05/01/exxon-pipeline-spill-idUSL2N0DI14U20130501 |agency=Reuters |title=Exxon says Missouri oil spills from already-ruptured Pegasus line |date=May 1, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150924180945/https://www.reuters.com/article/2013/05/01/exxon-pipeline-spill-idUSL2N0DI14U20130501 |archivedate=September 24, 2015 }}</ref>
* On May 9, Diesel fuel was detected to be leaking from a Marathon pipeline in [[Indianapolis, Indiana]]. Over 20,000 gallons of Diesel leaked, at a slow rate that was not detected by SCADA systems. Cleanup cause a nearby major road to be shut down for five days.
