There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|title=Report: Copper wire to blame for 2013 20K-gallon pipeline leak on nor… |url=http://www.theindychannel.com/news/call-6-investigators/report-copper-wire-to-blame-for-2013-20k-gallon-pipeline-leak-on-northwest-side |website=archive.is |accessdate=28 November 2016 |date=28 November 2016 |deadurl=bot: unknown |archiveurl=https://archive.is/20161128012639/http://www.theindychannel.com/news/call-6-investigators/report-copper-wire-to-blame-for-2013-20k-gallon-pipeline-leak-on-northwest-side |archivedate=November 28, 2016 |df= }}</ref>
* Late night on May 14, an explosion and fire hit a [[Williams Companies]] gas compressor station near [[Brooklyn Township, Pennsylvania]]. There were no reported injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wbng.com/news/local/Late-night-gas-compression-explosion-207490961.html |title=DEP: Compressor stations shows signs of explosion |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150220130422/http://www.wbng.com/news/local/Late-night-gas-compression-explosion-207490961.html |archivedate=February 20, 2015 }}</ref>
* On May 8, the Kinder Morgan Tejas pipeline compressor station near Crockett, Texas, required an emergency shutdown and subsequently had a fire that caused $7,502,188 in property damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/StatePages/Texas.htm |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141221194813/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/StatePages/Texas.htm |archivedate=December 21, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://alerts.skytruth.org/report/05f2642d-8a93-3b6f-bbac-9c57a37b |title=Skytruth Alert: NRC Report: Natural Gas near Crockett, TX 2013-05-08 |work=SkyTruth Alerts |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140813133342/http://alerts.skytruth.org/report/05f2642d-8a93-3b6f-bbac-9c57a37b |archivedate=August 13, 2014 }}</ref>
* On May 18, a 24 inch fill line failed, on an [[Enbridge]] tank, in [[Cushing, Oklahoma]], spilling about 105,000 gallons of crude oil. The cause was internal corrosion of the line.<ref>[https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Enbridge_2013_05_17.pdf Failure Investigation Report – Enbridge Pipelines, LLC, Tank 3013 24-inch Fill Line failure in Cushing, OK
]</ref>
* On May 30, two construction workers were injured, when a fire erupted during welding at a [[Williams Companies]] natural gas facility in [[Hunterdon County, New Jersey]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mycentraljersey.com/article/20130530/NJNEWS/305300063/?gcheck=1 |title=News – MyCentralJersey.com – mycentraljersey.com |work=MyCentralJersey.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141024102014/http://www.mycentraljersey.com/article/20130530/NJNEWS/305300063/?gcheck=1 |archivedate=October 24, 2014}}</ref>
* A 12-inch gas transmission pipeline failed near [[Torrington, Wyoming]] on June 13. LF-[[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam failure was suspected as cause. There was no fire or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 5-2013-1007H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/520131007H/520131007H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06192013_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170218004152/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/reports/enforce/documents/520131007H/520131007H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_06192013_text.pdf |archivedate=February 18, 2017 }}</ref>
* On June 18, in Washington Parish, Louisiana, a [[Kinder Morgan]] Florida Gas Transmission Company 30" diameter pipeline ruptured and exploded before dawn, jolting residents out of their beds. No one was seriously hurt but 55 homes were evacuated. The blast knocked down trees in an area about 200 yards across and the fire burned those within another 300 yards. "The ground around the crater is completely bare. The dirt around it is just like it had been cooked in a kiln," and an 80-foot section of pipe was destroyed.<ref>{{cite web|title=Gas line explosion rattles Washington Parish {{!}} Home {{!}} The Advocate — … |url=http://theadvocate.com/home/6283023-125/gas-pipeline-explosion-in-franklinton |website=archive.is |accessdate=28 November 2016 |date=3 October 2014 |deadurl=bot: unknown |archiveurl=https://archive.is/20141003145848/http://theadvocate.com/home/6283023-125/gas-pipeline-explosion-in-franklinton |archivedate=October 3, 2014 |df= }}</ref>
* On July 4, a fire involved a gas compressor and a nearby ruptured 2-inch gas pipeline in [[Gilmore Township, Pennsylvania]]. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.observer-reporter.com/article/20130705/NEWS02/130709662/-1/NEWS#.Uf3z46y0SB8 |title=Observer-Reporter – Blaze hits compressor station in Gilmore Township |work=Observer-Reporter |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020213054/http://www.observer-reporter.com/article/20130705/NEWS02/130709662/-1/NEWS |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* An 8-inch natural gas pipeline released gas from a rupture at 1,400&nbsp;psi, for 90 minutes in [[New Franklin, Ohio]] on July 22, forcing 75 people to evacuate the area. Afterward, the local Fire Chief said that pipeline owners refused to give information to first responders in previous requests.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ohio.com/news/city-not-privy-to-pipeline-locations-inside-own-borders-1.418507 |title=City not privy to pipeline locations inside own borders |author=Kathy Antoniotti |work=www.ohio.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141023135458/http://www.ohio.com/news/city-not-privy-to-pipeline-locations-inside-own-borders-1.418507 |archivedate=October 23, 2014 }}</ref>
* Early on July 23, a downed 13,000 volt power line sparked a massive gas fire in [[Mamaroneck, New York]] when a gas main was damaged by the electricity. Three automobiles were destroyed, and houses were threatened for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://newyork.cbslocal.com/2013/07/23/fire-crews-battle-blaze-in-mamaroneck/ |title=Downed Wires Lead To Car Fires, Ruptured Gas Line In Mamaroneck " CBS New York |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150919122910/http://newyork.cbslocal.com/2013/07/23/fire-crews-battle-blaze-in-mamaroneck/ |archivedate=September 19, 2015 }}</ref>
* On July 26, a leaking [[BP]] 20-inch crude oil pipeline spilled 50 to 100 barrels of crude oil in [[Washington County, Oklahoma]]. Some of the crude spilled into a drainage ditch leading to a water reservoir.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.newson6.com/story/22944566/crews-working-to-halt-bp-pipeline-leak-in-washington-county |title=Crews Work To Contain BP Pipeline Leak In Osage County |date=July 26, 2013 |work=newson6.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.newson6.com/story/22944566/crews-working-to-halt-bp-pipeline-leak-in-washington-county |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On the evening of August 12, a 10-inch NGL pipeline exploded and caused a massive propane-ethane mix fire in [[Erie, Illinois]]. A number of nearby residents were evacuated for a while, but, there were no injuries. About 772,000 gallons of mix were burned or lost. The cause was from a manufacturing defect.<ref name="ReferenceA">{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31618.html?nocache=6119#_Incidents_tab_5 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications - Operator Information |work=dot.gov |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161227132036/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31618.html?nocache=6119 |archivedate=December 27, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://thinkprogress.org/natural-gas-pipeline-causes-cornfield-to-explode-in-western-illinois-df1277613184#.irjwewihn|title=Natural Gas Pipeline Causes Cornfield To Explode In Western Illinois|first=Ryan|last=Koronowski|date=August 13, 2013|work=thinkprogress.org}}</ref>
* A leak developed on a valve on [[Longhorn Pipeline]] in [[Austin, Texas]] during maintenance on August 14, spilling about 300 gallons of crude oil. There were no evacuations.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.keyetv.com/news/features/top-stories/stories/pipeline-releases-oil-circle-c-neighborhood-11233.shtml |title=Search Results – KEYE-TV Austin |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130827010346/http://www.keyetv.com/news/features/top-stories/stories/pipeline-releases-oil-circle-c-neighborhood-11233.shtml |archivedate=August 27, 2013}}</ref>
* Atmos Energy crews dug into a 4-inch gas pipeline in [[Overland Park, Kansas]] on September 2, causing an explosion and fire. There was no major damage or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://fox4kc.com/2013/09/21/update-to-gas-explosion-in-overland-park/ |title=Update to gas explosion in Overland Park |work=fox4kc.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141021045317/http://fox4kc.com/2013/09/21/update-to-gas-explosion-in-overland-park/ |archivedate=October 21, 2014 }}</ref>
* A 10-inch gas gathering pipeline ruptured and burned in [[Newton County, Texas]] on September 21. About a dozen people from nearby houses were evacuated for a time. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.beaumontenterprise.com/news/article/Gas-line-not-yet-repaired-after-explosion-in-Buna-4838918.php |title=Gas line not yet repaired after explosion in Buna |work=Beaumont Enterprise |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020224732/http://www.beaumontenterprise.com/news/article/Gas-line-not-yet-repaired-after-explosion-in-Buna-4838918.php |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>
* On September 24, a Denton TX city water utility worker ruptured a 1/2-inch gas pipeline in [[Denton, Texas]], which immediately caused a fire that gave the worker minor burns. There was no other significant damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dentonrc.com/local-news/local-news-headlines/20130924-city-worker-hits-gas-line.ece |title=City worker hits gas line |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150923213624/http://www.dentonrc.com/local-news/local-news-headlines/20130924-city-worker-hits-gas-line.ece |archivedate=September 23, 2015 }}</ref>
* A farmer near [[Tioga, North Dakota]] smelled oil for several days, before discovering a leaking 6-inch 20-year-old [[Tesoro]] pipeline under his wheat field, on September 29. Crews tried to burn off the oil at first. The spill size was estimated at 865,000 gallons, and covered over seven acres. There were no injuries. Corrosion was suspected as being the cause. Governor Jack Dalrymple said he wasn't told of the spill until October 9. In May 2014, it was announced that it would 2 1/2 more years before the spilled crude would be cleaned up.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.yahoo.com/corrosion-may-led-north-dakota-pipeline-leak-regulator-185854060--finance.html |title=Corrosion may have led to North Dakota pipeline leak: regulator |date=October 11, 2013 |work=Yahoo! News |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141023215903/http://news.yahoo.com/corrosion-may-led-north-dakota-pipeline-leak-regulator-185854060--finance.html |archivedate=October 23, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.greenfieldreporter.com/view/story/121ae083847f4744a934a459c9e0d09d/ND--ND-Pipeline-Break-Cleanup |title=Archived copy |accessdate=June 14, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150615215044/http://www.greenfieldreporter.com/view/story/121ae083847f4744a934a459c9e0d09d/ND--ND-Pipeline-Break-Cleanup |archivedate=June 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On October 7, a gas pipeline burst in [[Howard County, Texas]]. There was no fire, but, dangerous hydrogen sulfide in the gas forced evacuations of nearby residents. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.newswest9.com/story/23630636/officials-working-pipeline-explosion-in-howard-county |title=No Injuries Reported After Pipeline Explosion in Howard County |date=October 7, 2013 |work=newswest9.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.newswest9.com/story/23630636/officials-working-pipeline-explosion-in-howard-county |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 7, authorities were notified of a Lion Oil Trading and Transportation crude oil pipeline leak in [[Columbia County, Arkansas]]. It was estimated that the leak started on September 21. Oil spread into a Horsehead Creek tributary.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.magnoliareporter.com/news_and_business/local_news/article_af1148dc-32b2-11e3-b1ce-001a4bcf887a.html|title=(With video and three photos) Oil spill cleanup continues along Horsehead Creek tributary near Macedonia|work=Magnolia Reporter – Magnolia, Arkansas News|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* A 30-inch Northern Natural Gas pipeline exploded and burned in [[Harper County, Oklahoma]] on October 8. 220 feet of the pipe was ejected from the ground. Flames were seen for a number of miles, and four houses nearby were evacuated. Oklahoma Highway 283 was closed for several hours until the fire was determined to be under control and safe. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.news9.com/story/23650973/resident-recalls-pipeline |title=Resident Describes Gas Line Explosion In Harper County |date=October 9, 2013 |work=news9.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160126063036/http://www.news9.com/story/23650973/resident-recalls-pipeline |archivedate=January 26, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.csmonitor.com/Environment/Latest-News-Wires/2013/1009/Pipeline-explosion-shoots-flames-into-Oklahoma-sky |title=Pipeline explosion shoots flames into Oklahoma sky |author= |work=The Christian Science Monitor |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140727160959/http://www.csmonitor.com/Environment/Latest-News-Wires/2013/1009/Pipeline-explosion-shoots-flames-into-Oklahoma-sky |archivedate=July 27, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2013-1016H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420131016H/420131016H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_10112013_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161223045225/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420131016H/420131016H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_10112013_text.pdf |archivedate=December 23, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 29, a [[Koch Industries]] 8-inch pipeline spill about 400 barrels of crude oil near [[Smithville, Texas]]. The oil polluted a private stock pond and two overflow reservoirs.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kvue.com/news/local/Officials-cleaning-up-400-barrel-oil-spill-near-Smithville-229756751.html |title=Archived copy |accessdate=October 30, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131031131030/http://www.kvue.com/news/local/Officials-cleaning-up-400-barrel-oil-spill-near-Smithville-229756751.html |archivedate=October 31, 2013}}</ref>
* A [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] operated 10-inch LPG pipeline was ruptured by contractors for the company installing a [[Cathodic protection]] system, near [[Milford, Texas]], on November 14, causing a large fire, and forcing the evacuation of Milford and 200 students of a nearby school. A nearby 14-inch pipeline was threatened by the failure, but did not fail. There were no injuries reported. About 183,000 gallons of propane burned.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kwtx.com/home/headlines/Gas-Line-Explosion-Reported-In-Rural-Central-Texas-231914001.html?ref=001 |title=Small Town Residents Allowed To Return After Fiery Blast |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141021130907/http://www.kwtx.com/home/headlines/Gas-Line-Explosion-Reported-In-Rural-Central-Texas-231914001.html?ref=001 |archivedate=October 21, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://in.reuters.com/article/2013/11/14/energy-pipeline-explosion-idINL2N0IZ1F320131114 |agency=Reuters |title=UPDATE 4-Chevron pipeline explodes, burns in rural Texas |date=November 14, 2013 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131212133736/http://in.reuters.com/article/2013/11/14/energy-pipeline-explosion-idINL2N0IZ1F320131114 |archivedate=December 12, 2013 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF 4-2014-5012 |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420145012/420145012_NOPV%20PCP%20PCO_05212014_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211164926/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420145012/420145012_NOPV%20PCP%20PCO_05212014_text.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_2731.html?nocache=116#_Incidents_tab_4 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications - Operator Information |work=dot.gov |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161227132020/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_2731.html?nocache=116 |archivedate=December 27, 2016 }}</ref>
* An [[ExxonMobil]] gas plant exploded and burned on November 17, near [[Kingsville, Texas]]. The plant burned for over a day, but there were no reported injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kiiitv.com/story/24003322/exxonmobils-king-ranch-gas-plant-continues-burning-after-overnight-fire |title=ExxonMobil's King Ranch Gas Plant Continues Burning – KiiiTV.com South Texas, Corpus Christi, Coastal Bend |date=November 18, 2013 |work=kiiitv.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.kiiitv.com/story/24003322/exxonmobils-king-ranch-gas-plant-continues-burning-after-overnight-fire |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On November 18, a gas pipeline burst near [[Ranger, Texas]], causing a fire in a field, with flames reaching 100 feet high. Some houses nearby were evacuated for a time. The owner of the pipeline, Hanlon Gas, had been installing a new compressor station, and they believe a malfunction led to the rupture and fire. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.bigcountryhomepage.com/story/gas-pipeline-rupture-send-flames-100-feet-into-air/d/story/cFdS71R_kEeMi0TUv8vasw |title=Gas Pipeline Rupture Send Flames 100 Feet Into Air |agency=Associated Press |work=BigCountryHomepage |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141023113953/http://www.bigcountryhomepage.com/story/gas-pipeline-rupture-send-flames-100-feet-into-air/d/story/cFdS71R_kEeMi0TUv8vasw |archivedate=October 23, 2014}}</ref>
* On November 28 a 30-inch Panhandle Eastern natural gas pipeline exploded in [[Hughesville, Missouri]] causing several nearby buildings to catch fire. There was a local evacuation but no injuries. Metallurgical examination determined the root cause of the failure to be corrosion.<ref name="dot3"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://fox4kc.com/2013/11/29/reported-pipeline-explosion-rocks-parts-of-missouri/ |title=Pipeline explosion sends fireball 300 feet into air |work=fox4kc.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150103231722/http://fox4kc.com/2013/11/29/reported-pipeline-explosion-rocks-parts-of-missouri/ |archivedate=January 3, 2015 }}</ref>
* On December 9, a 2-inch pipe on a propane dehydrator failed at the Dixie Pipeline Terminal in [[Apex, North Carolina]], forcing evacuations and sheltering in place at nearby businesses. There was no fire or explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wncn.com/story/24171804/gas-line-leak-reported-in-apex |title=Archived copy |accessdate=December 10, 2013 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20131213094441/http://www.wncn.com/story/24171804/gas-line-leak-reported-in-apex |archivedate=December 13, 2013}}</ref>
* A [[Sunoco]] pipeline was found leaking gasoline on December 20, near [[Coal Township, Pennsylvania]], from external corrosion. About 266 to 471 gallons of product were spilled, and, 1,421 tons of soil were removed, as part of the remediation of that leak.<ref>http://www.newsitem.com/news/2017-07-29/Today%27s_Top_Stories/Sunoco_fined_65000_for_pipeline_leak.html</ref>
* On December 27, two natural gas company workers had minor burns when the pipeline they were working leaked, and the escaping gas exploded and ignited in [[Shrewsbury, Massachusetts]]. Flames 30 feet high knocked out phone service in the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.telegram.com/article/20131227/NEWS/312279749/1116 |title=Crews respond to gas-line fire in Shrewsbury |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020142812/http://www.telegram.com/article/20131227/NEWS/312279749/1116 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref>

=== 2014 ===
* On January 7, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] line leak from equipment failure in [[Fountain Inn, South Carolina]], spilling about 52,000 gallons of petroleum product, of which around 8,000 gallons was not recovered.<ref name="dot5"/>
* On January 10, a 12-inch PSNC gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned in [[Asheville, North Carolina]]. The cause was damage to the pipeline during installation in 2003. There were no injuries, but the costs of property damage was around $825,000.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.citizen-times.com/article/20140211/NEWS01/302110026/Asheville-gas-line-explosion-cost-825-000?nclick_check=1|archive-url=https://archive.is/20140213195836/http://www.citizen-times.com/article/20140211/NEWS01/302110026/Asheville-gas-line-explosion-cost-825-000?nclick_check=1|dead-url=yes|archive-date=February 13, 2014|title=Ashevill gas line explosion costs $825,000|work=The Asheville Citizen-Times|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On February 10, a gas pipeline exploded and burned near [[Tioga, North Dakota]]. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.greenfieldreporter.com/view/story/9f9d80ef83364d64818f3134913f172a/ND--Tioga-Gas-Explosion |title=Archived copy |accessdate=February 13, 2014 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140222133632/http://www.greenfieldreporter.com/view/story/9f9d80ef83364d64818f3134913f172a/ND--Tioga-Gas-Explosion |archivedate=February 22, 2014}}</ref>
* On February 13, a 30-inch diameter Columbia Gulf Transmission gas pipeline carrying natural gas exploded near [[Knifley, Kentucky]], sending two people to the hospital with injuries, destroying two houses, and alarming residents, who saw flames from miles away. Later, it was determined that [[Hydrogen embrittlement]] had caused the pipe failure from when the pipeline was installed in 1965.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.wdrb.com/story/26571543/analysis-existing-cracks-a-cause-in-kentucky-pipeline-blast |date=September 18, 2014 |publisher=WorldNow and WDRB |title=Analysis: Existing cracks a cause in Kentucky pipeline blast |author=Marcus Green |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140920210310/http://www.wdrb.com/story/26571543/analysis-existing-cracks-a-cause-in-kentucky-pipeline-blast |archivedate=September 20, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Ky. gas line blast injures 2, destroys 2 homes |url=http://www.kansas.com/2014/02/13/3286103/ky-gas-line-blast-hospitalizes.html |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140222031345/http://www.kansas.com/2014/02/13/3286103/ky-gas-line-blast-hospitalizes.html |archivedate=February 22, 2014}}</ref>
* On February 19, a leaking gas main caused a gas build up in a nearby rowhouse, that exploded in [Baltimore, Maryland], killing one youth, and seriously injuring another walking by the area. 3 other people had minor injuries. The area on the gas main near the leak had been patch twice in previous months.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.naturalgaswatch.org/?p=2909 |title=Boy killed as house collapsed was planning to attend birthday party - Natural Gas Watch.org |work=naturalgaswatch.org |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160806225622/http://www.naturalgaswatch.org/?p=2909 |archivedate=August 6, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.cnn.com/videos/politics/2016/05/28/rene-marsh-aging-pipelines.cnn |title=America's aging pipelines – CNN Video |work=cnn.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160916070015/http://www.cnn.com/videos/politics/2016/05/28/rene-marsh-aging-pipelines.cnn |archivedate=September 16, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 6, contractors working for [[Shell Oil Company]] hit Shell's Houston-to-Houma (Ho-Ho) crude oil pipeline near [[Port Neches, Texas]], spilling 364 barrels of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.bayoubuzz.com/top-stories/item/623940-shell-says-ho-ho-pipeline-shut-after-leak-in-texas |title=Archived copy |accessdate=March 10, 2014 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140310083055/http://www.bayoubuzz.com/top-stories/item/623940-shell-says-ho-ho-pipeline-shut-after-leak-in-texas |archivedate=March 10, 2014}}</ref>
* '''[[2014 East Harlem gas explosion]]''': On March 12, there was a gas explosion in [[New York City]], [[New York (state)|New York]]. NTSB investigators found natural gas in the soil nearby, indicating that the gas leak had existed for a while before the explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://newyork.cbslocal.com/2014/03/14/firefighters-continue-search-for-missing-at-east-harlem-blast-site/ |title=NTSB: Abnormal Concentration Of Gas Found Near East Harlem Blast Scene |publisher=CBS New York |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141026110131/http://newyork.cbslocal.com/2014/03/14/firefighters-continue-search-for-missing-at-east-harlem-blast-site/ |archivedate=October 26, 2014 }}</ref>
* On March 18, a 20-inch Mid-Valley Pipeline Company pipeline failed in [[Hamilton County, Ohio]], spilling at least 364 barrels of crude oil into the adjacent [[Oak Glen Nature Preserve]]. Animals in the area were affected.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wlwt.com/news/oil-spill-cleanup-ending-20-salamanders-being-cared-for-offsite/25314396 |title=Oil spill cleanup ending; 20 salamanders being cared for off-site |work=WLWT.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141020114846/http://www.wlwt.com/news/oil-spill-cleanup-ending-20-salamanders-being-cared-for-offsite/25314396 |archivedate=October 20, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2014-5002H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320145002H/320145002H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_03252014_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161221122258/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320145002H/320145002H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_03252014_text.pdf |archivedate=December 21, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 18, a 3-inch, half-mile flare waste gas pipeline in a neighborhood in [[Arvin, California]], was discovered leaking, a few blocks from Arvin High School, in a residential area. It had been leaking for as long as two years.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.bakersfieldcalifornian.com/local/x588887534/Arvin-still-in-the-dark-about-leaking-gas-line |title=Arvin still in the dark about leaking gas line |work=The Bakersfield Californian |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141023135500/http://www.bakersfieldcalifornian.com/local/x588887534/Arvin-still-in-the-dark-about-leaking-gas-line |archivedate=October 23, 2014 }}</ref>
* On March 31, a pipeline running to a [[Williams Companies]] LNG storage facility in [[Plymouth, Washington]] exploded and sent shrapnel flying that ruptured an LNG storage tank. Nearly 1,000 residents were evacuated and at least five employees at the facility were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://thinkprogress.org/climate/2014/03/31/3421102/massive-explosion-natural-gas-plant/ |title=Massive Explosion Rocks Washington State Natural Gas Plant |publisher=thinkprogress.com |date=March 31, 2014 |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150114230930/http://thinkprogress.org/climate/2014/03/31/3421102/massive-explosion-natural-gas-plant/ |archivedate=January 14, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://co.williams.com/williams/news-media/plymouth-wa-update/ |title=Archived copy |accessdate=June 23, 2014 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140701204335/http://co.williams.com/williams/news-media/plymouth-wa-update/ |archivedate=July 1, 2014}}</ref>
* A 12-inch [[Williams Companies]] gas pipeline failed at a weld in [[Moundsville, West Virginia]]. The following explosion and fire explosion scorched trees over a 2-acre area near Moundsville. Several houses were evacuated as a precaution. There were no injuries reported.<ref>{{cite web|title=Company won't be cited for W.Va. pipeline blast |url=http://www.theintermountain.com/page/content.detail/id/493996/Company-won-t-be-cited-for-W-Va--pipeline-blast.html?isap=1&nav=5023 |accessdate=October 30, 2016 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://archive.is/20140517130357/http://www.theintermountain.com/page/content.detail/id/493996/Company-won-t-be-cited-for-W-Va--pipeline-blast.html?isap=1&nav=5023 |archivedate=May 17, 2014 |df= }}</ref>
* On April 17, a private excavator accidentally cut a gas line while doing some work in [[Union Township, Licking County, Ohio]] on April 17. The man suffered second degree burns to the upper portion of his body. There was no damage to any buildings.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.newarkadvocate.com/article/20140417/NEWS01/304170014/Natural-gas-line-ruptures-Union-Township-man-taken-hospital |title=Natural gas line ruptures in Union Township; man taken to hospital |work=The Newark Advocate |date=April 17, 2014 |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006083948/http://www.newarkadvocate.com/article/20140417/NEWS01/304170014/Natural-gas-line-ruptures-Union-Township-man-taken-hospital |archivedate=October 6, 2014}}</ref>
* On April 23, an explosion and fire hit a [[Williams Companies]] gas processing plant in [[Opal, Wyoming]]. All 95 residents of the town were evacuated, and part of US Highway 30 was closed for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.localnews8.com/news/explosion-and-fire-force-evacuation-of-town/25627492 |title=Archived copy |accessdate=May 15, 2014 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140517122251/http://www.localnews8.com/news/explosion-and-fire-force-evacuation-of-town/25627492 |archivedate=May 17, 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://trib.com/news/state-and-regional/fire-still-burns-at-damaged-wyoming-gas-plant/article_67b11cdf-0b76-53b9-8050-a2504d3e2e3d.html |title=Fire still burns at damaged Wyoming gas plant |agency=Associated Press |work=Casper Star-Tribune Online |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141016114009/http://trib.com/news/state-and-regional/fire-still-burns-at-damaged-wyoming-gas-plant/article_67b11cdf-0b76-53b9-8050-a2504d3e2e3d.html |archivedate=October 16, 2014 }}</ref>
* On May 6, [[Sinclair Oil Corporation]] pipeline operators detected a pressure drop on a pipeline, with the problem being traced two days later to a leak in [[Knox County, Missouri]]. A mixture of gasoline and Diesel fuel contaminated soil on a farm.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nemonews.net/2014/05/08/pipeline-rupture-hazardous-material-spill-knox/ |title=Pipeline Rupture, Hazardous Material Spill in Knox |work=nemonews.net |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141021071252/http://nemonews.net/2014/05/08/pipeline-rupture-hazardous-material-spill-knox/ |archivedate=October 21, 2014 }}</ref>
* On May 12, three workers from [[Plantation Pipeline]] inadvertently ruptured their pipeline at a pump station in [[Anderson County, South Carolina]], causing a geyser of gasoline, and spraying the workers with it. There was no fire, but the workers had to be decontaminated at a hospital.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wyff4.com/news/natural-gas-line-ruptures-in-anderson-county/25935562 |title=Gas line ruptures, 150-foot geyser of gas spews onto workers |work=WYFF4 |date=May 13, 2014 |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140717072505/http://www.wyff4.com/news/natural-gas-line-ruptures-in-anderson-county/25935562 |archivedate=July 17, 2014 }}</ref>
* On May 17, at [[Port St. John, Florida]], Kinder Morgan's 36" Florida Gas Transmission pipeline ruptured, forcing evacuation of 7 homes and halting train traffic through Brevard Co. for 3 hours near the Florida Power & Light plant. Florida Gas Transmission workers searched for a leak when pressure dropped in the line. Homes, vehicle & train traffic were reopened after the remaining gas escaped from the pipe.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.floridatoday.com/story/news/local/2014/05/17/gas-leak-prompts-evacuations-in-north-cocoa/9210351/,|title=Port St. John gas line rupture under investigation|publisher=}}</ref> This pipeline failure caused $177,321 in property damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/Operatorlist.html#. |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |website=Primis.phmsa.dot.gov |accessdate=January 19, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160128103932/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorList.html |archivedate=January 28, 2016 }}</ref>
* On June 26, near [[East Bernard, Texas]], a gas pipeline adjacent to a [[Kinder Morgan]] gas compressor plant blew out, destroying the roadway and setting a nearby truck on fire just south of Highway 59. Flames as high as 150 feet were shooting out of the pipeline. The focus was on a 27-inch pipeline that sends gasoline to different tank farms along the line.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://abc13.com/news/gas-line-explosion-sends-150-foot-flames-up-in-air/142620/ |title=Wharton County gas line explosion sends 150-foot flames up in air |work=ABC13 Houston |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |date=May 13, 2014 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006072131/http://abc13.com/news/gas-line-explosion-sends-150-foot-flames-up-in-air/142620/ |archivedate=October 6, 2014 }}</ref>
* On July 10, a vent stack at a Williams Field Services gas pipeline compressor station in [[Susquehanna County, Pennsylvania]] caught fire. Only minor damage was reported at other parts of the station.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://golackawanna.com/news/local-news-news/1523876/Susquehanna-County-compressor-station-shut-down-after-morning-fire#.U-Xv7aNQjTo |title=Susquehanna County compressor station shut down after morning fire |author= |work=Times Leader |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |date=July 10, 2014 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141021154242/http://golackawanna.com/news/local-news-news/1523876/Susquehanna-County-compressor-station-shut-down-after-morning-fire |archivedate=October 21, 2014}}</ref>
* On July 23, in [[Milledgeville, Georgia]], Midway Elementary School faculty and staff were evacuated due to a fire, caused by a gas leak at nearby Southern Natural Gas Co. tap station. Fire rescue personnel closed down Highway 441 South for an hour. Due to the amount of pressure, precautionary measures were taken so pipe wouldn't rupture under the road while Southern Natural Gas tried to determine the cause of the leak. "It could be some type of failure in a valve or regulator. Right now we don't know but Southern Natural Gas is looking into it." No injuries were reported.<ref>Felicia Cummings, "Gas leak near Midway Elementary," The Union-Recorder, July 23, 2014 4:15 pm | Updated: August 7, 2014.</ref>
* On August 4, a Greka 6 inch pipeline spilled over 1,200 gallons of crude oil at the Zick Compressor Station by Williams Field Services in Hop Bottom near [[Santa Barbara County, California]]. The oil spread out over less than a mile from the leak and did not enter a river. The station can process 455&nbsp;million cubic feet of natural gas per day.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ksby.com/news/update-crews-contain-oil-spill-near-santa-maria/ |title=Crews contain oil spill near Santa Maria |work=KSBY.com |date=August 4, 2014 |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150205054839/http://www.ksby.com/news/update-crews-contain-oil-spill-near-santa-maria/ |archivedate=February 5, 2015}}</ref>
* On August 12, a mulching machine hit a 12-inch natural gas pipeline in [[Rusk County, Texas]]. The operator of the machine was killed in the following explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ketknbc.com/news/one-man-killed-in-natural-gas-pipeline-explosion-i |title=White Oak man killed in Rusk Co. pipeline explosion |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150222125425/http://www.ketknbc.com/news/one-man-killed-in-natural-gas-pipeline-explosion-i |archivedate=February 22, 2015}}</ref>
* On August 20, a Buckeye Partners pipeline leaked, inside their terminal, in [[Linden, New Jersey]]. About 5900 gallons of jet fuel was spilled, of which most was recovered. The cause of the leak was from internal corrosion of the line.<ref>https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/147585_Buckeye_Linden_Failure_Investigation_Report_2014_08_20.pdf</ref>
* On August 21, four workers were injured in a fire while a crew was performing maintenance on a natural gas pipeline in [[Garvin County, Oklahoma]]. The injured workers were treated and released from a hospital, and there was no explosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.tulsaworld.com/business/energy/four-hurt-after-natural-gas-line-catches-fire-near-lindsay/article_09948ed6-442c-5451-b266-c1041e0ae427.html|title=Four hurt after natural gas line catches fire near Lindsay|work=Tulsa World|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref>
* On September 14, a contract worker performing routine maintenance on a [[Chevron Corporation|Chevron]] offshore gas pipeline was killed, and two other workers were injured. The accident occurred 6 miles south of [[Timbalier Bay]] off the southeast coast of Louisiana.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://online.wsj.com/articles/chevron-worker-dies-in-gulf-of-mexico-pipeline-accident-1410709059 |title=Chevron Shuts Gas Pipeline After Worker Dies in Gulf of Mexico Accident – WSJ |author=Lynn Cook |date=September 15, 2014 |work=WSJ |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140919073950/http://online.wsj.com/articles/chevron-worker-dies-in-gulf-of-mexico-pipeline-accident-1410709059 |archivedate=September 19, 2014 }}</ref>
* On September 16, more than 500 residents of [[Benton Charter Township, Michigan|Benton Township, Michigan]], were forced to leave their houses for 10 to 12 hours, after authorities discovered a leak on TransCanada Corporation's 22-inch [[ANR Pipeline|ANR]] gas transmission pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.huffingtonpost.ca/2014/09/17/transcanada-pipeline-benton-harbor_n_5837862.html |title=TransCanada Pipeline Rupture Prompts Evacuation Of Benton Harbor |work=The Huffington Post |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20140921013637/http://www.huffingtonpost.ca/2014/09/17/transcanada-pipeline-benton-harbor_n_5837862.html |archivedate=September 21, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wsbt.com/news/local/transcanada-after-pipeline-rupture-repairs-may-take-several-weeks/28150584 |title=TransCanada: After pipeline rupture, repairs may take several weeks |author= |work=wsbt.com |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141112012303/http://www.wsbt.com/news/local/transcanada-after-pipeline-rupture-repairs-may-take-several-weeks/28150584 |archivedate=November 12, 2014 }}</ref>
* On September 17, 3 LG&E subcontractors were injured, when a gas main exploded after being hit by equipment during maintenance of the gas main, along a stretch of U.S. 42 in [[Oldham County, Kentucky]]. There was no fire.<ref>http://www.wave3.com/story/26560231/pipeline-explosion-closes-us-42-in-oldham-county</ref> 
* On October 13, a gas transmission pipeline failed near [[Centerview, Missouri]], causing an explosion and massive fire for several hours. There were no injuries.<ref name="dot3"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kctv5.com/story/26772356/emergency-crews-respond-to-pipeline-rupture-fire-near-centerview#ixzz3G3Gp4Ie3 |title=Emergency crews respond to pipeline rupture, fire near Centervie – KCTV5 |author=Chris Oberholtz |date=October 13, 2014 |work=kctv5.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.kctv5.com/story/26772356/emergency-crews-respond-to-pipeline-rupture-fire-near-centerview |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 13, a [[Sunoco]]/Mid-Valley crude oil pipeline ruptured, and spilled about 168,000 gallons of crude oil in [[Caddo Parish, Louisiana]]. Wildlife was killed.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.shreveporttimes.com/story/news/local/2014/10/18/crude-oil-spills-caddo-bayou-kills-wildlife/17522017/ |title=Crude oil spills into Caddo bayou, kills wildlife |author=Vickie Welborn |date=October 18, 2014 |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20141022001631/http://www.shreveporttimes.com/story/news/local/2014/10/18/crude-oil-spills-caddo-bayou-kills-wildlife/17522017/ |archivedate=October 22, 2014 }}</ref>
* A 24-inch gas transmission pipeline was hit by excavators on October 23, near [[Newport, Arkansas]]. Five nearby houses were evacuated, and two highways and a railroad were closed for a time. There was no fire or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kait8.com/story/26866351/roads-open-repairs-underway-after-gas-leak |title=Roads open, repairs underway after gas leak |author= |date=October 22, 2014 |work=kait8.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160202035730/http://www.kait8.com/story/26866351/roads-open-repairs-underway-after-gas-leak |archivedate=February 2, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 28, an 8-inch natural gas condensate pipeline exploded in [[Monroe County, Ohio]]. A large fire followed. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theintelligencer.net/page/content.detail/id/615683/Blue-Racer-Pipeline-Shut-Down-After-Explosion.html?nav=510 |title=Blue Racer Pipeline Shut Down After Explosion |work=The Intelligencer |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304191713/http://www.theintelligencer.net/page/content.detail/id/615683/Blue-Racer-Pipeline-Shut-Down-After-Explosion.html?nav=510 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On December 8, gasoline was discovered leaking from [[Kinder Morgan]] [[Plantation Pipeline]] in [[Belton, South Carolina]]. It was found that the 26-inch pipeline had leaked into a nearby creek. The cause was a failure at a sleeve that was part of an earlier repair.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF 2-2015-5001S |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220155001S/220155001S_NOPSO_03092015_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220141445/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220155001S/220155001S_NOPSO_03092015_text.pdf |archivedate=December 20, 2016 }}</ref> As of April 2015, it was estimated that 8,000 barrels (42 gallons per barrel) or more than 300,000 gallons of gasoline had leaked. After four months of cleanup, only 176,901 gallons of product had been recovered and removed.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://savannahnow.com/news/2015-04-30/kinder-morgan-pipeline-leak-reaches-300000-gallons-south-carolina |title=Kinder Morgan pipeline leak reaches 300,000 gallons in South Carolina |work=savannahnow.com |accessdate=January 19, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://savannahnow.com/news/2015-04-30/kinder-morgan-pipeline-leak-reaches-300000-gallons-south-carolina |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>

=== 2015 ===

* On January 14, during work to free a trapped inline inspection unit, a leak was discovered on the Evangeline Pipeline, near [[Cameron Parish, Louisiana]]. This pipeline had been given a Corrective Action Order in October 2014, due to a number of leaks.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.icis.com/resources/news/2015/01/14/9853014/us-evangeline-pipeline-shuts-down-after-leak-discovered/ |title=US Evangeline Pipeline shuts down after leak discovered |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150702011745/http://www.icis.com/resources/news/2015/01/14/9853014/us-evangeline-pipeline-shuts-down-after-leak-discovered/ |archivedate=July 2, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.argusmedia.com/News/Article?id=976846 |title=News – Argus Media |publisher= |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150516143633/http://www.argusmedia.com/News/Article?id=976846 |archivedate=May 16, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No.: 4-2014-5027H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420145027H/420145027H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_10202014_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170209132956/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420145027H/420145027H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_10202014_text.pdf |archivedate=February 9, 2017 }}</ref>
* Also on January 14, a gas pipeline exploded near the [[Ross Barnett Reservoir]] in [[Brandon, Mississippi]], creating a sizable crater in the ground and burning 6 acres of vegetation before the fire was extinguished. No injuries were reported. The failure was due to a "hard spot" from manufacturing, that already had a repair sleeve on it. There are 788 sleeves on the Index 129 pipeline from Edna, Texas, to Sterlington, Louisiana; and, 726 sleeves on the Index 130 pipeline from Marchand Junction, Louisiana to Kosciusko, Mississippi. Both were built from pipe made in 1952.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wapt.com/news/central-mississippi/gas-line-explodes-burns-at-reservoir/30695664 |title=Gas line explodes, burns near reservoir |date=January 14, 2015 |publisher=[[WAPT]] News |accessdate=January 15, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150218044130/http://www.wapt.com/news/central-mississippi/gas-line-explodes-burns-at-reservoir/30695664 |archivedate=February 18, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/2015/01/14/reservoir-explosion/21740325/|title=Reservoir gas pipeline fire extinguished|date=January 14, 2015|publisher=[[The Clarion-Ledger]]|accessdate=January 15, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF 2-2015-1001S |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220151001S/220151001S_nopso_03272015_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211115940/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220151001S/220151001S_nopso_03272015_text.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On January 16, a transmission pipeline operated by [[Kinder Morgan]] subsidiary Southern Natural Gas had an equipment malfunction in Walthall County, Mississippi.<ref name="primis">Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety Administration operator data, http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov. {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170603005753/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/ |date=June 3, 2017 }}, Retrieved April 1, 2016.</ref>
* On January 17, oil from a broken pipeline seeped into the [[Yellowstone River]], and contaminated the water supply 10 miles south of Glendive, Montana. The release was from Bridger Pipeline LLC's 12-inch Poplar line, which can carry 42,000 barrels a day of crude from the [[Bakken Formation]] and runs from Canada south to Baker, Montana. Bridger Pipeline is a subsidiary of True Cos., a privately held Wyoming-based company. The company said in a statement that the pipeline was shut down within an hour of the leak. About 30,000 gallons of crude was spilled, with about 28,000 gallons of crude being lost.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Sider |first1=Alison |title=Oil Spill Contaminates Montana Town's Water Supply, EPA Says |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/oil-spills-into-yellowstone-river-after-pipeline-leak-1421688172 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170206043411/https://www.wsj.com/articles/oil-spills-into-yellowstone-river-after-pipeline-leak-1421688172 |archivedate=February 6, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.inforum.com/news/accidents/3661267-clean-water-likely-be-restored-glendive-thursday-after-oil-spill-along |title=Clean water likely to be restored to Glendive on Thursday after oil spill along Yellowstone |author=Tom Lutey |work=INFORUM |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160128204750/http://www.inforum.com/news/accidents/3661267-clean-water-likely-be-restored-glendive-thursday-after-oil-spill-along |archivedate=January 28, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31878.html?nocache=4750#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160308070842/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31878.html?nocache=4750 |archivedate=March 8, 2016 }}</ref>
* On January 21, a petroleum products pipeline in [[Honolulu, Hawaii]] ruptured, due to external corrosion, spilling about 42,000 gallons of petroleum product, of which about 22,000 gallons was lost.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31056.html?nocache=5782#_Incidents_tab_3 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160308054320/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_31056.html?nocache=5782 |archivedate=March 8, 2016 }}</ref>
* On January 21, a crude oil pipeline pump station caught fire northwest of [[Texas City, Texas]]. Texas City fire officials said that company officials reported that there had been issues with the pump station over the weekend.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.galvestondailynews.com/free/article_699f91e8-9c22-11e4-97c3-63576ec5ef16.html|title=Pipeline fire shuts down FM 2004 in Texas City|work=The Galveston County Daily News|accessdate=January 18, 2016}}</ref>
* On January 26, a 20-inch [[Enterprise Products]] ATEX pipeline carrying ethane exploded and burned in [[Brooke County, West Virginia]]. Despite snow in the area, five acres of woodlands burned, and 1,283,000 gallons of ethane were consumed, or lost. The fireball melted siding on nearby homes and damaged power lines; it is believed that day’s snowy weather lessened the damage. Reports suspect a girth weld failure from ductile tensile overload, with the pipeline being less than two years old. There were no injuries.<ref name="ReferenceA"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theintelligencer.net/page/content.detail/id/623827/Fire-Burned-24-000-Barrels-of-Ethane.html?nav=515 |title=24,000 Ethane Barrels Burned |work=The Intelligencer |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160406055110/http://www.theintelligencer.net/page/content.detail/id/623827/Fire-Burned-24-000-Barrels-of-Ethane.html?nav=515 |archivedate=April 6, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://america.aljazeera.com/blogs/scrutineer/2015/1/31/january-sees-five-major-pipeline-leaks.html |title=Breaking January Sees Five Major Pipeline Leaks |publisher=Al Jazeera America |accessdate=January 19, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160116185521/http://america.aljazeera.com/blogs/scrutineer/2015/1/31/january-sees-five-major-pipeline-leaks.html |archivedate=January 16, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/149469_Enterprise_Products_Operating_LLC_FIR_2015_1_26_Report_and_Appendices.pdf |title=Archived copy |accessdate=2017-05-08 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170430085202/https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/149469_Enterprise_Products_Operating_LLC_FIR_2015_1_26_Report_and_Appendices.pdf |archivedate=April 30, 2017 }}</ref>
* On January 29, near Bowling Green, [[Missouri]], a rupture in a Rockies Express 42-inch natural gas pipeline blew a 20 by 20-foot crater and forced a six-hour evacuation of 50 families. The rupture occurred in a vacant field a few yards east of Pike County Road 43. Strong winds helped dissipate gas until a temporary cap was put in place.<ref>{{cite web|title=Pipeline Ruptures Near Pike 43 {{!}} The People's Tribune|url=http://thepeoplestribune.com/?p=25397|website=thepeoplestribune.com|accessdate=28 November 2016}}</ref> This explosion caused $2,672,345 in property damage and was due to a fault in the pipe's fabrication or construction.<ref>Operator Information, Pipeline & Hazardous Materials Safety Administration, http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141030030518/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/ |date=October 30, 2014 }}.</ref>
* On February 10 in Hopkinton, Massachusetts, the temperature caused "natural force damage" to a [[Kinder Morgan]] Tennessee Gas Pipeline, causing $55,150 worth of property damage.<ref name="primis"/>
* On February 17, a suspected electrical arc made a hole in a [[Marathon Petroleum]] pipeline in [[Shively, Kentucky]], spill about 6,700 gallons of jet fuel. More than 2,500 tons of soil were removed to clean up the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wdrb.com/story/28752694/jet-fuel-remains-in-shively-soil-months-after-pipeline-spill |title=Jet fuel remains in Shively soil months after pipeline spill |author=Marcus Green |date=April 8, 2015 |work=wdrb.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.wdrb.com/story/28752694/jet-fuel-remains-in-shively-soil-months-after-pipeline-spill |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wdrb.com/story/30439304/more-than-2500-tons-of-soil-removed-from-shively-neighborhood-after-pipeline-spill |title=More than 2,500 tons of soil removed from Shively neighborhood a – WDRB 41 Louisville News |author=Marcus Green |date=November 4, 2015 |work=wdrb.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160111223557/http://www.wdrb.com/story/30439304/more-than-2500-tons-of-soil-removed-from-shively-neighborhood-after-pipeline-spill |archivedate=January 11, 2016 }}</ref>
* On February 25, a 26-inch crude oil pipeline in [[Navarro County]] near the Town of [[Dawson, Texas]], failed, spill about 50 barrels of crude oil. Near the failure, investigation showed that the pipe had lost about 80% of its thickness, due to external corrosion. This anomaly was not seen in a 2011 test of this pipeline.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2015-5005H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420155005H/420155005H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_03122015_text.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220144109/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420155005H/420155005H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_03122015_text.pdf |archivedate=December 20, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 2, a [[Kinder Morgan]] Tennessee Gas Pipeline leaked due to equipment failure, causing $281,890 of property damage in Marshall, Mississippi.<ref name="primis"/>
* On March 13 a pipeline Patrol pilot identified an oil sheen on a pond near [[Tehuacana Creek]], Texas which was then linked to a leaking 10 inch petroleum products pipeline. About 50 barrels of diesel fuel were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wacotrib.com/news/environment/cleanup-begins-on-diesel-pipeline-spill-near-tehuacana-creek/article_20e9cb1d-75ad-5b17-90a5-374c35f6876a.html|title=Cleanup begins on diesel pipeline spill near Tehuacana Creek|work=WacoTrib.com|accessdate=January 18, 2016}}</ref>
* On March 20, a pipe owned by [[Kinder Morgan]] subsidiary Southern Natural Gas failed in Rolling Fork, Mississippi, and on March 23, another of that subsidiary's pipes failed due to equipment malfunction in Augusta, Georgia, causing $311,785 in property damage.<ref name="primis"/>
* On April 9, 2 [[Williams Companies]] pipelines broke within hours of each other in [[Marshall County, West Virginia]]. A 4-inch condensate pipeline broke at 8&nbsp;pm local time, spilling about 132 barrels of condensate into a creek. Around 10:50&nbsp;pm local time, a 12-inch gas pipeline ruptured. There was no fire or injuries. Heavy rains were said to be the cause of the failures.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theintelligencer.net/page/content.detail/id/630275/-Heavy-Rains--Cited-In-Marshall----.html |title=‘Heavy Rains’ Cited In Marshall Pipeline Failure |publisher=The Intelligencer |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150417105218/http://www.theintelligencer.net/page/content.detail/id/630275/-Heavy-Rains--Cited-In-Marshall----.html |archivedate=April 17, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theintelligencer.net/page/content.detail/id/630514/DEP--132-Barrels-Spilled-Into-Marshall-County-Creek.html?nav=515 |title=DEP: 132 Barrels Spilled Into Marshall County Creek |work=The Intelligencer |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304113043/http://www.theintelligencer.net/page/content.detail/id/630514/DEP--132-Barrels-Spilled-Into-Marshall-County-Creek.html?nav=515 |archivedate=March 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 13, a [[Kinder Morgan]] / Natural Gas Pipeline Co. of America pipeline exploded and burned near [[Borger, Texas]]. One home was evacuated, but, there were no injuries. The explosion, caused by equipment failure due to environmental cracking, caused $455,000 in property damage.<ref>{{cite web|title=Natural gas pipeline fire near Borger extinguished |url=http://www.newschannel10.com/story/28788786/natural-gas-pipeline-fire-near-borger-extinguished |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160408102808/http://www.newschannel10.com/story/28788786/natural-gas-pipeline-fire-near-borger-extinguished |archivedate=April 8, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 17, a 12-inch natural gas pipeline near [[Fresno, California]] operated by Pacific Gas and Electric Corp was ruptured by a backhoe. The resulting explosion killed 1 person and injured 12 others.<ref>{{cite web|title=Pipeline explosion at Fresno shooting range caused by front loader, state report says |url=http://www.fresnobee.com/news/local/article26618077.html |accessdate=August 21, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150802204616/http://www.fresnobee.com/news/local/article26618077.html |archivedate=August 2, 2015 }}</ref>
* On May 15, [[Kinder Morgan]]'s [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] leaked in Powell County, [[Kentucky]] causing $23,400 in property damage.<ref name="primis"/>
* On May 19, a [[Plains All American Pipeline]] oil pipeline ruptured near [[Refugio State Beach]], also near [[Goleta, California]], spilling about 124,000 gallons of crude oil. It is referred to as the [[Refugio Oil Spill]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/05/20/us/california-oil-spill/ |title=California oil spill: Up to 105,000 gallons lost – CNN.com |author1=Paul Vercammen |author2=Pat St. Claire |date=May 20, 2015 |work=CNN |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160129203930/http://edition.cnn.com/2015/05/20/us/california-oil-spill/ |archivedate=January 29, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report], (PDF) ''Plains Pipeline, L.P., Line 901, Crude Oil Release, May 19, 2015, Santa Barbara County, California; May 2016''|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/pv_obj_cache/pv_obj_id_8B90E29F8ABBC9A581DEB7D209A0B0D901737301/filename/PHMSA_Failure_Investigation_Report_Plains_Pipeline_LP_Line_901_Public.pd}}</ref>
* On May 31, a 24-inch natural gas back-up pipeline that runs under the Arkansas River in [[Little Rock, Arkansas]] ruptured releasing 3.9&nbsp;million cubic feet of natural gas. The pipeline was not currently in use. No one was injured. A tugboat was damaged.<ref>{{cite web|title=Arkansas River pipeline blowout occurred on Sunday morning, cause still unknown |url=http://www.arktimes.com/ArkansasBlog/archives/2015/06/03/arkansas-river-pipeline-blowout-occurred-on-sunday-morning-cause-still-unknown |accessdate=August 21, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150831052201/http://www.arktimes.com/ArkansasBlog/archives/2015/06/03/arkansas-river-pipeline-blowout-occurred-on-sunday-morning-cause-still-unknown |archivedate=August 31, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Natural gas pipeline ruptures east of I-30 bridge, closing two miles of Arkansas River |url=http://www.arktimes.com/ArkansasBlog/archives/2015/06/02/natural-gas-pipeline-ruptures-east-of-i-30-bridge-closing-two-miles-of-arkansas-river |accessdate=August 21, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150825031124/http://www.arktimes.com/ArkansasBlog/archives/2015/06/02/natural-gas-pipeline-ruptures-east-of-i-30-bridge-closing-two-miles-of-arkansas-river |archivedate=August 25, 2015 }}</ref>
* On June 9 in Moorehouse Parish, Louisiana, [[Kinder Morgan]]'s [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] equipment failed, due to environmental cracking, and leaked, causing $73,395 in property damage.<ref name="primis"/>
* On June 9, a 24-inch natural gas pipeline ruptured in [[Lycoming County, Pennsylvania]]. About 130 individuals were evacuated from their homes. No injuries or damage reported. there was no fire The cause was [[Stress corrosion cracking]].<ref>{{Cite news|title=Williams natgas pipeline in Pennsylvania ruptures; no injuries |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/06/11/us-natgas-williams-transco-idUSKBN0OR1R720150611 |newspaper=Reuters |date=June 11, 2015 |accessdate=August 21, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150924220446/https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/06/11/us-natgas-williams-transco-idUSKBN0OR1R720150611 |archivedate=September 24, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Failure Investigation Report – Williams Partners L.P./Transco 24” Leidy Line B Failure, Unityville, PA 6/9/2015 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/150663_Transcontinental_Unityville_PA_June_9_2015.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170210021346/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/PipelineFailureReports/150663_Transcontinental_Unityville_PA_June_9_2015.pdf |archivedate=February 10, 2017 }}</ref>
* On June 10, [[Kinder Morgan]]'s [[El Paso Natural Gas]] control/relief equipment failed and leaked in Gray County, Texas.<ref name="primis"/>
* On June 13, a 42-inch gas gathering pipeline exploded and burned near [[Cuero, Texas]]. 7 homes were evacuated for a time, but there were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.victoriaadvocate.com/news/2015/jun/17/pipeline-rupture-released-thousands-of-pounds-of-g/ |title=Pipeline rupture released thousands of pounds of gas vapors |work=victoriaadvocate.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/https://www.victoriaadvocate.com/news/2015/jun/17/pipeline-rupture-released-thousands-of-pounds-of-g/ |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On June 15, [[Kinder Morgan]]'s Natural Gas Pipeline Co. of America equipment failed for unknown causes, with $260,555 of property damage in Marshall, Texas (that area's third documented Kinder Morgan leak).<ref name="primis"/>
* On June 18, in Victoria Texas, [[Kinder Morgan]]'s [[Tennessee Gas Pipeline]] pipe failed due to external corrosion and caused $159,346 in property damage).<ref name="primis"/>
* On June 22, a truck driver was killed when his rig veered off a highway and broke above ground facilities for a propylene pipeline in [[Houston, Texas]]. The highway was closed for several hours while the gas dissipated.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.chron.com/houston/article/Truck-collision-with-pipeline-backs-up-traffic-on-6342233.php |title=Texas 225 eastbound reopens after a truck collision with feeder road pipeline shut it down |work=[[Houston Chronicle]] |date=June 22, 2015 |accessdate=December 8, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20151231211851/http://www.chron.com/houston/article/Truck-collision-with-pipeline-backs-up-traffic-on-6342233.php |archivedate=December 31, 2015 }}</ref>

The cause of the explosion was not immediately known.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nbcdfw.com/news/local/4-Injured-in-White-Deer-Gas-Line-Explosion-310324841.html |title=4 Injured in White Deer Gas Line Explosion |work=NBC 5 Dallas-Fort Worth |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115900/http://www.nbcdfw.com/news/local/4-Injured-in-White-Deer-Gas-Line-Explosion-310324841.html |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>

Much of the crude reached a nearby creek. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.bnd.com/news/local/community/highland-news-leader/article27426022.html |title=Highland resident files suit against oil company responsible for spill |work=bnd |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160203115859/http://www.bnd.com/news/local/community/highland-news-leader/article27426022.html |archivedate=February 3, 2016 }}</ref>

* On August 3, a Tennessee Gas Pipeline natural gas pipeline operated by [[Kinder Morgan]] ruptured and exploded, with $191,498 in property damage. Later investigation showed that the pipe split along an [[Electric resistance welding|ERW]] seam, but, the failure was from [[stress corrosion cracking]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Sheriff's Office: Natural gas pipeline 'explosion' forced 150 Falfurrias families from their homes |url=http://www.valleycentral.com/news/story.aspx?id=1239109 |website=Valley Central |accessdate=August 21, 2015 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150814074847/http://www.valleycentral.com/news/story.aspx?id=1239109 |archivedate=August 14, 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 4-2015-1009H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420151009H/420151009H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_08062015.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161221002010/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/420151009H/420151009H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_08062015.pdf |archivedate=December 21, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/TGP_151027_Falfurrias_TX_2015_08_03_Final_Redacted.pdf |title=Failure Investigation Report—Tennessee Gas Pipeline Company, LLC, |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170218052247/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/TGP_151027_Falfurrias_TX_2015_08_03_Final_Redacted.pdf |archivedate=February 18, 2017 }}</ref>

* 0n August 13, crew working for [[Colonial Pipeline]] damaged one of Colonial's lines in [[Kannapolis, North Carolina]], spilling about 6,000 gallons of petroleum product. About 1,000 gallons of product was lost.<ref name="dot5"/>

There were no injuries or immediate damage; residents were evacuated.<ref>{{cite web|title=All-clear given to Cypress residents evacuated after gas leak |url=http://www.click2houston.com/news/fd-hazmat-responding-to-gas-leak-in-northwest-harris-county/34706166 |accessdate=September 6, 2015 |last=KPRC |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150906075718/http://www.click2houston.com/news/fd-hazmat-responding-to-gas-leak-in-northwest-harris-county/34706166 |archivedate=September 6, 2015 }}</ref>

* On October 8, an explosion occurred at a [[Williams Companies]] pipeline facility in [[Gibson, Louisiana]]. 4 employees were killed, and, one other injured. The cause of the explosion was from procedure not being followed during welding work.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wdsu.com/news/local-news/new-orleans/explosion-reported-at-natural-gas-pipeline-in-gibson/35726080 |title=Police: 3 dead, 2 in serious condition after Gibson plant explosion |author=Clint Durrett |date=May 15, 2012 |work=WDSU |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160526180907/http://www.wdsu.com/news/local-news/new-orleans/explosion-reported-at-natural-gas-pipeline-in-gibson/35726080 |archivedate=May 26, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_19570.html?nocache=8429#_Incidents_tab_4 |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |author= |date= |work=dot.gov |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307161646/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_19570.html?nocache=8429 |archivedate=March 7, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF 4-2016-1008 |url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/420161008_NOPV_PCP_PCO_07292016.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161231184226/http://phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles/PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/420161008_NOPV_PCP_PCO_07292016.pdf |archivedate=December 31, 2016 }}</ref>
* On November 15, work was being performed on a flow control valve, on a [[Sunoco]] 10 inch crude oil pipeline, in [[Wortham, Texas]], when the valve failed, injuring 5 workers, and spilling some crude oil. It was later determined that the valve was under 400 psi of nitrogen pressure when it was being worked on.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/pipeline/phmsa-failure-investigation-results-in-notice-of-probable-violation-and-proposed-civil-penalty-for-sunoco-pipeline |title=PHMSA – Briefing Room |first=Department of Transportation's Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety |last=Administration |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161104141746/http://www.phmsa.dot.gov/pipeline/phmsa-failure-investigation-results-in-notice-of-probable-violation-and-proposed-civil-penalty-for-sunoco-pipeline |archivedate=November 4, 2016 }}</ref>
* On November 30, about 11,000 gallons of gasoline, butane and propane leaked from a pipeline, in eastern [[Summit County, Utah]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.deseretnews.com/article/865642766/11000-gallons-of-gasoline-butane-and-propane-leak-from-pipeline-in-Summit-County.html?pg=all |title=11,000 gallons of gasoline, butane and propane leak from pipeline in Summit County |author= |date=November 30, 2015 |work=DeseretNews.com |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160306212804/http://www.deseretnews.com/article/865642766/11000-gallons-of-gasoline-butane-and-propane-leak-from-pipeline-in-Summit-County.html?pg=all |archivedate=March 6, 2016 }}</ref>

Approximately 42,000 gallons of crude oil were released within the terminal. A tank line had failed from internal corrosion.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Enterprise_Crude_Pipeline_LLC_Cushing_West_Terminal_2015_12_01_Redacted.pdf |title=Archived copy |accessdate=2017-05-08 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170430084914/https://www.phmsa.dot.gov/staticfiles//PHMSA/DownloadableFiles/Files/Pipeline/Failure%20Reports/Enterprise_Crude_Pipeline_LLC_Cushing_West_Terminal_2015_12_01_Redacted.pdf |archivedate=April 30, 2017 }}</ref>

=== 2016 ===
* On January 2, 3 people were injured, one seriously, one home destroyed, and 50 homes were damaged in [[Oklahoma City, Oklahoma]], when a leak gas from a gas main entered a home. Preliminary results indicate that a leak occurred at a weld seam on the gas main. Later, Oklahoma regulators filed a complaint over the failure with Oklahoma Natural Gas. The complaint alleged the utility failed to properly inspect its system following eight previous leak failures in the neighborhood going back to 1983.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://kfor.com/2016/01/06/ong-releases-cause-behind-oklahoma-city-house-explosion/#|title=Preliminary investigation: ONG releases cause behind Oklahoma City house explosion|author=|date=|work=KFOR.com|accessdate=May 23, 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://newsok.com/article/5522156|title=ONG agrees to pay $1 million in fines related to Oklahoma City home explosion|date=October 12, 2016|publisher=}}</ref>
* On January 9, a 30-inch [[Atmos Energy]] gas transmission pipeline exploded and burned in [[Robertson County, Texas]]. 4 families nearby were evacuated.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kbtx.com/content/news/Gas-line-explosion-in-Leon-County--364750381.html |title=Gas line explosion in Robertson County |author= |website=Kbtx.com |accessdate=January 18, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160112004246/http://www.kbtx.com/content/news/Gas-line-explosion-in-Leon-County--364750381.html |archivedate=January 12, 2016 }}</ref>
* On January 11, butane leaking from a pipeline storage facility, in [[Conway, Kansas]], forced a closure of a nearby highway for a time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://ksn.com/2016/01/11/gas-leak-closes-highway-56-west-of-mcpherson/ |title=Gas leak closes Highway 56 west of McPherson |author= |date= |work=KSN-TV |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160314200824/http://ksn.com/2016/01/11/gas-leak-closes-highway-56-west-of-mcpherson/ |archivedate=March 14, 2016 }}</ref>
* On February 14, a 6-inch crude oil pipeline broke near [[Rozet, Wyoming]], spilling about 1,500 gallons of crude oil into a creek bed.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.gillettenewsrecord.com/news/local/article_a584a743-70fa-52f9-b82c-00816a698e0d.html|title=Cause of oil leak determined to be internal corrosion of an old pipe|author=Scott hansen News Record Writer shansen@gillettenewsrecord.net|date=February 16, 2016|work=Gillette News Record|accessdate=May 23, 2016}}</ref>
