The cause was from manufacturing defects.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kplctv.com/story/31300076/breaking-authorities-have-confirmed-a-pipeline-fire-seen-north-of-sulphur |title=Pipeline fire north of Sulphur |author=Shireen Santhanasamy |date=February 24, 2016 |work=kplctv.com |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160512222602/http://www.kplctv.com/story/31300076/breaking-authorities-have-confirmed-a-pipeline-fire-seen-north-of-sulphur |archivedate=May 12, 2016 }}</ref><ref name="dot8">{{cite web|url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_3445.html?nocache=1113#_Incidents_tab_3 |publisher=primis.phmsa.dot.gov |title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications – Operator Information |accessdate=October 5, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161005112401/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_3445.html?nocache=1113 |archivedate=October 5, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 11, about 30,000 gallons of gasoline spilled from a leaking plug on a pipeline, at a tank farm in [[Sioux City, Iowa]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.siouxlandmatters.com/news/local-news/update-the-gas-spill-at-magellan-pipeline-company-has-been-contained-from-reaching-the-floyd-river |title=UPDATE: The gas spill at Magellan Pipeline Company has been |author=Jessica Plue |date= |work=SIOUXLANDMATTERS |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160320022456/http://www.siouxlandmatters.com/news/local-news/update-the-gas-spill-at-magellan-pipeline-company-has-been-contained-from-reaching-the-floyd-river |archivedate=March 20, 2016 }}</ref>
* On March 22, about 4,000 gallons of gasoline spilled from a 6-inch petroleum products pipeline in [[Harwood, North Dakota]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.valleynewslive.com/home/headlines/Pipeline-leak-being-repaired-near-Harwood-373097491.html |title=Pipeline leak being repaired near Harwood |author=Al Aamodt |date= |work=valleynewslive.com |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160425112039/http://www.valleynewslive.com/home/headlines/Pipeline-leak-being-repaired-near-Harwood-373097491.html |archivedate=April 25, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 2, the [[TransCanada Corporation]] Keystone Pipeline was observed by a local resident to be leaking, near [[Freeman, South Dakota]]. The cause was a crack in a girth weld, and amount of tar sands [[dilbit]] spill was about 16,800 gallons.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nationalobserver.com/2016/04/04/news/transcanada-shuts-down-keystone-after-oil-seeps-surface |title=TransCanada shuts down Keystone after oil seeps to surface |author= |date= |work=National Observer |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160520145152/http://www.nationalobserver.com/2016/04/04/news/transcanada-shuts-down-keystone-after-oil-seeps-surface |archivedate=May 20, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 3-2016-5002H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320165003H/320165003H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_04092016.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220001843/http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/320165003H/320165003H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_04092016.pdf |archivedate=December 20, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 12, a pipeline at a gas plant in [[Woodsboro, Texas]] exploded, killing 2 men, and injured another worker.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kiiitv.com/story/31706685/two-killed-one-injured-in-gas-plant-explosion-near-woodsboro |title=Two Killed, One Injured in Gas Plant Explosion Near Woodsboro |first= |last=TEGNA |work=kiiitv.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160720201618/http://www.kiiitv.com/story/31706685/two-killed-one-injured-in-gas-plant-explosion-near-woodsboro |archivedate=July 20, 2016 }}</ref>
* On April 17, a 10 petroleum products pipeline failed in [[Wabash County, Illinois]], resulting in a sheen on the [[Wabash River]]. About 48,000 gallons of diesel fuel was spilled.<ref>{{cite web|title=CPF No. 2-2016 5003H |url=http://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/enforce/documents/220165003H/220165003H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_04222016.pdf |accessdate=28 November 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211183607/https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/Comm/reports/enforce/documents/220165003H/220165003H_Corrective%20Action%20Order_04222016.pdf |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On April 29, a 30-inch Texas Eastern/Spectra Energy pipeline exploded, injuring one man, destroying his home and damaging several others. The incident was reported at 8:17&nbsp;a.m., near the intersection of Routes 819 and 22 in Salem Township, [[Westmoreland County, Pennsylvania]]. Later, Spectra Energy Corp. announced plans to dig up and assess 263 miles of that pipeline, from Pennsylvania to New Jersey. Corrosion had been detected at the failed seam 4 years before the rupture.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://triblive.com/news/westmoreland/10391146-74/819-fire-gas?fb_comment_id=fbc_1010377968997980_1010524192316691_1010524192316691#f1324664a15cc3c |title=Man burned in Salem Twp. gas line explosion; homes, businesses evacuated |author=Tribune-Review |date=April 29, 2016 |work=TribLIVE.com |accessdate=May 23, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160531173831/http://triblive.com/news/westmoreland/10391146-74/819-fire-gas?fb_comment_id=fbc_1010377968997980_1010524192316691_1010524192316691 |archivedate=May 31, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.bizjournals.com/pittsburgh/blog/morning-edition/2016/06/energy-company-assessing-pipeline.html |title=Spectra Energy Corp. assessing natural gas transmission pipeline after explosion in April 2016, according to Pittsburgh Post-Gazette – Pittsburgh Business Times |work=bizjournals.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160816135455/http://www.bizjournals.com/pittsburgh/blog/morning-edition/2016/06/energy-company-assessing-pipeline.html |archivedate=August 16, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://powersource.post-gazette.com/powersource/companies/2016/09/13/Pipe-that-burst-showed-defect-four-years-ago-Spectra-investigation-found/stories/201609130202 |title=Corrosion discovered four years before Westmoreland County pipe blast |work=post-gazette.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160917021259/http://powersource.post-gazette.com/powersource/companies/2016/09/13/Pipe-that-burst-showed-defect-four-years-ago-Spectra-investigation-found/stories/201609130202 |archivedate=September 17, 2016 }}</ref>
* On May 20, a [[Shell Oil Company]] pipeline leaked near [[Tracy, California]], spilling about 21,000 gallons of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.sfgate.com/bayarea/article/Oil-pipeline-near-Tracy-spills-thousands-of-7940489.php |title=Oil pipeline near Tracy spills thousands of gallons of crude |work=sfgate.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160922075735/http://www.sfgate.com/bayarea/article/Oil-pipeline-near-Tracy-spills-thousands-of-7940489.php |archivedate=September 22, 2016 }}</ref>
* On June 23, a Crimson Pipeline crude oil line leaked in [[Ventura County, California]]. Initial reports said the spill size was from 25,200 gallons to 29,000 gallons, but, later reports estimate 45,000 gallons of crude were spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://weather.com/news/news/ventura-county-california-pipeline-oil-spill-pacific-ocean-crimson-pipeline |title=California Crimson Pipeline Oil Spill Stopped Before Reaching Pacific Ocean |work=weather.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160925081844/https://weather.com/news/news/ventura-county-california-pipeline-oil-spill-pacific-ocean-crimson-pipeline |archivedate=September 25, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.vcstar.com/news/local/ventura/more-oil-spilled-in-ventura-barranca-than-initially-believed-3728a273-59cc-1271-e053-0100007f587a-386083421.html |title=More oil spilled in Ventura barranca than initially believed |work=vcstar.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160812210040/http://www.vcstar.com/news/local/ventura/more-oil-spilled-in-ventura-barranca-than-initially-believed-3728a273-59cc-1271-e053-0100007f587a-386083421.html |archivedate=August 12, 2016 }}</ref>
* On July 6, a [[Plantation Pipeline]] line was noticed to be leaking in [[Goochland County, Virginia]]. The spill did not reach nearby waterways.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.richmond.com/news/local/central-virginia/goochland/article_d75750d5-424f-591c-8da6-1c9b8673423e.html|title=Petroleum leak reported along Goochland-Henrico line|work=richmond.com|accessdate=September 16, 2016}}</ref>
* On August 12, contractors were working on one of the main lines in Sunoco Pipeline LP's [[Nederland, Texas]] terminal when crude oil burst through a plug that was supposed to hold the oil back in the pipeline and ignited. The contractors were knocked off the platform to the ground, suffering injuries from the fall and severe burns. 7 contractors were injured.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.houstonpress.com/news/sunoco-sued-after-august-pipeline-fire-has-a-history-of-safety-violations-8721539 |title=Sunoco, Sued After August Pipeline Fire, Has a History of Safety Violations |first=Dianna |last=Wray |date=September 2, 2016 |work=houstonpress.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160915204358/http://www.houstonpress.com/news/sunoco-sued-after-august-pipeline-fire-has-a-history-of-safety-violations-8721539 |archivedate=September 15, 2016 }}</ref>
* On September 5, a pipeline in [[Bay Long, Louisiana]] was hit by dredging operations, resulting in a spill of about 5,300 gallons of crude oil into the water.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nola.com/environment/index.ssf/2016/09/small_oil_spill_reported_in_ba.html |title=Dredge hits coastal Jefferson Parish pipeline, Coast Guard reports |work=nola.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160911143245/http://www.nola.com/environment/index.ssf/2016/09/small_oil_spill_reported_in_ba.html |archivedate=September 11, 2016 }}</ref>
* On September 9, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] mainline leak was noticed by workers on another project, in [[Shelby County, Alabama]]. At least 252,000 gallons of gasoline leaked from line.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://kfor.com/2016/09/16/state-of-emergency-declared-after-crucial-oil-pipeline-leaks-250000-gallons-in-alabama/ |title=State of emergency declared after crucial oil pipeline leaks 250,000 gallons in Alabama |work=kofr.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160917132958/http://kfor.com/2016/09/16/state-of-emergency-declared-after-crucial-oil-pipeline-leaks-250000-gallons-in-alabama/ |archivedate=September 17, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.wbrc.com/story/33088344/colonial-pipeline-at-least-42000-of-gas-leaked-from-line |title=Colonial Pipeline: At least 42,000 gallons of gas leaked from line |first=Melanie |last=Posey |work=wbrc.com |accessdate=September 16, 2016 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160917021027/http://www.wbrc.com/story/33088344/colonial-pipeline-at-least-42000-of-gas-leaked-from-line |archivedate=September 17, 2016 }}</ref>
* On September 10, a [[Sunoco]] pipeline ruptured near [[Sweetwater, Texas]]. About 33,000 gallons of crude oil were spilled. The pipeline was just over a year old.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-pipeline-sunoco-logistics-idUSKCN11L2CM |title=U.S. regulator orders inquiry, repairs after Sunoco's Permian leak |date=September 15, 2016 |publisher= |via=Reuters |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160916014012/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-pipeline-sunoco-logistics-idUSKCN11L2CM |archivedate=September 16, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 11, two Nicor Gas workers were injured, and two townhouse units destroyed in a massive fire and explosion, caused by a gas leak in [[Romeoville, Illinois]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://patch.com/illinois/romeoville/romeoville-police-responding-reports-loud-explosion |title=Two Nicor Gas Workers Injured, Townhouse Units Destroyed in Romeoville Explosion |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161013081215/http://patch.com/illinois/romeoville/romeoville-police-responding-reports-loud-explosion |archivedate=October 13, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 17, an 8-inch ammonia pipeline started leaking, near [[Tekamah, Nebraska]]. A farmer living nearby went to find the source of the ammonia, and was killed by entering the vapor cloud. About 50 people were evacuated from their homes.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.omaha.com/news/nebraska/farmer-died-as-he-investigated-source-of-anhydrous-ammonia-odor/article_45a82ff2-9531-11e6-b7d2-8fd7420414f7.html|title=Some families being allowed into their homes; those nearest deadly chemical leak unable to return|first=Andrew J. Nelson and Emily Nitcher / World-Herald staff|last=writers|publisher=}}</ref>
* On October 19, a contractor in [[Portland, Oregon]] hit a 1-inch gas pipeline during work. Within an hour, there were 2 explosions, injuring 8 people, destroying or damaging several buildings, and started a fire. Contractors claim a utility locate was done before work began.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.oregonlive.com/portland/index.ssf/2016/10/subcontractor_takes_reponsibil.html |title=Subcontractor takes responsibility for Portland gas line breach |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161022093341/http://www.oregonlive.com/portland/index.ssf/2016/10/subcontractor_takes_reponsibil.html |archivedate=October 22, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 21, an 8-inch Sunoco pipeline ruptured in [[Lycoming County, Pennsylvania]], spilling about 55,000 gallons of gasoline into the [[Susquehanna River]]. The river was running high at the time.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://lancasteronline.com/news/local/gallons-of-gasoline-spills-into-susquehanna-effect-on-lancaster-county/article_5ed0d20c-97b8-11e6-8fb8-17dc59d3a8e1.html |title=55,000 gallons of gasoline spills into Susquehanna, effect on Lancaster County drinking water unclear |first=TOM KNAPP |last=Writer Staff |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161023235929/http://lancasteronline.com/news/local/gallons-of-gasoline-spills-into-susquehanna-effect-on-lancaster-county/article_5ed0d20c-97b8-11e6-8fb8-17dc59d3a8e1.html |archivedate=October 23, 2016 }}</ref>
* On October 23, a pipeline ruptured on the Seaway Pipeline, in [[Cushing, Oklahoma]], spraying the area with crude oil. About 319,00 gallons of crude were spilled. The cause was from prior excavation damage.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.upi.com/Seaway-Pipeline-crude-oil-leak-reported-in-Cushing-Okla/4361477309759/ |title=Seaway Pipeline crude oil leak reported in Cushing, Okla. |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161027114240/http://www.upi.com/Seaway-Pipeline-crude-oil-leak-reported-in-Cushing-Okla/4361477309759/ |archivedate=October 27, 2016 }}</ref><ref name="dot.gov">{{cite web|url=https://primis.phmsa.dot.gov/comm/reports/operator/OperatorIM_opid_30829.html?nocache=9093#_Incidents_tab_4|title=PHMSA: Stakeholder Communications - Operator Information|website=primis.phmsa.dot.gov}}</ref>
* On October 31, a [[Colonial Pipeline]] mainline exploded and burned in [[Shelby County, Alabama]], after accidentally being hit by a track hoe. One worker died at the scene, and 5 others were hospitalized, with one of those workers dying a month later. The explosion occurred approximately several miles from the 9 September 2016 breach.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-pipeline-blast-alabama-idUSKBN12V2FC |title=Colonial may open key U.S. gasoline line by Saturday after fatal blast |date=November 2, 2016 |publisher= |via=Reuters |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161101014638/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-pipeline-blast-alabama-idUSKBN12V2FC |archivedate=November 1, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://helena.colonialresponse.com/|title=Helena – Colonial Pipeline Response|publisher=}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://abcnews.go.com/US/wireStory/osha-2nd-person-dies-alabama-pipeline-explosion-44034349 |title=OSHA: 2nd Person Dies After Alabama Pipeline Explosion |first=ABC |last=News |publisher=ABC News |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161208044434/http://abcnews.go.com/US/wireStory/osha-2nd-person-dies-alabama-pipeline-explosion-44034349 |archivedate=December 8, 2016 }}</ref>
* On November 29, an Enterprise Products pipeline exploded in [[Platte County, Missouri]], burning an ethane propane mixture. There were no evacuations or injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kansascity.com/news/business/article118276613.html |title=Pipeline explosion in Northland draws federal investigator |publisher=Kansas City |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161203213423/http://www.kansascity.com/news/business/article118276613.html |archivedate=December 3, 2016 }}</ref>
* On December 2, equipment failure in a [[Denbury Resources]] source water pipeline led to a leak of approximately 84,000 gallons of source water into Skull Creek, in [[Bowman County, North Dakota]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.thedickinsonpress.com/news/local/4171398-leak-causes-approximately-2000-barrels-source-water-flow-skull-creek-bowman |title=Leak causes approximately 2,000 barrels of source water to flow into Skull Creek in Bowman County |date=December 2, 2016 |publisher=North Dakota Department of Health |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220035740/http://www.thedickinsonpress.com/news/local/4171398-leak-causes-approximately-2000-barrels-source-water-flow-skull-creek-bowman |archivedate=December 20, 2016 }}</ref>
* On December 5, a 6-inch Belle Fourche pipeline spilled 529,800 gallons of crude oil, into Ash Coulee Creek, in [[Billings County, North Dakota]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.duluthnewstribune.com/news/4173960-western-north-dakota-oil-pipeline-shut-down-after-spill |title=Western North Dakota oil pipeline shut down after spill |publisher=Duluth Tribute |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220124314/http://www.duluthnewstribune.com/news/4173960-western-north-dakota-oil-pipeline-shut-down-after-spill |archivedate=December 20, 2016 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.bemidjipioneer.com/news/4239577-oil-spill-creek-originally-underestimated-making-it-one-largest-nd-history |title=Oil spill in creek originally underestimated, making it one of... |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170325023840/http://www.bemidjipioneer.com/news/4239577-oil-spill-creek-originally-underestimated-making-it-one-largest-nd-history |archivedate=March 25, 2017 }}</ref>
* Sometime in December, a natural gas pipeline running beneath [[Turnagain Arm]] in [[Cook Inlet]], near [[Nikiski, Alaska]], southwest of [[Anchorage]] ruptured, leaking large quantities of natural gas into the water.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Carpenter |first1=Dan |title=Investigation finds Hilcorp gas leak poses risks & started earlier than first reported |url=http://www.ktuu.com/content/news/Investigation-finds-Hilcorp-gas-leak-poses-risks--starter-earlier-than-first-reported-415636093.html |accessdate=14 April 2017 |language=en |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170308223454/http://www.ktuu.com/content/news/Investigation-finds-Hilcorp-gas-leak-poses-risks--starter-earlier-than-first-reported-415636093.html |archivedate=March 8, 2017 }}</ref>

=== 2017 ===
* On January 7, a Colonial Pipeline stubline leaked gasoline into Shoal Creek, in [[Chattanooga, Tennessee]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.timesfreepress.com/news/breakingnews/story/2017/jan/07/local-haz-mat-teams-contain-gasoline-leak-near-tennessee-river/406330/ |title=Colonial Pipeline leaks in Chattanooga near Tennessee River |publisher=Times Free Press |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170108134928/http://www.timesfreepress.com/news/breakingnews/story/2017/jan/07/local-haz-mat-teams-contain-gasoline-leak-near-tennessee-river/406330/ |archivedate=January 8, 2017 }}</ref>
* On January 14, the Ozark Pipeline, an [[Enbridge]], now Marathon, division, spilled about 18,900 gallons of light oil, at the Lawrence Pump Station, near [[Halltown, Missouri]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lawrencecountyrecord.com/news/article_517163be-31bf-11e7-8caf-53a312062bf1.html|title=Enbridge reps discuss oil spill cleanup, restoration|publisher=}}</ref>
* On January 16, a gas pipeline exploded and burned, near [[Spearman, Texas]]. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.chron.com/news/houston-texas/texas/article/Reports-Texas-Panhandle-gas-explosion-captured-10872641.php |title=Reports: Texas Panhandle gas explosion captured by police dashcam |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170126071038/http://www.chron.com/news/houston-texas/texas/article/Reports-Texas-Panhandle-gas-explosion-captured-10872641.php |archivedate=January 26, 2017 }}</ref> 
* On January 25, a Magellan pipeline leaked 46,830 gallons (1,115 barrels) of diesel fuel onto private agricultural land, in Worth County, Iowa, near [[Hanlontown, Iowa|Hanlontown]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.desmoinesregister.com/story/news/2017/01/25/pipeline-leaks-thousands-gallons-diesel-northern-iowa/97051728/|title=Pipeline Leaks 138,600 Gallons of Diesel in Northern Iowa|publisher=The Des Moines Register}}</ref><ref>http://globegazette.com/news/local/worth-county-agencies-reimbursed-for-january-diesel-spill-costs/article_1896bde5-38ba-56dd-83ba-f120f6747e95.html</ref>
* On January 30, a Texas Department of Transportation crew dug into the 30 inch [[Seaway Pipeline]], near [[Blue Ridge, Texas]], spraying crude oil across road. About 210,000 gallons of crude were spilled. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kxii.com/content/news/BREAKING-Ruptured-pipeline-near-Blue-Ridge-spews-oil--412209343.html |title=Blue Ridge pipeline spill affecting flow of oil nationally |first=Brittany |last=Harlow |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170201054041/http://www.kxii.com/content/news/BREAKING-Ruptured-pipeline-near-Blue-Ridge-spews-oil--412209343.html |archivedate=February 1, 2017 }}</ref><ref name="dot.gov"/>
* On January 31, a DCP pipeline exploded under a runway, at Panola County Airport-Sharpe Field in [[Texas]]. There were no injuries, but the airport will shut that runway down for an extended amount of time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.news-journal.com/news/2017/feb/01/flights-canceled-panola-county-airport-after-pipel/ |title=Flights canceled at Panola County airport after pipeline explosion - Longview News-Journal |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170203001840/https://www.news-journal.com/news/2017/feb/01/flights-canceled-panola-county-airport-after-pipel/ |archivedate=February 3, 2017 }}</ref>
* On February 10, a [[Phillips 66]] [[natural gas liquids]] pipeline (TENDS pipeline Sorrento system)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ogj.com/articles/print/volume-95/issue-17/in-this-issue/transportation/texaco-plans-louisiana-ngl-system-expansion.html |title=Texaco plans Louisiana NGL system expansion |date=1997-04-28 |publisher=Oil and Gas Journal |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211084342/http://www.ogj.com/articles/print/volume-95/issue-17/in-this-issue/transportation/texaco-plans-louisiana-ngl-system-expansion.html |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}{{cite web|url=http://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20160825006415/en/Phillips-66-Partners-Acquire-South-Louisiana-NGL |title=Phillips 66 Partners to Acquire South Louisiana NGL Logistics Assets |date=August 25, 2016 |publisher=BusinessWire |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170211155227/http://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20160825006415/en/Phillips-66-Partners-Acquire-South-Louisiana-NGL |archivedate=February 11, 2017 }}</ref> near the Williams-Discovery natural gas plant on [[US Route 90]] near [[Paradis, Louisiana]] exploded while being cleaned, killing one worker, and sending another worker to a burn unit.  Traffic on US 90 and La 631 was shut down and residents in the area evacuated.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://wgno.com/2017/02/09/fire-reported-at-natural-gas-plant-in-paradis/ |title=One missing, two injured in Paradis pipeline explosion |date=February 9, 2017 |author=Heather Miller |publisher=WGNO |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170210050541/http://wgno.com/2017/02/09/fire-reported-at-natural-gas-plant-in-paradis/ |archivedate=February 10, 2017 }} The pipeline can be traced with the [http://www.phillips66pipeline.com/maps/ Phillips 66 pipeline finder] and viewed via [https://www.google.com/maps/place/LA-631+%26+W+Bayou+Rd,+Des+Allemands,+LA+70030/@29.8621692,-90.4479067,93m/data=!3m1!1e3!8m2!3d29.8710889!4d-90.4495833 satellite map]</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.houmatoday.com/news/20170216/pipeline-explosion-still-being-investigated |title=Pipeline explosion still being investigated |first=Bridget Mire S Staff |last=Writer |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170217042043/http://www.houmatoday.com/news/20170216/pipeline-explosion-still-being-investigated |archivedate=February 17, 2017 }}</ref>
* On February 15, a 36-inch [[Kinder Morgan]] gas pipeline exploded and burned in [[Refugio County, Texas]]. There were no injuries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.victoriaadvocate.com/news/2017/feb/15/nature-gas-pipeline-explosion-rocks-crossroads/ |title=Natural gas pipeline explosion rocks Crossroads - Victoria Advocate |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170216072950/https://www.victoriaadvocate.com/news/2017/feb/15/nature-gas-pipeline-explosion-rocks-crossroads/ |archivedate=February 16, 2017 }}</ref>
* On February 27, a crude oil pipeline ruptured in [[Falls City, Texas]]. spilling about 42,630 gallons of crude oil. The cause was from internal corrosion.<ref name="dot.gov"/>
* On March 29, a natural-gas leak of a high-pressure pipeline, in [[Providence, Rhode Island]], owned by [[Spectra Energy]], released about 19 million cubic feet of natural gas, or enough natural gas to heat and keep the lights on for 190,000 homes for a single day. Approximately two gallons of polychlorinated biphenyls (PCBs) were also released, in the form of contaminated natural gas condensate.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ecori.org/renewable-energy/2017/5/4/gas-leak-emissions-revealed |title=Leaked Natural Gas was Enough to Heat 190,000 Homes |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170505183955/https://www.ecori.org/renewable-energy/2017/5/4/gas-leak-emissions-revealed |archivedate=May 5, 2017 }}</ref>
* On April 4, a pump on the [[Dakota Access Pipeline]] spilled about 84 gallons of oil, at a pump station in [[Tulra, South Dakota]]. The leak was not noticed until May 9.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.upi.com/Top_News/US/2017/05/11/Dakota-Access-pipeline-leaks-84-gallons-in-South-Dakota/9791494505216/ |title=Dakota Access pipeline leaks 84 gallons in South Dakota |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170511161414/http://www.upi.com/Top_News/US/2017/05/11/Dakota-Access-pipeline-leaks-84-gallons-in-South-Dakota/9791494505216/ |archivedate=May 11, 2017 }}</ref>
* On April 13 and 14, it was discovered that [[Energy Transfer Partners]] spilled drilling fluid into two separate wetlands in rural Ohio while constructing the [[Rover Pipeline]]. The spills occurred in wetlands near [[Richland County, Ohio]]. The spill on the 13th released 2 million gallons of drilling fluid and the spill on the 14th released approximately 50,000 gallons of drilling fluid.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Norris |first1=Courtney |title=The Rover Pipeline leaked millions of gallons of drilling fluid into Ohio wetlands |url=https://www.pbs.org/newshour/rundown/two-weeks-rover-pipeline-leaked-drilling-fluid-ohio-wetlands/ |website=PBS Newshour |accessdate=8 June 2017 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170604023054/http://www.pbs.org/newshour/rundown/two-weeks-rover-pipeline-leaked-drilling-fluid-ohio-wetlands/ |archivedate=June 4, 2017 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last1=Geiling|first1=Natasha|title=Company behind Dakota Access Pipeline spills over 2 million gallons of drilling fluids into Ohio wetlands|url=https://thinkprogress.org/dakota-access-company-ohio-spill-d73cb24c8dd6|website=ThinkProgress|accessdate=8 June 2017}}</ref>
* On April 21, a [[Plains All American Pipeline]], experienced a crude oil release on the Buffalo Pipeline, near [[Loyal, Oklahoma]]. About 19,000 gallons of crude oil was spilled.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ecowatch.com/buffalo-pipeline-leak-oklahoma-2377971688.html |title=Buffalo Pipeline Leaks 19,000 Gallons of Crude Oil on Farmland in Oklahoma |date=April 25, 2017 |publisher= |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170507024029/http://www.ecowatch.com/buffalo-pipeline-leak-oklahoma-2377971688.html |archivedate=May 7, 2017 }}</ref>
* On April 22, a 1,050-gallon oil pipeline spill near [[Bismarck, North Dakota]] polluted a tributary of the Little Missouri River, but was prevented from flowing into the larger waterway.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Nicholson|first1=Blake|title=Oil Pipeline Spill Pollutes North Dakota Tributary|url=https://www.usnews.com/news/best-states/north-dakota/articles/2017-04-25/bowman-county-pipeline-spills-1-050k-of-oil-and-saltwater|website=USNews|publisher=Associated Press|accessdate=6 May 2017}}</ref>
* On May 8, a Wood River Pipelines (part of [[Koch Industries]]) line broke in [[Warrensburg, Illinois]], spill 250 gallons of crude oil.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.illinoishomepage.net/news/local-news/pipeline-spill-controlled/710455965|title=Pipeline Spill Controlled|first=Kaitlyn Connolly, Richard|last=Flesch|date=May 12, 2017|publisher=}}</ref>
* On May 25, workers were installing a replacement pipeline at a tank battery, near [[Mead, Colorado]], when there was an explosion and fire. One worker was killed, and, 3 others injured.<ref>http://denver.cbslocal.com/2017/08/11/oil-tank-explosion-mead-anadarko/</ref><ref>http://denver.cbslocal.com/2017/05/26/mead-oil-tank-battery-explosion-fire/</ref> 
* On July 13, a contractor doing maintenance on Magellan's Longhorn Pipeline hit that pipeline, in [[Bastrop County, Texas]]. About 87,000 gallons of crude oil were spilled, resulting in evacuations of nearby residents.<ref>http://www.fox7austin.com/news/local-news/267668049-story</ref><ref>http://www.statesman.com/news/local/new-data-shows-bastrop-county-oil-spill-leaked-000-gallons/Y8YK4xM4uPE37actcJi1HP/</ref>
* On July 27, while installing a water pipeline by horizontal drilling, a contractor hit a ONEOK Natural Gas Liquids pipeline, spilling about 126,000 gallons of NGL's, near [[Watford City, North Dakota]].<ref>http://bismarcktribune.com/business/local/contractor-that-damaged-pipeline-is-repeat-offender/article_7e83cb2b-9429-5ed5-872f-73940b86f15b.html</ref>
* On August 2, a pipeline leaked up to 1,000 gallons of oil, in [[Signal Hill, California]].<ref>http://www.presstelegram.com/general-news/20170802/oil-pipeline-spill-shuts-signal-hill-streets</ref>
* On August 2, a contractor ruptured a jet fuel pipeline, in [[Parkland, Washington]].<ref>http://www.thenewstribune.com/news/local/article165087782.html</ref>
* On August 2, a natural gas explosion and fire struck the Minnehaha Academy, in [[Minneapolis, Minnesota]]. Workers may have been moving a gas meter when the explosion hit, killing two people and injuring at least nine others, according to investigators.<ref>https://patch.com/minnesota/southwestminneapolis/minnehaha-academy-blast-investigation-could-take-year-ntsb</ref>
